It was the kind of intimacy she hadn’t let herself want for so long, and now that she had it, it hummed through her chest like a second heartbeat.

She didn’t say anything. She just walked up behind Rio and gently brushed her fingers along her lower back in greeting. The way Rio’s body leaned into the touch—subtle but certain—sent a thrill straight through her.

“I grabbed some wine,” Wanda announced, swinging the bottle in one hand and balancing the dessert box in the other. “And brownies. Possibly infused with something mildly illegal, but I’ll neither confirm nor deny.”

Rio laughed and turned off the burner. “Sounds like you’re fitting right in.”

Within minutes, the three of them had settled around the small dining table. Rio had made a warm orzo salad with roasted vegetables and lemon-herb chicken. Everything tasted too good for the kind of tension still simmering just beneath the surface of their conversation.

After a few bites, Rio wiped her fingers on a dish towel and picked up her phone. “Okay, I’m gonna call Alice. Just a heads-up—she doesn’t know anything about the Threads or the magic. Let’s keep the weird to a minimum.”

“Define ‘minimum,’” Wanda muttered, but nodded.

Agatha leaned in, close enough that Rio’s thigh brushed hers under the table. “You trust her?”

“With my life,” Rio said. “And apparently, with our growing mystery.”

Rio set her phone on speaker, glancing at Agatha with a hint of amusement in her eyes. Agatha was seated across from her at the cottage’s cozy dining table, sipping a glass of wine with a look of curiosity. Wanda was settled in the corner, enjoying the atmosphere with a quiet smirk on her face.

“Okay, here she comes,” Rio said, pressing the call button. “Brace yourself.”

The phone rang a couple of times before Alice’s familiar voice echoed through the speakers. “What’s up, my favorite troublemaker?”

“Hey, Al,” Rio started, settling in beside Agatha. “I’ve got something weird to run by you.”

“Is it about your—what was it again, your ‘charming herbalist’?” Alice teased. “Cause I’m still waiting for the juicy details.”

Rio flushed, casting a glance at Agatha, who smiled slyly over the rim of her glass. Agatha had, of course, overheard Alice’s earlier comments.

“Uh, yeah,” Rio said, her voice flat as she ran a hand through her hair. “Actually, funny you should bring that up… Because Agatha’s right here. And, um, her best friend Wanda is too. So… you know.”

There was a beat of stunned silence on the other end of the line before Alice exploded in a fit of laughter. “You’ve got to be kidding me.”

“Seriously,” Rio groaned, burying her face in her hands. “So please, behave.”

Agatha leaned in toward the phone with an exaggerated sweetness in her voice. “Hi, Alice. Nice to see you again.”

“Oh, this is gold. Hi, hot apothecary lady.”

Wanda raised her glass to the phone. “Cheers to interesting company.”

Rio looked away, mortified, as Agatha smirked knowingly. Alice, of course, wasn’t holding back. “Oh, I have so many questions, Vidal.”

“Stop it,” Rio groaned. “Let me get to the point, okay?”

“Right, right. What’s going on?” Alice said, pulling it back to business, though her teasing tone was still there.

“Okay, so here’s the deal,” Rio said, leaning forward. “There’s a woman in town. Claims she’s a folklorist, doing research on local myths—specifically on the whole Thread legend.”

“The Thread?” Alice’s voice shifted slightly, more interested. “Huh, that sounds like a rabbit hole. And… you’re calling me for what, a backstory dive?”

“Well, yeah. But there’s something off about her, Alice. She mentioned stuff she shouldn’t really know. And, like, the vibe is just… wrong.”

“Wrong how?” Alice asked, her curiosity piqued.

“I don’t know,” Rio admitted. “It’s hard to put into words, but it’s like she knows too much for someone who’s just researching it academically. Something doesn’t sit right, and I need to know what she’s really after.”

Wanda shifted in her chair, sensing the tension. “You’ve got the name of the university, right? The one she claimed to be working with?”

“I do. I’ll text it to you,” Rio said, grabbing her phone and quickly typing it out to Alice. “Just… keep it under wraps for now.”

“You got it,” Alice said, the teasing edge to her voice finally fading. “Give me a few hours to dig through the deep web and see what I can find. Don’t get too lost in whatever this mystery is.”

“You’re the best,” Rio said, grateful.

“Oh, and hey,” Alice added, “I want all the dirty details later.”

Rio, not looking up from her phone, muttered, “Jesus Christ, Al. She’s right here.”

Alice’s voice dropped, though she clearly didn’t regret it one bit. “Nice. All right, I’ll check in later. Keep me posted on whatever weirdness is going down. Be careful, okay?”

“I will,” Rio replied before ending the call, turning her phone off. She dropped it onto the table, where it buzzed with a notification she ignored.

“Your friend is a bit of a handful, huh?” Agatha teased, an amused gleam in her eye.

“I’m not even going to try to explain that woman to you,” Rio muttered, but there was a fondness in her tone.

Wanda, however, had no such reservations. “Oh, I love her,” she said, her grin wide. “Sounds like she’s a bit of a character.”

“Can we focus on the weirdness at hand, please?” Rio sighed, sitting back in her chair. “What’s our next move?”

“Well,” Agatha began, her voice lowering to something more serious, “we’ve got a lead. And while I’m sure Alice is amazing at hacking her way through this stuff, I think we might need to take a more hands-on approach…”

Rio looked at Agatha, the weight of the situation settling on her shoulders. “You mean… magic?”

Wanda sat up a little straighter, her gaze sharp as it flicked between Rio and Agatha.

“All right,” she said, setting the glass down with a soft clink. “This folklorist lady—let’s just stop pretending she’s here for a dissertation. You said she gave you the creeps, Ags. That doesn’t happen often.”

Agatha nodded slowly from her spot on the couch, where she was curled into Rio’s side, one of Rio’s hands resting warmly on her thigh. “She was… too smooth. Too charming. There was something about her eyes—like she was always two steps ahead of the conversation. And the way she asked about the Threads… It didn’t feel like academic curiosity.”

Rio’s brows lifted. “You didn’t tell her anything, did you?”

“Of course not.” Agatha’s voice was firm. “But she knows something. And she didn’t just happen to show up in Thistle Grove today.”

Wanda leaned back in her chair, looking thoughtful. “Then we should find out who she really is.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “We already have Alice doing that for us.”

Wanda gave her a withering look. “And you think the Watchers have LinkedIn profiles?”

Rio laughed under her breath and muttered, “Apparently not.”

Wanda turned to her, smiling now. “This is a perfect opportunity, you know.”

“For what?” Rio asked, even though something in her chest already knew.

Wanda’s eyes glinted with mischief and gravity in equal measure. “Your first spell.”

Agatha shifted beside her. “Wanda—”

But Wanda waved her off. “You’ve been channeling power without even trying, Rio. This way, you can do it with intent. With control. Besides, if this woman is a threat, we need to know what we’re dealing with. You’ve got the fire, Ags has the focus, and I’ve got the backup wine and enough magical common sense to hold the room together. So.” She clapped her hands once. “Let’s conjure us a truth.”

Rio looked at Agatha, nervous but eager. “You think I can do this?”

Agatha studied her, then took her hand. “I know you can.”

Within minutes, they’d cleared the coffee table and started setting up the circle. Wanda pulled supplies from her bag with a flourish—candles, salt, herbs, and an obsidian mirror that shimmered faintly even in the cottage’s soft light.

Agatha guided Rio through the setup, her voice calm and even. “This will work like a scrying focus,” she said, gesturing to the mirror. “But since only I’ve seen her, you’ll need to use my memory. Let me guide you through it.”

Rio swallowed. “Is that safe?”

Wanda, from where she was tying a bundle of rosemary, smirked. “With Agatha? Absolutely.”

Agatha ignored her. She knelt in front of Rio, close enough that their knees touched. “Take my hands. I want you to close your eyes and breathe with me.”

Rio did, heart thudding.

“I’m going to give you the memory,” Agatha said gently, her voice soft like a spell in itself. “Just a flash of her face. Her voice. The way the air felt when she walked into the shop.”

Rio exhaled, nodding.

Agatha’s fingers threaded through hers. And then, like flipping through pages in the dark, Rio felt it. A crisp voice with something oily beneath it. Pale eyes, almost silver. A smile too polished. The scent of old parchment and pressed flowers. And power, just under the surface, coiled tight.

Her breath caught.

“Good,” Agatha whispered. “You’ve got her. Now say it with me.”

They repeated the spell together, voices weaving:

Through sight unseen and veil drawn tight,

Reveal the truth. Restore the light.

The mirror clouded, then shimmered. For a long second, nothing happened.

Then: a flicker.

A woman with sleek dark hair, standing in front of the apothecary. That same pale smile. A glint of silver around her neck—an amulet etched with runes that pulsed faintly.

The image sharpened: the woman stepping into a quiet inn, greeted by someone cloaked in shadows. She handed the amulet over with a murmured phrase that didn’t quite carry.

The mirror went dark.

Rio’s eyes flew open. Her fingers were trembling.

“Holy shit,” she breathed. “I saw her.”

Agatha squeezed her hands tightly. “You did it.”

Wanda set her wine glass down with a soft thunk, her eyes on the now-dark mirror. “All right,” she said, voice low and no longer teasing. “That woman didn’t just come here for folklore. The amulet she was wearing—bloodline magic. Old and very specific.”

Rio glanced at Agatha, then back at Wanda. “Wait—what does that mean? Bloodline magic?”

Wanda turned to face her fully. “It means she didn’t just stumble into that charm at some antique store. It was passed down, or stolen from someone who had magic in their blood. And the kind that lets you walk into a room and mask your presence from another witch? That’s not beginner stuff.”

“But who would want to hide from you?” Rio asked, voice quiet.

Agatha exhaled. “That’s what we’re trying to figure out.”

Wanda’s eyes didn’t leave Rio’s. “You ever heard of the Watchers?”

Rio shook her head. “No. Should I have?”

“They’re not a group you’d hear about unless you were born into magic or stepped on their toes.” Wanda leaned back slightly. “They don’t practice openly. They observe, record, and occasionally… interfere. Always in the name of keeping the balance. But that ‘balance’ usually just means suppressing the witches they think are too powerful or too unpredictable.”

Rio frowned. “So they’re like magical cops?”

Agatha let out a soft laugh, bitter around the edges. “More like inquisitors with a better PR team.”

Wanda nodded grimly. “They don’t care that we’re not part of any coven or order. That we’ve been on our own our whole lives. What matters to them is potential. And the three of us—whether we like it or not—we carry something old. Ancient. Something they fear.”

“The Threads,” Rio said softly, piecing it together.

“Exactly,” Wanda said. “We’re not just some mystical lineage that makes flowers bloom or visions appear in tea leaves. When the three Threads are aligned—when we’re present and connected—our magic doesn’t just flow. It amplifies. It reshapes. And that scares them.”

Rio’s breath caught in her throat. She looked at Agatha, who held her gaze, calm and solid, despite everything.

Wanda went on, her voice gentler now. “I don’t think this woman is a Watcher. Not officially. But the charm? The way she hid herself? She’s trained. Either she’s one of them, or she learned from them. And if she’s poking around myths about the Threads, she’s looking for something.”

Agatha’s jaw clenched. “Us.”

Wanda said, looking at both of them. “All three of us. We are the key to a shitload of power. But only if we stop being afraid of it.”

A long silence settled between them.

Then Rio said, steady and sure, “Then we learn. We prepare. And we don’t let her take anything from us.”

Wanda raised her glass again, a proud smile touching her lips. “Look at you. Already talking like a Thread.”

Agatha shook her head with a soft chuckle, eyes warm as they settled on Rio. “God help us all.”




Chapter 13: Thirteen

Chapter Notes

We are now diving head first into the mythology, so I truly hope you guys enjoy this. As always, I appreciate your comments so much!

A few hours and a couple of bottles of wine later, Wanda tossed her scarf around her neck with a flourish and raised an eyebrow at both of them as she reached for the door.

“Try not to fry the power grid again, will you?”

Rio’s jaw dropped as she turned to Agatha, mortified. “You told her?”

“I didn’t have to,” Agatha said smoothly, eyes glittering with mischief. “Wanda’s a nosy bloodhound when it comes to excess magical discharge.”

Wanda snorted, already halfway out the door. “You’re lucky I like you both. Enjoy your night, lovebirds. Keep it grounded, if you can.”

The door closed behind her with a click, and silence settled like a blanket around them.

Rio turned slowly toward Agatha, narrow-eyed. “Excess magical discharge?”

Agatha shrugged innocently and stepped closer. “You’re the one who literally blew a fuse.”

“I did not—” Rio sputtered, then groaned and buried her face in Agatha’s neck. “I’m never going to live this down.”

Agatha laughed, low and sweet, her hands sliding around Rio’s waist. “You’ll survive.”

Rio kissed her before she could make another quip, and that was the moment the shift happened again—something deeper taking hold. The kind of kiss that ached with everything they hadn’t said out loud, with gratitude and longing and the sharp, dizzying relief of finally.

They didn’t rush this time.

There was too much to feel.

Agatha’s fingers skimmed along the small of Rio’s back as they undressed each other slowly, clothes slipping off with reverence, not urgency. Each kiss, each graze of skin to skin, was a rediscovery. A memory whispered back into being.

Rio guided Agatha to the stairs and into the bedroom, their limbs tangling like they had so many times in dreams. Only this time it was real. This time Agatha moaned when Rio’s mouth found the hollow of her throat. This time Rio gasped when Agatha’s hands gripped her hips, grounding her, anchoring her. Every touch crackled—not just with magic, but with meaning. With emotion.

They didn’t speak for a long while.

There was no need.

Agatha’s name spilled from Rio’s lips in a breathless prayer when she came, and Agatha clung to her like she needed her more than air. Rio didn’t wait to catch her breath before kissing Agatha again, slower this time, sinking into the pleasure of making her unravel, of learning what made her sigh and keen and whisper curses into her shoulder.

When Agatha came again, magic flared low and warm in the air—but the lights held. The cottage buzzed gently around them, energy coursing through the walls but no longer in chaos. It responded to them. Balanced.

Agatha laughed softly against Rio’s neck, limbs heavy, content. “We only flickered the lights this time.”

Rio let out a breathless laugh, brushing Agatha’s damp hair away from her cheek. “Wanda would be so proud.”

Agatha turned her head slightly, kissed the inside of Rio’s wrist. “She’d probably call us underachievers.”

They lay in a mess of blankets, flushed and tangled, bodies still humming. Rio dragged a finger lazily along Agatha’s spine, feeling the sharp edges of longing soften into something gentle, something real.

After a long moment, Rio whispered, “I didn’t think I could feel this way again.”

Agatha’s breath hitched. She lifted her head, propped it on her hand so she could look at her. “Me neither.”

The weight of it settled between them—not heavy, but real. Welcome. Scary, but somehow right.

They didn’t need to say what this was. Not yet. But it shimmered around them like a truth too bright to ignore.

Eventually, Rio pulled a throw blanket up over both of them. The night deepened. Salem, having returned at some point, perched on a windowsill in another room, wisely keeping his distance from the emotional—and magical—carnage.

“I think we traumatized my cat,” Rio mumbled into Agatha’s hair.

Agatha snorted. “Good. That smug little gremlin has it too easy.”

They fell asleep wrapped around each other, magic curled like a living thing between them. 

But Rio’s dreams were waiting.

~*~

In the stillness of the night, Rio’s mind drifted into something deeper. She could feel the pull of it—like the weight of an ocean just beneath the surface, waiting to swallow her whole. It started like a whisper, soft but unmistakable.

And then, in a blink, everything changed.

The cottage, with its warm walls and familiar scent of herbs, faded away. The air grew cold, and Rio was standing in a dense forest. The trees were tall, their trunks dark and twisted, their branches forming a canopy so thick it blotted out the sky. There was no sun, no light to guide her. Only the faintest glow of something distant, pulsing like a heartbeat.

Rio’s feet were bare against the forest floor, the cool, damp earth pressing up against her skin. She felt it before she saw it—the weight of a thousand eyes on her, the sensation of being watched by something ancient, something far older than the trees themselves.

Her heart pounded, but her feet kept moving. Something tugged at her, pulling her deeper into the forest. She followed the path laid out in front of her, branches reaching toward her like hands, urging her forward.

As she moved, shadows seemed to flicker just beyond her peripheral vision, but whenever she turned her head, they vanished. Her breath quickened, and her steps faltered as she reached the edge of a clearing. There, standing in the center, was a figure.

A woman, tall and regal, with long dark hair that flowed like liquid midnight. She wore robes of deep violet, embroidered with threads of gold, and her eyes—when they met Rio’s—glowed like stars. They were older, wise, and infinite, like they carried the weight of ages, and they locked onto Rio’s with an unspoken understanding.

The woman didn’t speak, but Rio could feel her presence like a shock through her entire being. It was as if the woman’s essence was both an invitation and a warning.

“Who are you?” Rio asked, her voice a whisper against the silence of the forest. But the words felt hollow, useless. She already knew the answer before she could even form it.

The woman stepped forward, and the ground beneath her feet seemed to shift, like the earth itself was bending to her will. She raised a hand, and suddenly the trees around them groaned, their bark splitting open to reveal glimpses of hidden things—eyes, teeth, shapes that should not exist in this world.

The woman’s lips parted in a slight, knowing smile, and Rio felt a pull in her chest, something magnetizing her to the woman’s very being. Come closer, the figure seemed to beckon, though no words were spoken.

Rio couldn’t resist. Her feet moved of their own accord, drawn toward the woman in the center of the clearing, her heart beating louder now, the pulse in her chest almost deafening.

“Why?” Rio whispered, barely able to breathe. “Why am I here?”

The woman’s smile widened, but her eyes never left Rio’s, and Rio felt the weight of centuries settle in her bones.

“Because you are the last of them,” the woman said, her voice both a lullaby and a warning. “The last of them all.”

Before Rio could speak, a sharp pain erupted in her chest—like something tearing through her, a rip in the fabric of her own soul. She stumbled back, clutching at her heart, gasping for air.

Suddenly, the woman was gone. The forest shifted and swirled, becoming a blur of shadow and light, a dizzying whirlpool of impossible shapes. The trees vanished, and in their place was nothing but emptiness, an infinite void that stretched on forever.

And then, the figure’s voice came again, but it was not the woman now—it was something darker, something ancient.

Remember. Remember the threads. Remember your blood.

The ground beneath her feet cracked, and Rio fell, her scream swallowed by the vast nothingness that surrounded her.

~*~

Rio’s eyes snapped open. She gasped for air, her pulse racing as if she had just sprinted through the forest, as if she had just been caught in the grasp of that pull. Her body was slick with sweat, her heart still pounding from the vividness of the dream.

The cottage around her was still dark, quiet, except for the sound of Agatha’s soft breathing beside her. Rio’s hand shot out, finding her. She gripped Agatha’s wrist, her fingers trembling. Agatha stirred but didn’t wake.

The last of them. The words echoed in Rio’s mind, leaving her shaken. Who had she seen? What had just happened?

Her mind raced, but one thing was certain—this wasn’t just a dream. It was a message. A warning. A call.

And Rio had no idea what it all meant. But she felt, in every fiber of her being, that the time was coming.

She turned over and buried her face against Agatha’s chest, trying to calm the storm that raged inside her. Whatever this was, whatever was happening to her, it was far from over.

~*~

She finally managed to drift back to sleep, though her mind still raced with the echoes of the previous dream. The shadows of the woman, the pull, and the words “the last of them” clung to her like a fog.

But this time, the dream came differently.

The darkness was softer now, gentler. She found herself standing in the same dense forest from before, but it wasn’t as foreboding. The trees were no longer twisted, and the air wasn’t heavy with something ancient. Instead, it was a place that she felt like she knew—like something she hadn’t thought about in years.

She was a child again, around 7 or 8 years old, running freely through the same forest behind the cottage. The scent of damp earth and pine filled her nose, the crunch of leaves underfoot as she dashed along, laughing, her small hands brushing the underbrush. There was sunlight filtering through the trees now, golden and warm, and she felt light—lighter than she ever remembered feeling.

Then she heard it.

A soft, melodic voice, gentle but powerful, a lullaby that echoed through the trees, like the earth itself was singing. Rio slowed to a stop, her little face tilting up to listen. The voice was familiar, even though she couldn’t place it. It was as if it had been part of her for as long as she could remember, as if it had always been there.

She looked around, trying to find the source, but the voice seemed to be all around her, in the air, in the earth, and it made her feel safe—like nothing bad could happen in this place, in this moment. She smiled, eyes closing for a brief second, letting the sound wash over her.

And then, just as suddenly, the lullaby ended.

Rio turned around, feeling an overwhelming sense of longing, as if something precious was slipping away. The dream flickered, the woods blurring around her. She reached out, but everything was fading, dissolving.

~*~

Rio jolted awake, her eyes snapping open, her heart racing again, but this time in a different way. The warmth of the cottage still surrounded her, the soft rustle of the night air through the window beside the bed. But something about this dream felt different.

She wasn’t shaken by fear or confusion this time. Instead, she felt… content. A sense of calmness washed over her. She smiled softly to herself, the memory of the lullaby lingering in her mind.

But the smile quickly faltered as the confusion crept back in. It didn’t feel like a dream at all. It felt too real.

She had never run through the forest behind the cottage as a child. She had never heard a lullaby sung to her before. And yet, it all felt so familiar. Almost like… like a memory.

She turned to look at Agatha, who was still peacefully sleeping beside her. The soft rise and fall of her chest was steady and comforting. Rio didn’t want to disturb her, but the weight of what she’d just experienced was too much to ignore.

The lullaby. The forest. The feeling of being cared for, protected.

Rio couldn’t shake the sense that something had been lost—something important, something that had been a part of her, but was now out of reach.

She rolled onto her side, reaching out to gently brush a lock of Agatha’s hair from her face, her fingers brushing the smoothness of her skin. The connection between them was real, undeniable, but this dream… this memory… Rio couldn’t help but feel it was tied to something more—something from before, something that was waiting for her to remember.

But for now, all she could do was lie there, feeling the warmth of Agatha’s body against her own, and try to understand what had just happened.

Maybe, just maybe, it would all make sense soon.

~*~

Rio lay awake, her thoughts swirling around the dreams that haunted her from the night. The first one, the one that had rattled her awake earlier, still felt so vivid, like a pulse running through her veins. It was a warning, something ancient, and yet it was calling her. 

The second one, though, had felt like a forgotten piece of her life slipping back into place. It had been warm, comforting, nostalgic. But the first one was different.

She turned toward Agatha, still asleep beside her. Her breath was steady, soft, but Rio could feel the pull to talk. To explain everything she’d experienced. She wanted to share it. She needed to.

The soft morning light trickled in through the curtains, casting a warm glow over Agatha’s face. Rio couldn’t help herself. She kissed Agatha’s neck, soft and slow, just like the way her heart fluttered at the thought of the dreams. Agatha stirred, blinking up at Rio with a sleepy smile.

“Good morning,” Agatha mumbled, her voice thick with sleep.

“Morning,” Rio murmured, leaning in for another kiss. This time it was a little deeper, lingering, as if she were trying to anchor herself to something real.

Agatha returned the kiss, but the alarm interrupted their moment with a jarring buzz. Agatha groaned, clearly not ready to face the day just yet, but she didn’t move to silence it immediately. Instead, she relaxed back into Rio’s arms.

Rio pulled her closer, tucking her face into Agatha’s neck. “Let’s just stay like this a bit longer,” she whispered.

Agatha chuckled softly but didn’t argue. They stayed tangled in the sheets, neither of them ready for the day to begin. But Rio’s mind wouldn’t let go of the dreams, especially the first one—the one that had felt so vivid, so real. She couldn’t keep it inside any longer.

“Agatha,” Rio whispered into her skin. “I need to tell you something.”

Agatha blinked slowly, her eyes still hazy with sleep. “What’s wrong?”

“I had another dream,” Rio said, her voice hesitant. She pulled back just enough to look into Agatha’s eyes. “But it’s… different this time. It feels like a warning, I don’t know.”

Agatha’s brow furrowed in curiosity, her usual calm attentiveness taking over. “What kind of warning?”

“The first dream,” Rio began, her voice quieter now, more fragile. “The one where I was in a dark forest. There was a woman, but like…I don’t know, she felt…otherworldly? And she said that I was the last of them, whatever that is.” She took a breath, remembering the sharp pain in her chest as the woman’s words pierced through her. “And then something happened, I don’t know. But it was like my chest was on fire, like I’d been hit with something? And then another voice said that I should remember the Threads. Remember my blood.”

Agatha’s expression shifted, her gaze intent as she listened, her fingers lightly brushing Rio’s cheek. “That was the first dream?”

“Yeah,” Rio replied. “And it felt so… real. Like I wasn’t dreaming at all. Like I was there.”

She paused, trying to find the right words to explain it all. “The forest was so dark, Agatha. So thick with trees that the sun couldn’t even break through. And the air was… heavy. There was this feeling of being watched. Like something ancient was out there, just waiting. But when I saw her—the woman—everything froze. She looked so powerful, but… also like she was waiting for me. And her eyes—Agatha, they were so old. I don’t know how to explain it, but it felt like… like she knew me.”

Agatha listened intently, her eyes never leaving Rio’s face, absorbing every detail. Rio’s voice trembled as she continued, the weight of the dream pressing down on her.

“When she spoke, it wasn’t just her voice. It was like the whole forest spoke through her. Like everything around us understood that I was supposed to be there. She said I was the last of them… but I don’t even know who they are. I could feel her, Agatha. Like she was… inside me, too. And then… I don’t know what happened. The pain in my chest—sharp, like something tore through me.”

Rio’s breath hitched as the memory lingered, almost too overwhelming to handle. She rubbed her chest absentmindedly, as though the phantom pain still lingered. “I don’t know why, but I think she was trying to tell me something. Something important. But I don’t know what it was.”

Agatha reached out, gently cupping Rio’s face in her hands, grounding her. “The last of them… the forest… this woman. It sounds like she’s tied to something ancient. To your blood, Rio. And whatever this is, whatever you’re remembering, it might be bigger than you think.”

Rio nodded slowly, her heart still racing from the intensity of the dream. “But what does it mean? Why now? And who the hell is she, Agatha? What does she want with me?”

Agatha kissed her forehead gently, the weight of the moment settling around them. “I don’t know, but I think it’s time you started looking for answers. The magic… your magic… it’s awakening, and it’s calling you to something. She is calling you, and I think we’ll start to understand why when you follow the trail of these dreams.”

Rio felt a shiver of understanding run through her. 

“So, what should I do?” Rio asked, her voice small but determined. “What’s my next step?”

Agatha gave her a soft, reassuring smile. “You start by writing it down. Every feeling, every detail. Your magic is awakening, and that’s probably activating things inside you. This is how you’ll begin to understand it. Write it in the grimoire. Let it guide you.”

Rio’s heart fluttered at Agatha’s words. A guide. That was what she needed—something to help her make sense of this. And Agatha, with her quiet strength and wisdom, was there to help her.

“Okay,” Rio whispered, feeling a spark of determination. “I’ll do that.”

But just before Agatha could respond, Rio hesitated, her thoughts shifting. “There’s… something else,” she said, her voice uncertain, but more grounded now. “After that first dream… I had another one. But this one was different. It didn’t feel like a warning or something dark. It was… warm. It was like… a memory of me as a child. I was running through that same forest. The trees weren’t dark and twisted this time. They were alive—light was filtering through them. I remember laughing. And then I heard a voice, soft and sweet, singing a lullaby.”

Rio paused, blinking in confusion. “It felt like a memory. But it also didn’t. It was like I was the child, running and laughing, but… but it wasn’t something I actually remember. I know it’s something I’ve never lived through because I’d never even been in a forest like this as a child. But It was like the forest was mine, like it was part of me.”

Agatha’s eyes softened as she listened, her hand moving to caress Rio’s arm gently. “It sounds like you’re beginning to remember pieces of yourself, Rio. Your connection to the forest… to your bloodline. That lullaby… it might be something passed down, something you’re remembering. It’s like your past is coming to meet you.”

Rio looked at her, a bit overwhelmed by everything. “But why now, Agatha? Why do I feel like these memories are surfacing all of a sudden?”

Agatha smiled gently, brushing a lock of hair away from Rio’s face. “Because your magic is flooding your system as it awakens. It’s calling you to remember who you are, to understand the threads of your past. And as much as it might scare you, Rio, it’s guiding you. It’s bringing you back to yourself.”

Rio nodded slowly, the weight of everything settling in. “So… I write it down. I’ll start with the grimoire. I have to remember.”

Agatha kissed her softly, her eyes full of warmth and quiet confidence. “You’ll figure it out, sweetheart. One step at a time. And you’re not doing this alone.”

Rio turned into her, feeling the weight of the world—of whatever was happening to her—lighten just a little. She wasn’t alone anymore. Not with Agatha by her side.

~*~

 

The world outside was already warming with morning sun, the soft golden light filtering through the windows and casting long lines across the floor. But the cottage remained quiet, almost reluctant to shake off the remnants of dreams and magic.

Eventually, Rio and Agatha pulled themselves from the warmth of the sheets. The scent of fresh coffee drifted in from the kitchen—Agatha had charmed the coffee maker, clearly anticipating the struggle of waking up after a night like that.

Rio padded barefoot across the wood floor, tugging on Agatha’s oversized sweater she’d borrowed the night before. She opened the curtains in the living room to let the sunlight in, yawning as she glanced over the mess of sketchbooks and loose pages scattered across the low coffee table. Her notes from the last few days—visions, dreams, plants, memories—blurred together like a chaotic tapestry.

Agatha emerged a few minutes later looking casually beautiful, dressed in a deep green blouse and black jeans, her hair swept up casually but still somehow perfect. “I’ve got to open the shop in an hour,” she said, pouring herself a mug of coffee.

They made breakfast together—scrambled eggs, toast, fruit—quietly moving around each other like a familiar dance. Comfortable. Easy. Rio’s mind buzzed with the memories from the night before, but there was something reassuring about the clink of silverware and the smell of toast. Grounding.

After they ate, Rio sat cross-legged on the couch, her laptop propped up on a pillow, papers spread around her. She chewed on the end of a pen as she flipped through one of her sketchbooks, the edges smudged with charcoal and ink. “Okay,” she said aloud to no one in particular. “Outline time.”

“You’ve got a lot to work with now,” Agatha said as she pulled on her coat near the door. “Whatever’s waking up in you—it’s practically writing itself.”

Rio nodded. “Yeah, it’s just figuring out how to frame it. I think I want to center the main character around someone who’s forgotten her past but slowly realizes she’s tied to something bigger. Maybe magic.”

Agatha looked back at her with a faint smile. “Sounds familiar.”

Before Rio could respond, a low, offended meow rang out from the hallway. Salem emerged dramatically from under a chair, his fur puffed up slightly, tail flicking with irritation. He paused at the edge of the rug, staring at them both with pure feline judgment.

Rio blinked. “Oh no. Don’t tell me…”

Salem narrowed his eyes and gave another yowl that translated perfectly as How dare you banish me while you desecrated the couch? Again .

Agatha stifled a laugh behind her mug. “Looks like someone is sulking.”

Rio groaned and dropped her head back on the couch. “We need to start giving him a heads up or something.”

“He had a heads up,” Agatha said, walking over and crouching beside the couch to scratch behind Salem’s ears. “He chose drama.”

Salem swatted lightly at her hand in punishment, then leapt up onto the back of the couch with a dramatic huff, flopping down beside Rio and staring at her like she owed him rent.

“I think he forgives you,” Agatha said, amused.

Rio reached up and scratched Salem’s chin cautiously. “Thanks, your majesty.”

With a final sip of coffee, Agatha grabbed her keys. “I gotta go. Try not to let the cat guilt you into giving him all the snacks.”

“No promises,” Rio called after her.

As the door closed behind Agatha, Rio looked around the cozy, cluttered living room. Her laptop pinged softly, the blank outline waiting for her to fill it in. She took a deep breath, then set her fingers to the keys.

It was time to start telling the story.

~*~

The cursor blinked on her screen, taunting her, but for once, Rio didn’t mind. She’d actually managed to map out a solid first act and several anchor points for the graphic novel’s arc, and the ideas weren’t slowing down. If anything, they were racing ahead of her, demanding to be captured.

She sat back, stretching with a satisfied groan, then slid off the couch and padded into the kitchen for a second—okay, third—cup of coffee. Salem followed her, but when she offered him a piece of toast, he turned his nose up with disdain and leapt onto the windowsill instead, basking in a patch of light like the world’s most judgmental gargoyle.

Rio laughed and wandered back to the living room. Her gaze fell on the grimoire, still resting on the side table near the bundle of lavender Agatha had left the first night she’d come by. It hadn’t moved since. She stared at it for a moment, heart slowly picking up speed.

The dreams. She needed to write them down before they began to blur, or worse, fade completely. She should have done it already.

She set her coffee down and gently opened the cover. The pages still smelled faintly of dried herbs and ink, the binding creaking just a little like it hadn’t been opened in years. Rio hesitated, her fingers brushing over the thick parchment.

Then she reached for her pen.

The moment her fingers wrapped around it, a small shiver ran through her—goosebumps rose along her arms, and the room seemed to shift slightly around her. The air grew thicker, warmer, charged. Not in a dangerous way, but in a way that made her feel… seen. Acknowledged. Like the cottage itself was holding its breath.

This is real, she thought. This is mine.

She found a blank page near the middle—one untouched by Eliza’s spidery handwriting or the scattered botanical illustrations—and slowly began to write.

Last night, I dreamed of a woman in a forest…

She poured it all out: the cold earth beneath her bare feet, the flickering shadows, the woman’s eyes—glowing like stars. The teeth in the trees. The words “You are the last of them.”

Her hand didn’t shake, but her heart did. Still, she didn’t stop. She moved on to the second dream, the one that left her with a strange warmth in her chest. She described the lullaby—its eerie familiarity, the way it tugged at something ancient in her bones. The forest behind the cottage. The way the child had laughed. The way it had felt like her laugh. Like home.

When she finally stopped, the page was nearly full. She looked down at what she had written, the ink still glistening slightly in the late morning light, and felt something shift inside her—an anchor dropping into place.

This was the first time she had written in the grimoire.

The first time she had claimed it.

The first time she had truly, consciously stepped into the magic that had been waiting for her all along.

She closed the book gently, pressing her palm against the cover for a long moment. Then she exhaled and leaned back into the couch, staring at the ceiling with a faint smile, heart still pounding.

Outside the window, the breeze stirred the branches of the old trees lining the property, and somewhere far off in the woods, a bird sang a melody that almost—almost—echoed the lullaby from her dream.

~*~

Rio had just set the grimoire aside when her phone buzzed from the arm of the couch. She reached for it, expecting a check-in from Agatha, but the screen lit up with Alice Wu.

She answered with a warm, “Hey, stranger.”

Alice didn’t waste time. “Okay, I’ve got something. And I’m telling you now, it’s giving serious horror movie vibes.”

Rio sat up straighter, heart kicking up a notch. “About Mara Greaves?”

“Yup. So, first off, there’s basically no online presence for her. No Twitter, no Instagram, no LinkedIn, no professional website. Even the university mentions are dusty—like, early 2000s dusty.”

“So she’s either off the grid or doesn’t want to be found.”

“Exactly. But here’s where it gets weird. I found a handful of papers published under her name, mostly in niche folklore and anthropology journals—legit enough, if a little… fringe. But the content? It starts out all historical—ancient rites, bloodlines, matrilineal myths—but then it veers. She gets obsessed with these so-called ‘hereditary lineages’ and something she calls ‘The Bound Three.’”

Rio blinked. “The what?”

“Right? It sounded like a cult or a fairytale. But she writes about it like it’s real. There’s a pattern in the writing, too—women in threes, tied by blood, by fate, blah blah blah. Like myth meets conspiracy theory.”

A chill worked its way up Rio’s spine.

“I even found a post on an old academic blog—someone claiming Mara Greaves might be a pseudonym. And get this, the name that kept coming up as an alternate was ‘Dahlia.’ Just Dahlia. You know, like Cher. Or Zendaya.”

Rio went still. “Dahlia,” she repeated slowly.

“You know her?” Alice asked, tone suddenly serious.

“No. I don’t think so,” Rio said, a little too quickly. “The name’s just… familiar, I guess.”

“Well, I don’t know what you’re doing in that little town, but I’m telling you, if you see a woman in a velvet cloak offering you tea made from grave moss or whatever, run.”

Rio gave a weak laugh. “Noted.”

“I mean it. You and weirdness are a magnet lately.”

“You have no idea,” Rio murmured.

“What was that?”

“Nothing,” she said quickly. “Thanks for looking into her, Al. You’re the best.”

“You owe me pie. And a beer.”

“Consider it done. I’ll call you soon.”

“Be safe, okay?”

“I will. Promise.”

Rio ended the call, phone resting in her palm as her mind spun. Dahlia. The Bound Three. A folklorist who didn’t really exist. Her fingers drifted toward the grimoire again, a pulse fluttering beneath her skin.

This wasn’t folklore.

It was her life.

~*~

The sun was bright over Thistle Grove, but it did little to warm the chill working its way down Rio’s spine.

She hadn’t intended to go far—just a quick walk, clear her head after the call with Alice and the restless energy from her dreams. Maybe drop by the apothecary, see Agatha, maybe kiss her stupid and pretend the world wasn’t creeping closer with every strange thread that pulled tighter around her life.

She was halfway through the square, coffee in one hand, sketchbook tucked under her arm, when she saw her.

A woman standing outside the antique store, her posture graceful but unnervingly still. Her coat was deep plum, the fabric old-fashioned and beautifully made, silver buttons glinting in the sunlight. She was speaking to Mr. Delaney, the shopkeeper, who was laughing nervously at something she’d said.

Rio stopped in her tracks.

That face.

She’d seen it before—last night, behind Agatha’s eyes, when Wanda guided her into the spell. She knew that long, dark coat, the pale streak of hair, the unnerving calm that radiated off her like a second skin.

Mara Greaves.

Except the memory hadn’t done her justice. In real life, she was worse—more vivid, more magnetic. And those eyes… those eyes turned on Rio the moment she looked too long.

Mara’s gaze cut through the air between them, as though she’d felt Rio’s recognition like a flare in the dark.

Rio’s breath caught.

Mara didn’t speak. She only offered a small, curious smile. Not warm. Not threatening either. Just… weird. Like she’d been waiting for Rio to catch up.

Rio’s fingers tightened around her coffee cup.

She turned abruptly and walked—fast—toward the apothecary, heart hammering against her ribs. She didn’t look back.

She didn’t have to.

She could still feel those eyes on her.

~*~

The bell above the apothecary door gave its usual cheerful chime as Rio stepped inside, but she barely noticed it. Her thoughts were a blur, her stomach tight. She kept her expression carefully blank as she crossed the threshold, forcing herself to breathe like a normal person. Just another morning. Just another visit to see her maybe-girlfriend-maybe-more who also happened to be a witch.

Agatha stood behind the counter, her hair pinned back loosely, sleeves rolled up, helping a trio of tourists sniff their way through a set of spell candles. She glanced up at the sound of the bell, her eyes catching Rio’s—and something in her gaze sharpened immediately.

But she didn’t say a word.

Rio offered a tight smile and moved to the shelves, pretending to examine a jar of lavender bath salts while her brain scrambled to keep her heart from jumping out of her chest.

Mara Greaves had stared at her like she’d seen her before—like she knew.

And after what Alice told her on the phone—about how Mara had lied about being a folklorist, how her credentials didn’t quite line up… it was all just a little too much.

She didn’t even remember walking here. Her body had just moved.

Eventually, the customers made their purchases and left in a flurry of bags and thank-yous. Agatha locked the door behind them, flipped the sign, and then turned slowly toward Rio, her brow already furrowing.

“Okay,” she said, voice low. “What happened?”

Rio looked at her for a beat, then exhaled through her nose and crossed the room.

“I saw her,” she said. “Mara Greaves. She was talking to Delaney near the bookstore. And when I walked past… she looked at me. Like—like she recognized me.”

Agatha blinked. “Recognized you?”

Rio nodded. “It wasn’t just a glance. She paused. Her whole face changed, like she was trying to place me. And it felt—Agatha, it felt wrong. It gave me chills.”

She hesitated, then added, “Alice called. Said she what she could find on Mara Greaves was sketchy at best. And get this, her supposed research centers around bloodlines and what she called the bound three or something like that.” 

Agatha’s face had gone very still. “She’s not just some nosy folklorist.”

“No,” Rio said. “She’s something else. And it looks like she knows who I am. Just like she knew who you were.”

Agatha reached for her, hands settling gently on her arms. “Okay. That’s what we needed to know.”

“I’m sorry I barged in—”

“Don’t be.” Her voice was firmer now. “You did the right thing.”

Rio swallowed. “So what do we do?”

Agatha glanced toward the back of the shop, then leaned in. “We keep playing it cool. But tonight, we’re calling Wanda. We need to start thinking about defense, especially for you. And we’re going to figure out exactly what this woman wants.”

 

Chapter 14: Fourteen

Agatha knew something was wrong the second Rio walked into the shop.

She was too still. Too careful. She didn’t offer one of her usual quips or sidelong smirks. Just a polite nod, as if she were a stranger walking into an unfamiliar place. Her eyes skimmed the shelves but didn’t see anything.

Agatha played it cool, keeping one eye on the tourists as she rang up their candles, but her attention was fully on Rio—every twitch of her hand, the tightness in her jaw. By the time the last customer left and the door clicked shut, she had already flipped the sign to closed for lunch and was rounding the counter.

“Okay,” she said softly. “What happened?”

Rio told her everything. About Mara. About the way she’d looked at her. About the phone call from Alice and the false identities and the deep, aching feeling that none of this was a coincidence.

By the time she finished, Agatha could see the crackle of fear behind her eyes, the way she clutched her own arms like she didn’t trust her body to stay grounded.

Agatha didn’t hesitate. She stepped forward and slid her hands up Rio’s arms, then cupped her face.

“Breathe,” she murmured. “You’re okay.”

Rio started to nod, but Agatha leaned in and kissed her—not rushed, not fiery, just soft and steady. Grounding. Their mouths fit together easily, familiarly now, like muscle memory. Agatha kissed her again, slower this time, and felt Rio begin to melt a little in her arms.

When they parted, Rio’s eyes had softened just a touch, but her brow was still furrowed.

“I’m still a little freaked out,” she whispered.

“I’d be more worried if you weren’t,” Agatha said gently. “But you’re not alone, okay? You have me. You have Wanda. We’ll figure out what she’s doing here.”

Rio nodded slowly. “What time is it?”

“Almost noon. Wanna step out? I need a break too. And I know Wanda only has classes until twelve today—we can pick her up and head back to her place.”

Rio managed a faint smile. “You think Wanda will feed us?”

Agatha grinned. “I know she will. She cooks when she’s stressed out.”

She grabbed her coat, slipped a “Back at 2pm” sign in the window, and took Rio’s hand without thinking. It felt natural now, easy. Even when everything else was spiraling.

As they stepped out into the cool air and started toward the elementary school, Agatha tightened her grip slightly.

She was worried, yes. Deeply. But she was also certain of one thing.

Whatever Mara Greaves was doing in Thistle Grove—she had just made a serious mistake by getting too close to the Threads.

~*~

Rio took a slow sip of water before she spoke. “Alice didn’t come up totally empty. There’s some academic record—really obscure—of someone named Mara Greaves from the early 2000s. Something about the ‘Bound Three’. But after that, she just… vanished.”

Agatha’s brows drew together. “Vanished, or changed her name?”

Rio gave a tight nod. “That’s the thing. Alice found a name that kept popping up. Someone referred to her as Dahlia. Just Dahlia. No last name. Alice thinks it was the same person. Same research field, same tone of writing.”

Wanda froze with a fork halfway to her mouth. “Dahlia?”

She stood slowly, moving to her bookshelf, pulling down an old leather-bound tome filled with local stories and folklore. She flipped through it quickly, eyes scanning the pages, until she found what she was looking for.

“Here,” she said, laying the book open.

The page was yellowed with age, featuring a faded black-and-white photo: Thistle Grove Harvest Festival, 1958.

In the back row, barely visible, stood a woman with dark hair and piercing eyes. Even in the old photograph, something about her was unnerving. Timeless.

“There,” Wanda said, pointing. “That’s her, isn’t it? She’s never listed with a last name. Just Dahlia. My gran used to tell stories about her. Said she didn’t age. That she showed up every few decades, always asking questions. Listening. Writing things down.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Well, shit. She looks exactly the same. That picture’s over sixty years old.”

Rio felt the chill crawl up her spine. “And now she’s back in Thistle Grove.”

Wanda nodded grimly. “She’s not just a folklorist. She’s something else. And if she looked at you like she recognized you…”

“She did,” Rio whispered. “She looked right at me, like I was a puzzle she’d already solved.”

Agatha reached over and took her hand. “Then it’s time we figure out what she’s really doing here.”

~*~

By the time they got back to the cottage, the sky had gone from bright to overcast, the air heavy with the scent of pine and distant rain. Agatha didn’t waste time. As soon as the door closed behind them, she turned to Rio, her tone firm but kind.

“We’re going to ward this place,” she said, slipping off her coat and hanging it on the hook by the door. “Top to bottom. Every threshold, every window, even the chimney.”

Rio blinked. “You mean like… a magical security system?”

“Yup,” Agatha said. “Protection. Repulsion. Confusion for those who don’t belong. It won’t make the place impenetrable, but it’ll slow someone like her down. And that gives us time.”

Rio nodded, rubbing her arms. “What about Wanda?”

“I told her to do the same. She’ll reinforce the wards around her place before nightfall.” Agatha walked to the hearth and lit a small bundle of dried rosemary and mugwort. The smoke curled upward, fragrant and sharp. “And I’ll be doing mine tonight too.”

Rio watched her for a beat, then stepped closer. “You’re not just going to do it for me, are you?”

Agatha turned to face her, a smile playing faintly on her lips. “Gods, no. I’m going to teach you. You need to know how to focus your magic—not just let it spark when it wants, but use it with control and intent. Especially now.”

Rio swallowed hard and nodded again.

Agatha stepped forward, reaching for her hand. “We’ll start with grounding. Then intent. Then casting. And when we’re done, this place will be yours in every way that matters. Safe. Claimed. Guarded.”

The words wrapped around Rio like a warm cloak. She squeezed Agatha’s hand.

“Okay. Let’s do this.”

Agatha stood at the threshold of the cottage, fingers trailing over the weathered wood of the front door. The scent of old pine and drying herbs hung in the air, and the flicker of candlelight softened the corners of the space that had begun, slowly, to feel like a home again. It had always been Eliza’s sanctuary—but now, it belonged to Rio.

And it needed to be protected.

She glanced at Rio, who hovered near the kitchen, arms folded across her chest like she wasn’t sure whether to be anxious or eager.

Agatha reached into her satchel and pulled out a small pouch of powdered rowan bark and salt, a handful of dried vervain, and a thin, dark-bladed knife. She set it all carefully on the table and met Rio’s eyes.

“Come here,” she said gently. “Let’s start with grounding.”

Rio approached and stood in front of her, visibly trying to slow her breathing.

Agatha took her hands, holding them between her own.

“You already know what magic feels like. You’ve felt it when it erupts—when it reacts. But now I want you to feel it when you reach for it voluntarily. Not when it rushes you. Start by closing your eyes.”

Rio obeyed.

“Feel your breath,” Agatha whispered. “Feel the way it sits in your body. Let it sink down. Down into your ribs, into your hips, into the soles of your feet.”

The silence stretched. Outside, the wind rustled the trees, but inside there was only warmth.

Agatha let her own magic hum low, steady beneath her skin—not enough to interfere, just enough for Rio to feel it if she reached out.

Rio’s brow furrowed slightly, and then smoothed.

“I think I feel it,” she murmured. “It’s like—heat. In my chest.”

Agatha smiled. “Good. That’s your center. Keep that flame steady. Now I want you to imagine that heat flowing into the earth beneath your feet. Like roots. Let it anchor you.”

She guided Rio through it, feeling the shift in the air as her magic settled—like a thread being slowly woven through the room, stitched into the very bones of the cottage.

Agatha stepped back and retrieved the pouch of rowan and salt.

“This is protection. I’ll mark the outer points, but you will seal them. Every line of it will hold stronger if it comes from you.”

Rio opened her eyes, more focused now.

“What do I say?”

Agatha crouched near the threshold, drawing a small sigil with her finger in the dust. “Words are just tools to direct will. Say what you mean. Mean it. Try: ‘ None may cross who wish me harm. This space is mine, and mine to keep.’”

Rio repeated the phrase softly, then again, louder, and when she spoke it a third time, the sigil pulsed faintly, a bronze shimmer before vanishing into the wood grain.

Agatha blinked. “Good. Again. The windows now.”

They moved through the cottage together, Rio tracing her fingers along the frames, speaking her intent aloud. Each time, the air shifted—not much, just enough that Agatha felt it. The cottage grew warmer, brighter. More alive.

She couldn’t help the thrill of pride that curled in her chest.

At the hearth, Rio faltered. “I don’t know what to say this time.”

Agatha stepped close behind her, letting her hands rest lightly on Rio’s hips. “Speak to the fire. Tell it you want it to guard this place. Not to burn, but to watch.”

Rio hesitated, then whispered, “Guard this home, spirit of flame. Burn away what doesn’t belong.”

The coals in the hearth flared suddenly, a ripple of orange light licking up toward the chimney, before settling again. Agatha felt the hair on her arms rise.

“Okay,” Rio breathed. “Did I do that?”

“You absolutely did,” Agatha murmured, amazed. “You’re… strong. It’s like your power knows this house already.”

Rio turned toward her, visibly flushed from focus and wonder. “I think it does. It feels… right. Like it’s answering me.”

Agatha smiled. “It is.”

She reached up and brushed a bit of ash from Rio’s cheek. “Let’s do the back door, and then I’ll show you how to knot wards into string for the window panes.”

As they walked together to the rear of the house, Agatha glanced at her out of the corner of her eye.

Rio had always carried power in her—flickering, stormy, untrained—but now, for the first time, she was channeling it. Owning it. Her magic was still wild, yes, but it was beginning to sharpen. To answer her voice, not just her fear.

And gods help anyone who dared try to cross her now.

~*~

The late afternoon sunlight slanted warmly through the lace curtains of The Hollow, painting golden patterns across the worn wood floors. Wanda and Agatha sat in their usual spot near the front window, nursing mugs of spiced coffee and chatting with Lilia, who hovered behind the counter with a satisfied little smirk like she always knew more than she let on.

It had been a couple of days since Agatha had taught Rio on how to ward the cottage, and so far, things had been thankfully quiet. 

Wanda was mid-story about one of her particularly precocious students when the door chimed open.

They all glanced over casually—but Agatha froze when she saw the woman who stepped inside.

Short, stylish, slightly frazzled from travel, but unmistakably familiar. Alice Wu.

She looked around the cozy space, clearly scanning for someone.

“Uh—hi,” she said, approaching the counter. “I was wondering if you could point me in the direction of Rio Vidal’s place?”

Lilia straightened up, her eyes twinkling. “Well now, aren’t you a sight. You must be Alice.”

Alice’s eyes widened slightly. “How do you—?”

That was when Wanda jumped in and gave her a little wave from the table. “Hi! FaceTime, remember? I’m Wanda. That’s Agatha.”

Alice blinked, then grinned. “Right! Right. Wow. Okay—this is a really small town.”

Agatha stood, surprised but amused. “You’re looking for Rio?”

“Yeah. I wanted to surprise her for her birthday.” She shrugged, the corners of her mouth lifting. “She hates it when I make a big deal out of it, so I figured I’d make a small deal out of it instead. Just show up.”

Agatha blinked. “Her birthday?”

Alice tilted her head. “Tomorrow. The 6th. Wait—did she not tell you?”

Wanda covered her snort behind her mug. Agatha recovered quickly, smoothing over her surprise.

“No, she didn’t mention it,” Agatha said, trying to sound casual, but Wanda could already see the wheels turning behind her eyes. 

Alice shook her head with a laugh. “She always pretends it’s just another day, but I figured, you know… new town, new start. I couldn’t let her be alone. Especially not this year.”

“Well, she’s definitely not alone,” Agatha said before she could stop herself, voice soft but firm. Then she added quickly, “We can take you to the cottage, if you’d like.”

Alice smiled warmly at that, relief flickering in her eyes. “Thanks. I appreciate that.”

As Wanda asked Alice how her flight had been, Agatha stood quietly, her mind racing—not because she was upset Rio hadn’t told her, but because suddenly, all she could think about was how she wanted to make tomorrow special too.

Rio might not like to celebrate—but maybe it was time she learned how it felt to be truly cherished.

~*~

By the time they reached the cottage, the December sky had already started turning dusky gold, that soft burnished light that always made the woods behind Rio’s place feel a little enchanted. 

Alice followed a few steps behind Agatha and Wanda, bundled in a scarf and carrying a box of Rio’s favorite pastries from the Hollow. She looked like she was vibrating with excitement.

Agatha, on the other hand, was quiet. Processing. The revelation that it was Rio’s birthday tomorrow had caught her off guard—but in the kind of way that stirred something warm and protective in her chest.

Wanda had been smug the whole walk over. “You’re thinking about doing something, aren’t you?”

Agatha had only lifted an eyebrow. “She didn’t even tell me. She clearly didn’t want to make a thing out of it.”

“Exactly why you should.”

They stepped up to the front porch and Wanda gave the door a sharp little knock.

From inside, Salem let out an offended yowl—probably having been disturbed from his very important nap—and Rio’s muffled voice called, “Hang on!”

The door creaked open a few seconds later.

Rio stood there in thick socks and leggings, an old sweater hanging off her shoulder. A pencil was stuck in her messy bun, and she had a half-full mug of coffee in hand. She looked relaxed, maybe even happy—until she noticed the unexpected third person standing just behind Agatha and Wanda.

Her eyes widened.

“Alice?!”

Alice lit up. “Hey, stranger.”

Rio froze, mouth falling open, before setting her coffee down on the windowsill and practically tackling Alice in a hug. “Oh my god! What are you doing here? How are you here?!”

Alice laughed as Rio squeezed her. “Surprising you for your birthday, obviously.”

“You flew across the country?”

“Well, yeah.” Alice pulled back just enough to look at her. “Did you really think I wouldn’t show up for your birthday just because you decided to move to the other end of the universe?”

Rio flushed, still clearly overwhelmed. “I—no, I just—you know I don’t really do the whole birthday thing.”

Agatha stepped in then, quieter but close. “You didn’t tell me.”

Rio met her eyes, a soft kind of guilt brushing over her features. “It’s not you. I just don’t like the fuss. It never really meant anything growing up, you know?”

Agatha nodded slowly. “It means something now.”

Rio’s face flickered—an emotion she tried to tamp down—and then she looked back at Alice. “How did you even find this place?”

“Ran into these two when I stopped to ask for directions at a diner. They recognized me.”

Rio laughed, still a little stunned, still holding Alice’s arm like she couldn’t quite believe she was real. “I can’t believe you’re really here.

“You love it,” Alice said.

Rio glanced at Agatha again, then back at the three of them on her doorstep. Her voice dropped a little. “Yeah. I really do.”

“Now,” said Wanda, ushering them all forward, “let’s get inside before I freeze to death. I can’t feel my damn nose.”

“Come in, come in,” Rio said, opening the door wider. “God, this is insane.”

Agatha caught her hand as she passed, gave it a squeeze. “Just wait until tomorrow, birthday girl.”

Rio narrowed her eyes at her. “Don’t you start.”

But she was smiling.

And Agatha couldn’t look away.

~*~

Once everyone had stepped inside, shaking off the cold and shedding coats, scarves, and boots, Rio turned toward Alice, gesturing toward the couch. “Make yourself at home. There’s coffee if you want some—though I make no promises about the strength.”

But then her eyes found Agatha’s. Something shifted in her expression—softened. She took a quiet step closer and touched Agatha’s wrist gently. “Hey,” she said, her voice lower now, just for her. “You didn’t even get a proper hello.”

Agatha smiled faintly, leaning in without hesitation. “I noticed.”

Rio brushed her fingers down Agatha’s arm, then slid them around her waist, pulling her in. “Thank you,” she murmured, voice just above a whisper. “For bringing her. For being here.”

Agatha tilted her chin and leaned in, her lips finding Rio’s with practiced ease—warm and slow and grounding. A kiss that said: I’ve got you. I’m here.

Rio melted into it for a breath, then pulled back with a contented sigh. Agatha tucked a strand of hair behind Rio’s ear. “I knew you’d be happy to see your best friend.”

Rio nodded, a little dazed still, the adrenaline of surprise giving way to something more content. “You were right.”

From the living room, Alice called, “Are you two going to keep making out in the entryway or should we just9 pretend not to notice?”

Rio groaned. “God, she’s going to be impossible now.”

“I’m already impossible,” Alice replied, grinning from the couch. “Now I’m just winning.”

Agatha laughed, kissed Rio’s cheek one more time, and stepped back. “Come on, birthday girl. Let’s show your best friend what Thistle Grove hospitality really looks like.”

Rio grabbed the pastry box Alice had brought and made a face. “This smells suspiciously like my favorite lemon tarts.”

“It is your favorite lemon tarts,” Alice said. “Because I love you and also because I bribed the woman at the Hollow with way too much cash to make extra just for you.”

Rio blinked. “I might cry.”

“You’re allowed. It’s your birthday weekend.”

Rio set the box down on the coffee table and threw a cushion at her. “Traitor.”

Alice caught it and flopped back dramatically. “Guilty as charged.”

Agatha settled beside Rio, their knees touching, the warmth between them solid and sure. Wanda emerged from the kitchen holding a mug of coffee and a handful of cookies.

Outside, the sky had turned to deep indigo. Inside, the lights were soft, the laughter easy, the walls holding onto the magic of love, friendship, and something beginning to feel like family.

And for once, Rio didn’t feel like hiding from her birthday.

Not at all.

~*~

The scent of lemon tarts and roasted coffee clung to the warm air inside the cottage, curling around Agatha like a shawl. She sipped from her mug as she watched Rio and Alice move around each other with the ease of old friendship—half snark, half secret language. Wanda had made herself at home on the floor, as usual, nursing a cup of something with an herbal bite.

Agatha, tucked into the corner of the couch with her legs folded beneath her, wasn’t used to being surrounded like this. It should have made her restless. Instead, she found herself almost… content.

Alice was thumbing through Rio’s sketchbook, pausing to study panels and flip back occasionally, clearly impressed. “These are so good,” she said, mouth full of tart. “Like—you’ve gotta be halfway through the next book already.”

“Halfway through the outline,” Rio said, perched on the armrest right beside Agatha. “Not the same thing.”

“She’s being modest,” Agatha said with a small, amused smile. “I’ve seen some of her boards and they’re amazing.”

“Can I see it?” Alice asked, bright-eyed.

“No, not yet” Rio said, apologetically. “Private. Agatha’s only seen them cause they’re in my room.”

“Rude.”

“Artist boundaries,” she said with a smirk.

Agatha nudged Rio’s hip lightly, just to feel her warmth. It still surprised her—how easily affection seemed to slip between them now. She didn’t take it for granted.

A sharp mrow turned all their heads. Salem had emerged from wherever he’d been hiding, his sleek gray form winding through the shadows until he paused at the edge of the rug, glaring.

Agatha raised a brow. “Dramatic entrance.”

Rio leaned toward her and whispered, “He’s still mad we kicked him off the couch the other night.”

Wanda coughed pointedly into her mug, hiding a laugh.

Salem approached Alice like a tiny god assessing a mortal. She held still, brow lifted, and only moved when he—unexpectedly—leapt up and claimed her lap with casual arrogance.

“Well, hello to you too,” she murmured, scratching behind his ears. “Is he always this forward?”

“He usually shies away from strangers,” Rio commented, surprised.

Alice grinned. “I have a very approachable aura.”

Salem sat smugly for a moment longer before hopping down and marching over to Agatha, flopping bonelessly at her feet like a child proving a point.

“He’s got a flair for the dramatic,” Alice said. “I respect it.”

Alice flopped dramatically across the cushions. “God, I missed you. You better believe we’re doing something tomorrow for your birthday, Vidal. Thistle Grove better have cake or sparklers or something witchy.”

Agatha’s heart skipped.

“Witchy,” Alice clarified quickly. “You know. The vibe. Candles. Mystical fog. Old women who can tell your whole future by the state of your boots.”

Wanda snorted into her cup.

Rio nearly choked on her drink.

Agatha covered a smile with her hand and shot Wanda a look: say nothing.

Salem gave an imperious sniff.

Alice leaned back, petting him again. “Your cat definitely judges people.”

“He judges everyone,” Rio laughed.

Agatha’s hand found Rio’s again, fingers twining lazily. The room hummed with warmth and firelight, and though her magic was quiet, it pulsed under her skin, content. 

Rio glanced sideways, giving her a small, quiet smile meant only for her. Agatha leaned in and kissed her temple, and Rio whispered something too low for anyone else to hear.

“Thanks for not making a big deal.”

Agatha brushed a thumb over her knuckles. “Too late.”

~*~

Wanda had gone home a little while ago, and Alice had started yawning so frequently it was almost musical. The cottage had settled into a cozy stillness, the kind that made Agatha want to curl up in front of the fire with Rio and forget the outside world existed.

“I should probably crash,” Alice said, rubbing her eyes. “Need my full energy to harass Rio properly tomorrow.”

Rio snorted. “You’ve never needed energy for that.”

“True,” Alice said, stretching. “So—couch?”

Rio glanced toward it and winced. “Yeah. Unless you want to risk your life with the floor.”

“The couch is fine,” Alice said, already digging through her bag for her toothbrush.

As soon as she disappeared into the bathroom, Agatha turned to Rio with a raised eyebrow. “Are you going to let your best friend sleep on that rock masquerading as furniture?”

Rio groaned. “I was going to try to make it better? I saw a couple of handy spells in the grimoire. But I don’t want her to notice anything. The outside of the couch has to stay exactly the same.”

Agatha stepped in closer, voice quiet and warm. “Then that’s the spell. Transformation on the inside, illusion on the outside. You can do it. I’ll help.”

Rio hesitated, looking from Agatha to the couch like it might bite her. “What if I mess it up? What if it explodes? Or folds in on itself? Or starts talking?”

“It won’t,” Agatha said with a soft laugh. “You’re getting better every day, and you already have the intent—comfort, safety, subtlety. That’s half the spell right there.”

Rio exhaled, steadying herself. “Okay. Let’s do this.”

She stepped forward, placing her hands on the back cushions. Her voice was barely a whisper as she spoke the incantation. There was a slight hum in the air, a faint shimmer only a witch would see, and then—the cushions plumped, the interior support shifted, and the couch sighed into a deep, warm, cushy comfort.

On the outside, it remained exactly as it had before—well-worn but intact, a humble piece of furniture.

Rio blinked. “Did it work?”

Agatha walked over, pressed a hand to the back, then sat—sinking into the plush, transformed inside. “Oh yes. She’s going to think you’ve had this cozy couch all along.”

Rio grinned, her pride blooming beneath the nerves. “Damn. I actually did it.”

“You did,” Agatha said, eyes bright. “And it’s perfect.”

“Thanks, babe,” Rio said automatically, still smiling.

Agatha stilled. “Did you just call me babe?”

Rio froze. “No.”

“You did.”

“Fine,” Rio muttered, eyes warm with quiet affection. “Maybe I did. So?”

Agatha leaned in, lips brushing her cheek. “I like it.”

Before she could kiss her properly, Alice stepped out of the bathroom, towel-drying her hands. “Whoa. That couch looks—shockingly decent. Did I just not sit on it properly before?”

Agatha and Rio shared a brief, silent look.

“Must’ve been the angle,” Rio said quickly.

Alice shrugged and flopped down. “Well, I call dibs on this spot for life. Night, ladies. And Salem, wherever you are.”

Salem blinked lazily from under a chair, his tail flicking like he was considering a response.

“Night, Alice,” Rio said, still softly grinning.

When they slipped into the bedroom a few minutes later, Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio from behind and murmured against her ear, “You’re more powerful than you know.”

Rio tilted her head toward her. “I’ve got a pretty great teacher.”

Agatha kissed the curve of her neck. “You’ve got a good heart. The magic just follows.”

Rio turned, eyes shadowed with flickers of worry that hadn’t quite faded, but there was something else now, something stronger—certainty, longing, the quiet promise of trust.

Agatha reached for her without a word, tucking a strand of hair behind Rio’s ear before drawing her in. Their mouths met slowly, reverently, like they had all the time in the world. There was no rush, no hunger too sharp. Just this: the gentle heat between them, the soft exhale of relief at being alone again.

Rio’s hands settled at Agatha’s waist, tugging her closer, and Agatha let herself be guided back toward the bed. The mattress dipped beneath them, and everything outside the circle of their bodies melted away.

Agatha pressed kisses down the line of Rio’s jaw, over the curve of her throat, feeling every hitch in her breath like a secret shared. She moved with care, reverence, not because Rio was fragile—but because she was precious.

“You did so well today,” she whispered as she ran her fingers over Rio’s ribs, the quiet thrum of magic still lingering beneath her skin. “You were amazing. And brilliant. And mine.”

Rio’s fingers curled into Agatha’s shirt, her voice suddenly tight from the praise. “You’re going to make me cry, you know.”

“Let me make you feel cherished instead,” Agatha said, kissing her softly again, again, until Rio melted into her with a sigh.

Clothes were shed in slow touches, warm and unhurried, until there was nothing left between them but skin and honesty. Agatha made love to her with a quiet fierceness, like she could imprint the truth into Rio’s body: you’re not alone anymore. You are known. You are safe.

And when Rio whispered her name—low and reverent, the sound trembling at the edge of a moan—Agatha thought, this is what it means to belong.

They moved together in sync, wrapped in starlight and soft breaths, and when Rio finally came apart beneath her, Agatha held her through every wave, murmuring her name like a spell, like a vow.

After, when the world had settled again, they lay tangled together in the sheets, heartbeats slowing, breath steady.

Rio’s hand brushed over Agatha’s stomach in lazy patterns. “I still can’t believe Alice is here.”

Agatha hummed, pressing a kiss to her temple. “She’s good for you.”

“So are you,” Rio said, voice drowsy but sure. 

Agatha didn’t say anything—just held her tighter, lips curving into the barest of smiles.

Saturday would bring surprises. Celebrations. Maybe even trouble.

But for now, in this sliver of quiet night, they had each other.

And that was enough.

~*~

Chapter 15: Fifteen

Chapter Notes

I apologize for the long wait. Had a family emergency and things are just now settling down again.

Hope you enjoy this one.

Rio woke slowly, the weight of sleep still heavy on her limbs, and a strange warmth curling in her chest.

She’d been dreaming again.

This one had the same quality as the others—half dream, half memory, soft around the edges but vivid enough to leave a mark. Snow fell gently in the forest behind the cottage, blanketing the trees in a quiet hush. Someone had strung little glass lanterns between the branches, and a table had been set beneath the shelter of an old pine, tucked in close to the trunk where the snow didn’t reach.

A birthday cake sat at the center, white frosting with sugared cranberries on top, flickering candles struggling to stay lit in the cold. She’d been small again, bundled in a knit scarf and red mittens, cheeks flushed from the cold. Laughter rang through the trees—hers, bright and unburdened. There were voices she didn’t quite recognize, soft and kind, singing a lullaby that twisted into something familiar. Something warm.

She couldn’t remember who held her hand, but she remembered the feeling.

Loved. Wanted.

She opened her eyes slowly. The bedroom was quiet except for the sound of Agatha breathing beside her. The witch hadn’t stirred yet, still wrapped in sleep, her hair fanned across the pillow like ink spilled in water.

Rio turned toward her, nestling in closer, and pressed a kiss just beneath her jaw. “Hey,” she whispered. “You awake?”

“Mmm. Wasn’t,” Agatha murmured, voice still low with sleep. “But I’m not complaining.”

“I had another one,” Rio said, voice barely above a whisper. “A dream, but… it felt real. Like a memory again.”

That got Agatha’s attention. Her eyes opened slowly, and she reached for Rio, tucking her close. “Tell me.”

Rio closed her eyes, replaying the details. “It was winter. Snow everywhere. But I wasn’t cold. There were lanterns in the trees and… a little table under a pine. A birthday cake. I was just a kid. Someone sang to me. I don’t know who.”

Agatha ran her hand down Rio’s back in long, slow strokes. “Do you remember the song?”

“Bits of it. Like a lullaby. But it wasn’t sad. It felt… like I mattered. Like someone really wanted me to have a good birthday.”

Agatha exhaled quietly. “I wonder if that’s an actual memory.”

Rio shook her head, her throat tight. “It can’t be. I never celebrated growing up. Birthdays were just another day in the system. But this dream—it felt like the kind of memory I should have had.”

Agatha pressed a kiss to her forehead. “Then maybe it’s your legacy catching up to you. Telling you that you’re home now. That it’s safe to feel joy, too.”

Rio smiled softly. “You’re kind of good at this, you know.”

“At what?”

“This… comforting thing.”

“I’ve had practice,” Agatha murmured, pulling her a little closer. “And I happen to care about you a lot, baby.”

Rio stilled slightly, then laughed under her breath. “Still not over you calling me baby.”

Agatha grinned against her skin. “Get used to it.”

And for once, Rio thought maybe she could.

~*~

They didn’t get up right away. Instead, they stayed in that suspended state between awake and asleep, just enjoying the closeness.

The morning light filtered in through the curtains, pale and golden, catching on the edge of the dresser and the folds of the quilt tossed halfway off the bed. The room smelled like cedar and lavender and a little like sleep. Warm, slow, peaceful.

Agatha was curled around her, one arm draped over Rio’s waist, her breath soft against Rio’s hair. She hadn’t moved much, just shifted slightly when Rio stirred, and now she was watching her with those sharp, beautiful eyes that somehow always looked softer first thing in the morning.

Rio blinked up at her. “You’re staring.”

Agatha smiled. “I like the view.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but her mouth tugged into a smile anyway. She tucked herself in closer, nuzzling her face against Agatha’s neck. “So unfair. It’s too early to be charming.”

“And yet here I am,” Agatha murmured, brushing her fingers lightly over Rio’s cheek. “Thirty-five looks good on you.”

Rio chuckled. “Ugh, it was supposed to be just a regular day.”
