Agatha huffed a breath of amusement. “Your best friend flew across the country to surprise you. Kind of hard to miss.”

“Alice,” Rio groaned into Agatha’s skin. “You know, I should’ve known she’d pull something like this.”

“She’s wonderful,” Agatha said, her voice gentler now. “But right now I only want to think about you.”

That made something flutter in Rio’s chest—something warm and careful and maybe just a little terrifying. She didn’t answer right away. Just let herself breathe, pressed against the warmth of Agatha’s skin, her heartbeat a steady thrum beneath her ear.

“I never liked birthdays,” she admitted after a moment. “They always felt… weird. Like I was supposed to feel happy. Grateful. Special. But mostly I just felt like a mistake someone got rid of”

Agatha didn’t say anything, just ran a soothing hand down her spine.

“I didn’t even tell Alice for the first couple of years,” Rio added. “She only figured it out when she saw my ID.”

Agatha leaned in and kissed her forehead. “Then let’s not celebrate it the way other people do. Let’s make it yours. Just yours.”

Rio looked up at her, heart thudding quietly in her chest. “You really are amazing, you know that?”

Agatha smirked. “I’ve heard.”

Rio laughed—really laughed, the sound bubbling up and catching even her by surprise. She leaned up and kissed Agatha, soft and slow, like a thank you she didn’t know how to say. Agatha kissed her back just as gently, one hand cradling her jaw, thumb brushing the corner of her mouth.

There wasn’t heat in the kiss, not this time. Not urgency. Just something quiet and whole and a little bit dizzying. Something that said: I see you. And I’m not going anywhere.

They didn’t say anything after that. There was no need. Everything that mattered was there between them—in the brush of fingers, in the warmth of shared breath, in the way Agatha looked at her like she was something precious.

Rio didn’t say it out loud, but she felt it.

She was in love with her.

And maybe that was the real gift today.

~*~

They finally peeled themselves out of bed for a shower—though “quick” might’ve been generous. Between Agatha’s wandering hands and Rio’s inability to stop smiling whenever their eyes met, it took way longer than it should have. But eventually they made it downstairs, hair still damp, hands brushing occasionally as they walked side by side into the kitchen.

And there, like some strange and wonderful domestic dream, stood Alice wearing an oversized flannel shirt, flipping pancakes like she owned the place.

“Morning, birthday girl!” Alice said, bright and smug, not even looking up as she flipped one with casual expertise. “Sit. I’m making your favorites.”

Rio blinked. “You’re making pancakes?”

Alice turned and raised a brow. “Excuse me, I’m making the pancakes. Plus scrambled eggs, that weird breakfast hash you like, and I may have found an unopened jar of Nutella in your cabinet and I’m not above using it.”

Agatha gave Rio a sidelong look, her mouth twitching. “She’s very efficient.”

“You have no idea,” Rio muttered, heart full and aching all at once.

Alice finally looked over at them properly, her eyes softening for just a second. “Happy birthday, Rio.”

Rio walked over and wrapped her in a tight hug. “You’re a menace, you know that?”

“Yeah, yeah,” Alice said, hugging her back. “You’re welcome.”

Agatha hovered in the doorway for a beat longer, watching them. Then she quietly crossed over to the coffee pot, giving them the moment. When Rio glanced back, she caught Agatha smiling into her mug, her eyes warm, her posture relaxed.

This felt… real.

Homey. Safe. Hers.

And maybe—just maybe—for the first time in her life, Rio didn’t want to run from her birthday.

She wanted to stay.

~*~

After a breakfast filled with teasing and college stories from Alice that made Rio want to curl up and die of embarrassment, her best friend finally stood and stretched. 

“Okay. I’m gonna go take a quick shower so I can be cute for this charming small-town festival thing you people do.”

“You’re adorable already,” Rio called after her, grinning.

Once Alice disappeared up the stairs, silence settled in. A warm, golden sort of quiet. Agatha slid her chair closer and tucked a piece of hair behind Rio’s ear.

“Happy birthday, darling,” she murmured, her gaze full of something that made Rio’s breath catch. “You look radiant today.”

Rio felt heat rise to her cheeks. “Stop.”

“I haven’t even started.”

Agatha leaned in then, slow and deliberate, her lips brushing over Rio’s in a kiss that started soft—just a press of mouths, a breath shared—but deepened as Rio leaned into it. Her fingers curled into the loose fabric of Agatha’s shirt, pulling her closer.

Every touch from Agatha felt like sunlight. Like something blooming just beneath Rio’s skin. And as their mouths moved together, slow and lazy and unhurried, she felt it—the soft buzz of something waking up.

When she opened her eyes, the tiny pot of herbs on the windowsill had burst into bloom. Petals unfurling, buds yawning open like they, too, were leaning into the joy swelling in her chest.

Agatha followed her gaze and let out a quiet, delighted laugh. “You’re doing it again.”

“I know,” Rio whispered, a little breathless, forehead resting against Agatha’s. “I can’t help it. I’m just… happy.”

Agatha kissed her again, slower this time, as if sealing something unspoken between them. Not quite I love you, but something close. Something just as deep.

Agatha kissed her again—deeper this time, more lingering. Rio tilted her head, chasing the warmth of it, her hands sliding up to cradle Agatha’s jaw. She felt the magic bloom beneath her skin like heat rising from a sun-warmed stone, spilling out of her in quiet waves. There was no pulling it back.

On the kitchen table, a few more flowers blossomed—wild and bright and entirely out of season. A tiny golden daisy peeked up beside the salt shaker, a pale violet unfurling just next to the butter dish. Agatha pulled back slightly, eyes sparkling as she reached for one.

“Well, would you look at that,” she murmured, twirling the delicate stem between her fingers before holding it out toward Rio with an exaggerated flourish. “Happy birthday, my lady.”

Rio couldn’t help herself—she kissed her again, giddy and smiling against Agatha’s mouth, laughing into the press of it. Her arms wrapped around Agatha’s waist, pulling her closer until they were both flush against the table, and the only thing Rio could think about was how damn good it felt to be wanted like this. To be known and still adored.

That was precisely the moment Alice walked into the kitchen again, towel around her neck, eyebrows raised—and then immediately dropped her hand over her eyes.

“I literally just left the room not even five minutes ago,” she said, voice dry. “I haven’t even showered yet and you’re already making out in front of the condiments.”

Agatha chuckled softly and stepped back, brushing a piece of hair from Rio’s face. Rio turned toward her best friend, cheeks flushed and grinning.

Alice peeked through her fingers. “Is it safe?”

“No,” Rio said brightly, reaching for her coffee. “But come in anyway. You’re the one who invaded my cottage.”

“Rude,” Alice muttered, flopping into a chair. “Next time I surprise you for your birthday, I expect less tongue and more balloons.”

“You’re getting pancakes,” Rio said. “That’s festive enough.”

Alice sighed like a martyr and picked up her fork. “I made the pancakes, don’t you forget it.”

Agatha caught Rio’s gaze from across the table and smiled again—soft and knowing and utterly spellbound. Rio felt that smile in her chest, like the sunlight was blooming there too.

And for the first time in a long time, she didn’t feel like she was missing anything.

~*~

After breakfast, the cottage slowly hummed to life with that soft, golden kind of excitement that only came with special days—warm clothes being pulled from closets, coffee mugs refilled, a soft playlist Rio had thrown on from her phone drifting through the speakers.

Upstairs, Rio stood in her room, holding up two different sweaters like the fate of the day depended on it. Agatha leaned against the doorway, arms folded, watching her with a quiet fondness that made Rio’s chest ache in the best way.

“You look beautiful in both,” Agatha said, voice low, her smile curved and slow. “But the dark green one brings out the mischief in your eyes.”

Rio rolled her eyes but grinned. “You’re ridiculous.”

“And you’re blushing.” Agatha crossed the room and pressed a kiss to Rio’s cheek, then one to the corner of her mouth. “I need to run back to my place real quick, grab a change of clothes and feed Scratchy. I’ll meet you at The Hollow in an hour?”

Rio nodded, her smile lingering. “Sounds good. Alice’ll want to poke around town a bit anyway.”

Agatha paused by the door, fingers trailing along the frame. Then she turned back, her expression softening.

“Before you go…” she said. “You should take a moment to write that dream down in the grimoire. The one you had this morning.”

Rio tilted her head slightly. “You think it’s important?”

“I do,” Agatha said gently. “The way you described it… how real it felt? That’s not something to ignore. Dreams like that—when magic brushes up against memory—it’s how the truth starts to unravel. You’ll want a record of it.”

Rio glanced toward her nightstand where the grimoire rested, quiet and waiting.

“I will,” she said. “Promise.”

Agatha stepped back into the room and kissed her one more time—slow, deliberate, thumb brushing the corner of Rio’s mouth.

“Happy birthday,” she whispered. “Again.”

Then she was gone in a rustle of coat and perfume and that little smile she always left behind, like a bookmark in Rio’s soul.

~*~

Rio stood by her bedroom window for a long moment after Agatha left, watching the trees sway in the cold breeze. The sunlight broke through the thinning clouds and lit the cottage’s old wooden floor in gold. Her hand brushed absently over the spot on her cheek where Agatha had kissed her. She smiled to herself.

Then she turned and walked over to her nightstand.

The grimoire felt heavy in her hands—more than just its leather-bound weight. It felt like legacy. Like truth. She opened it to the next blank page, the scent of old paper and dried herbs rising up to meet her.

Sitting cross-legged on her bed, Rio took a breath, then picked up her pen.

December 6th. Early morning.

Another dream—or maybe a memory. It felt… real. More than real. A birthday party. The kind I never had as a kid. There was warmth, laughter, cake with honey-sweet frosting, and people who looked at me like they loved me. There was music, too—strings and humming and a voice I couldn’t quite place singing my name like it was something sacred.

I woke up happy. I felt safe. I can still hear the breeze through the trees, the sound of someone laughing from across the table. I don’t know what it means. But I know I want to remember it.

She stared at the ink for a moment before adding, in smaller letters:

Thank you, whoever you were.

Closing the book, she pressed her hand to its cover and let it rest there for a few beats before getting up to finish getting ready.

~*~

The bell above The Hollow’s front door jingled as Rio and Alice stepped inside, and Rio instantly breathed in the warm, spicy air—cinnamon, cloves, and something a little harder to name. Comfort, maybe. Magic disguised as memory.

Agatha was already there, seated near the window with Wanda, a half-finished mug of tea between her hands. The moment Rio spotted her, something inside her clicked into place, like her day had just officially begun. Agatha looked up, smiled, and Rio felt her stomach flutter—ridiculous, considering how much time they’d been spending together lately, how thoroughly Agatha had wormed her way into her every thought.

“There they are,” Agatha said, rising as they crossed the room.

Rio didn’t hesitate. She leaned in and kissed her—quick but warm, the kind of kiss that said I missed you, even though it had only been an hour or two. Agatha’s hand found hers under the table as they both sat, their fingers lacing together naturally.

“I’m just saying,” Alice announced, tugging off her coat, “this place smells like magic and baked goods had a love child.”

Rio caught Agatha watching her, that same quiet, tender intensity that always made her feel like she was glowing from the inside out. The memory of that kitchen kiss earlier—the flower blooming in Agatha’s fingers, the way she’d said happy birthday, my lady—played on repeat behind her eyes.

“You okay?” Agatha whispered, close enough that Rio felt the brush of her breath.

Rio nodded. “I’m more than okay.”

She wasn’t lying. Her heart was still humming from the way the morning had unfolded—waking up wrapped in Agatha’s arms, the warm bubble of domestic bliss with Alice clanging around the kitchen, and the overwhelming contentment that had settled into her bones like sunlight.

“Good,” Agatha murmured, brushing her thumb along the back of Rio’s hand.

“You two are nauseating,” Alice said, biting into a scone. “Like, I get it now, but still.”

Rio laughed and squeezed Agatha’s hand. “I‘ll take that as a compliment.”

Outside, the square was starting to buzz. She could see pops of color through the window—festival booths going up, a kid dragging a red balloon, strings of lights being strung from lamppost to lamppost. The town felt alive in a way she hadn’t fully appreciated until now.

“So,” Wanda said, resting her chin on her palm with a knowing smirk, “thirty-five. How’s it feel?”

Rio groaned and let her head drop dramatically onto Agatha’s shoulder. “It feels like betrayal. I told you all that in confidence.”

Agatha kissed her temple and murmured, “You wear it well.”

“You’re all so annoying,” Rio mumbled, but she was smiling as she said it.

And when Agatha tilted her head just enough to meet her gaze, Rio couldn’t help it—she leaned in for another kiss. A soft one. Meaningful. The kind that carried unspoken things.

Things they weren’t saying yet.

Things they were both starting to feel.

~*~

Rio was halfway through a buttery scone and trying to decide if she had room for another when the front door burst open with a jingle and a dramatic gust of cold air. A streak of black eyeliner, oversized boots, and chaotic energy came bounding in.

“Is she here?” Billy’s voice rang through the café. “Tell me she’s here.”

Lilia peered out from behind the counter with a raised brow. “You’re blowing in like a storm, child.”

“I am a storm,” Billy replied dramatically, and then his eyes landed on Rio. “There she is!”

He bounded across the room and flung himself into a hug so fast, Rio had barely set her tea down before he wrapped his arms around her.

“Oh—hi?” she managed, startled but smiling. “Wow, okay, we’re hugging. This is happening.”

“I’m sorry, but it’s not every day your actual favorite graphic novelist moves into town and turns out to be besties with your godmother and maybe-sort-of-dating her too,” Billy said, pulling back with a grin. “Happy birthday, Rio Vidal. I brought you a present.”

Rio blinked. “You—what?”

Billy reached into his coat and pulled out a little box, tied with twine. “I made it myself. No pressure, but if you don’t like it, I’ll die.”

Agatha let out a quiet laugh, sipping her tea like this was just another regular afternoon.

Rio took the box and opened it slowly, revealing a tiny, hand-carved wood charm in the shape of a pen—no, wait, a fountain pen with vines curling around it. There were little inky details etched into the handle. It was delicate and full of character, the kind of thing that looked like it belonged in a story.

“This is… Billy, this is amazing,” she said, genuinely touched. “Thank you.”

Billy beamed. “It’s enchanted to keep your creativity flowing.”

Alice, who had just taken a sip of her tea, immediately choked.

Wanda coughed into her mug. Agatha gently elbowed Billy, who blinked like a deer in headlights.

“I—uh. I mean, not actually enchanted,” Billy said quickly, shooting Alice a glance. “Obviously. That would be weird. Haha. Magic’s not real. Who said that? Ha.”

Alice narrowed her eyes, suspicious. “Did… did you just say it’s enchanted?”

“No. Definitely didn’t,” Billy said too fast.

Rio snorted into her tea. Agatha was biting her lip, and even Wanda was trying very hard not to smile.

Alice pointed a finger at Rio. “I swear, if you all turn out to be in some weird cottagecore cult—”

“Oh, we are,” Wanda said sweetly. “We even have themed scones.”

Rio was laughing so hard she had to wipe a tear from her eye. Agatha looked over at her with that familiar fondness, and Rio felt a warm rush bloom inside her. Not the kind of magic she still didn’t fully understand—but something just as powerful. Joy. Belonging. Love, even if they hadn’t said it yet.

Billy flopped dramatically into a chair beside them. “I’m staying for scones.”

Lilia slid another plate onto the table with a wink. “You always are, dear.”

And just like that, Rio let herself lean back into Agatha’s side, sipping her tea and letting the laughter buzz around her like electricity. For the first time in a long time, her birthday didn’t feel like something she had to survive.

It felt like magic. The kind she could believe in.

~*~

The Thistle Grove town festival was already in full swing by the time Rio, Agatha, Wanda, and Alice made their way to the town square.

String lights crisscrossed overhead like constellations in the twilight sky, and the air smelled like cinnamon, roasting nuts, and woodsmoke. Children darted past with caramel apples and glittering fairy wings, a live band played near the gazebo, and vendors lined the street offering everything from wool scarves to homemade cider.

“Okay, this place is straight out of a Hallmark movie,” Alice said, wide-eyed as she took in the scene. “I half-expect a sleigh to roll up and someone to spontaneously propose.”

“That usually happens closer to Christmas,” Agatha quipped from beside her, the ghost of a smirk on her lips.

Rio chuckled and looped her arm through Alice’s. “Come on, let me show you the best cider stand. Lilia says the guy who runs it talks to his apples before he picks them, and honestly? It shows.”

As the two of them wandered, Rio pointed out all her favorite shops—The Hollow, of course, and the tiny antique bookstore tucked next to the flower shop where she once spotted a black cat curled up on a stack of poetry volumes. Alice listened intently, throwing in her usual sarcasm and playful jabs, but Rio could tell she was charmed.

She glanced over her shoulder now and then, catching glimpses of Agatha and Wanda a little ways behind them, deep in quiet conversation as they moved through the crowd. Agatha’s coat was dark against the golden lights, her face still, eyes sharp and scanning. Rio’s heart pulled a little tighter at the sight.

It was comforting, somehow—knowing Agatha was always watching.

They were passing a row of booths when Rio felt it—a strange hum beneath her skin. Not quite danger. Not quite anything, really. Just a flicker. Her steps slowed.

Alice noticed. “You okay?”

“Yeah,” Rio said quickly, brushing it off. “Just… the cobblestones are uneven.”

But the feeling didn’t leave. She glanced back again—and saw Agatha now with Wanda’s hand lightly on her arm, both of them still, looking across the square.

Rio followed their gaze.

There, near the corner where two side streets met, a man in a slate-gray coat stood facing a vendor cart. Nothing about him was particularly memorable, but Wanda’s expression had sharpened and Agatha’s eyes had narrowed ever so slightly.

“Who’s that?” Rio murmured when Agatha finally reached her side again.

Agatha shook her head once. “Don’t know yet.”

“Nothing to panic about,” Wanda added lightly as she joined them, offering a small smile that didn’t quite reach her eyes. “Just… something to file away. He passed by earlier and I got a weird magic vibe from him.”

Rio felt that same flicker of unease again, just stronger now. She glanced at Alice, who was sipping cider and totally unaware. That protective instinct roared up in her like a sudden wave.

But Agatha was already there beside her, voice soft and low, meant only for Rio’s ears. “We’ll keep an eye out. Nothing happens to you on my watch. Okay?”

Rio met her eyes, the warmth of that promise anchoring her in place. “Okay.”

And just like that, the moment passed. The band picked up a new song, and a few townsfolk started dancing near the square. Alice nudged Rio’s side.

“Alright, this cider is life-changing,” she declared. “Now show me where the pies are.”

Rio laughed again, the tension easing slightly, and as they moved toward the bakery stand, Agatha’s hand brushed against hers. She didn’t say anything—but she didn’t have to.

There was something unspoken humming between them. Not just magic.

Trust.

~*~

The rest of the afternoon passed in a blur of music, laughter, and the scent of freshly baked everything. Rio couldn’t remember the last time she’d felt this… full. Not in the overeating sense, though Alice had insisted on trying a bite of every pastry Thistle Grove had to offer. But full in the quiet, soul-deep way. Like maybe this strange little town had carved out a space just for her.

Alice was currently winning an arm-wrestling contest with an unsuspecting teenager at the apple-pressing booth—cheered on by a small crowd. Rio leaned against a wooden post by the cider stand, sipping a warm cup of the spiced stuff, when she felt Agatha step in close behind her.

“She’s thriving,” Agatha murmured, nodding toward Alice as the teen groaned in defeat and dramatically collapsed onto the table.

Rio grinned. “She’s in her element. Chaos and carbs.”

Agatha hummed in agreement and reached around Rio’s waist to steal a sip of her cider. Her other hand brushed against Rio’s back, grounding and gentle.

For a while, they stood in companionable silence, watching children dart between booths, old friends embrace, and the town square glow with a kind of joy that felt rare and untouched. Every so often, Rio could feel Agatha’s gaze flick to that same corner of the square where the gray-coated man had stood. But he hadn’t returned. And Rio found herself relaxing, if only a little.

“Thank you,” she said quietly, turning just enough to see Agatha’s profile. “For… everything.”

Agatha looked down at her. “I haven’t done that much.”

“You showed up,” Rio said simply. “And you stayed.”

That earned her a look. Soft. Meaningful. And not a little devastating.

“You deserve people who stay, Rio.”

Her throat caught. Before she could say something dumb or start crying right next to the fudge booth, Agatha leaned in and kissed her temple.

“You ready to head back soon?” Agatha murmured against her skin. 

Rio nodded. “Yeah. I think I’m done peopling for the day.”

Alice joined them not long after, still high on festival energy and clutching a bag of caramel popcorn. “Okay, I’m officially obsessed with this town. Let’s move here. Let’s start a commune. I’ll bring the sarcasm.”

“You already do,” Rio teased, slinging an arm around her.

They strolled home slowly, the streets of Thistle Grove gradually quieting as the festival wound down. Lanterns still glowed in shop windows, and couples walked hand in hand, bundled against the chill. It was the kind of evening that begged for something more—something tender and slow and lit only by firelight.

Back at the cottage, Alice collapsed onto the couch with a dramatic groan and promptly fell asleep halfway through a monologue about fudge.

Rio tucked a blanket over her, heart squeezing just a little.

She found Agatha in the kitchen, standing at the window with a mug in her hands, watching the stars begin to flicker to life above the treetops. The moonlight silvered the edges of her hair.

Rio stepped up behind her and wrapped her arms around her waist, pressing her cheek between her shoulder blades.

They didn’t speak. They didn’t need to.

And in that quiet moment, safe and warm and tucked into something that felt like love even if they hadn’t said the word, Rio knew:

This birthday was everything she never thought she’d have—and everything she was still afraid to hope for.

~*~

Sunday dawned silver and quiet, the kind of Maine morning where the fog drifted in like a dream and lingered well into breakfast. Rio stretched in bed, sore in all the best ways, then slipped into her robe and followed the scent of coffee down the stairs.

In the kitchen, Alice was already awake, flipping through one of Rio’s sketchbooks at the table, while Agatha stood at the stove, barefoot, hair tied back in a low bun as she stirred something in a cast-iron skillet.

“Good morning, sleepyhead,” Alice called. “Your kitchen goddess made pancakes. And also—I want to steal this page,” she added, waving a sketch of an eerie, flower-filled forest. “It’s gorgeous. New story?”

“Sort of,” Rio mumbled, pressing a kiss to Agatha’s cheek before sliding into the seat beside Alice.

Agatha glanced over her shoulder with a small, knowing smile. “We’re calling it a slow burn.”

They ate breakfast in easy conversation. Laughter slipped in naturally. Alice teased Rio. Rio teased back. Salem hopped up on the windowsill to soak in what little sun there was, casting the occasional judgmental glance toward Alice but otherwise behaving himself.

And then it happened.

Alice stood to grab more syrup and accidentally knocked over Rio’s mug. Hot coffee sloshed across the table—straight toward one of Rio’s sketchbooks.

“No—!” Rio shouted, instinct kicking in hard. She flung out her hand, and—

The coffee stopped.

Frozen mid-spill, droplets hanging suspended in the air like tiny amber orbs, not a single page touched.

Alice stood there, still holding the syrup, eyes wide and unblinking. “What. The. Fuck.”

Agatha swore under her breath.

Rio’s heart thundered in her chest. She hadn’t meant to do it—it had just happened, instinctive and sharp and completely visible. Even Salem turned his head slowly toward her, as if to say nice going.

Alice dropped the syrup.

“You just did… something. That wasn’t gravity. Or reflexes. That was—what the hell was that, Rio?!”

Rio looked at Agatha. Agatha gave a tiny nod. No more hiding.

“Okay,” Rio said softly, her voice unsteady but calm. “I can explain. But… you might want to sit down.”

Alice sat down slowly, as if afraid the chair might disappear beneath her. “You’re going to explain? Please do. Because my best friend just froze coffee midair like we’re in The Matrix, and I haven’t even finished my caffeine yet.”

Rio winced, then looked down at her hands. The coffee had settled neatly back into the mug without a splash, like it had never moved at all.

“Okay. So,” she started, then stopped. “You know, the cottage? The inheritance? The random letter from some lawyer’s office in the middle of nowhere?”

Alice nodded. “Yeah, and I remember telling you it was weird as fuck.”

“Right. Well, turns out it wasn’t random. Or fake. This cottage really did belong to my biological family. And…they were… witches. Like, real witches. And so am I, apparently.”

Alice blinked. “I’m sorry. What?”

Rio shrugged helplessly. “Yeah. That’s what I said too. At first, I thought I was losing my mind. Things started happening—lights flickering, plants growing faster than they should, dreams that felt like memories. Then I met Agatha—”

“Hi,” Agatha said, mildly, raising a hand from the kitchen.

Alice stared at her. “You’re a witch too?”

“Mm-hmm.”

“And you’ve both been doing actual magic this whole time?”

“Well,” Rio said, “not… a whole lot of it.”

“Except for the part where you just stopped time with a flick of your wrist!”

“That’s new,” Rio said quickly. “I didn’t even know I could do that. I wasn’t trying to do anything! I was just—protecting my sketchbook.”

Agatha crossed the room then, laying a hand gently on Rio’s back. “It’s your instincts. Your magic is growing—and fast. It’s responding to emotion, to need, maybe even to your environment.”

Alice gave a breathless laugh, somewhere between awe and disbelief. “You’re serious. This isn’t a prank. This is real?”

“I wouldn’t prank you with witchcraft,” Rio said, smiling faintly.

“Okay, I mean… fair.”

There was a long pause. Then Alice exhaled hard, rubbing her forehead. “So, what now? Do you like… have a wand? Are you going to Hogwarts next?”

Rio grinned. “I have a familiar and a cottage. That’s close enough, right?”

Agatha chuckled softly. “You have more than that. You have a coven. Even if you don’t know it yet.”

Alice looked between them, her expression slowly shifting from disbelief to something like wonder. “Holy shit. My best friend is a witch.”

Rio looked up at her. “Still want to stick around for a while?”

Alice gave her a lopsided smile. “Are you kidding? I want front row seats.”

Alice leaned forward, eyes gleaming. “Okay. Spill. Start from the top, and no skipping the juicy parts. Like, how exactly are you a witch? What can you even do?”

Rio rubbed the back of her neck, a wry smile tugging at her lips. “Honestly? I’m still figuring it out. But it’s… mostly tied to how I feel.”

Alice raised an eyebrow. “Meaning?”

“Meaning,” Rio said, gesturing vaguely, “if I’m happy, flowers bloom out of nowhere. I’m not kidding. Like—actual flowers. The kitchen table’s seen some things.”

Alice stared. “Wait, the bouquet I saw yesterday morning—”

“Yeah. That just sort of… happened.” Rio’s cheeks flushed. “Agatha says it’s part of my affinity. I make things grow. I can transform stuff too, but it’s still hard to control.”

“Transform stuff how?” Alice asked, eyes wide.

Rio hesitated, then laughed softly. “I turned my couch into a pullout bed. Agatha kind of… encouraged me to try it last night when you went to the bathroom.”

“You what?” Alice’s jaw dropped, then she looked toward the living room like she could see the magic lingering. “Okay, that’s actually super cool. But like—what happens if you’re upset?”

Rio’s expression shifted, more serious now. “It’s… not great. The night I found out about this whole thing, I caused a pretty bad thunderstorm.”

Alice blinked. “You made a storm?”

Rio shrugged helplessly. “Agatha thinks my emotions are a conduit. I’m learning to channel it, but it’s… intense.”

Alice leaned back, shaking her head. “Holy crap, Rio. You’re like a walking weather system with a garden subscription.”

That got a laugh out of Rio. “Not exactly what I was going for, but sure.”

Alice’s smile softened. “Okay, real talk—how are you doing with all this? Really?”

Rio looked down at her hands, then back up at her friend. “Scared. Excited. Overwhelmed. But also… like I’m finally part of something. Like there’s this part of me that’s always been there, waiting.”

Alice reached over and squeezed her hand. “I’m proud of you. Seriously. Magic or not, you’re still the same weird, brilliant nerd I’ve always loved.”

Rio smiled, heart full. “Thanks, Al.”

~*~

 

 

Chapter 16: Sixteen

Agatha hadn’t stopped watching Alice since the moment Rio finished telling her everything. She sat perched on the arm of the couch, her tea cooling in her hands, though she hadn’t taken a sip in minutes. Salem lay stretched across the floor, looking perfectly unbothered by the seismic shift that had just taken place in the living room.

Alice had been quiet, but not the stunned, spiraling kind of quiet Agatha feared. No, she was observing—absorbing. Her brows furrowed and unfurrowed. Her fingers curled lightly against the rim of her mug. Her eyes flicked between the two women in front of her with an intensity Agatha recognized. She was drawing conclusions.

“You okay?” Rio asked, her voice soft, tentative.

Alice blinked. “Yeah, yeah. I mean, I think so. It’s a lot. But I’m not freaked out or anything.”

Agatha exchanged a quick glance with Rio, who looked visibly relieved. She let her hand rest gently on Rio’s back, grounding her. The last thing Rio needed today was to feel like her truth had driven someone away.

Alice leaned forward, placing her mug on the coffee table with a gentle clink. “So. That Mara Greaves thing.”

The name alone sent a prickle down Agatha’s spine.

Rio didn’t say anything. Her fingers tightened slightly in the blanket she still had draped around her.

Alice’s gaze stayed steady. “Was that about magic too?”

Agatha took in a slow breath. No use dodging it now. “Yes,” she said quietly. “She’s not just a folklorist. And she’s not just passing through.”

“She’s dangerous?” Alice asked, her voice more analytical than fearful.

“In a way that we don’t fully understand yet,” Agatha replied, her tone edged with caution. “But yes. There’s power in her. Old, cloaked power. She’s not just here to admire the scenery.”

Alice nodded, sitting back slowly. “And you’ve known this since you first asked me to look into her?”

Agatha hesitated. “We suspected it. The name she’s using… it’s not her only one. What you told Rio, that she uses the name Dahlia really helped. We found records of her that go back decades, and she looks exactly the same. Which isn’t exactly normal.”

A moment of silence passed between them. Alice tapped her fingers against her knee, then let out a small breath. “So what are we doing about her?”

Agatha couldn’t help but smile slightly. “You’re taking this remarkably well.”

Alice gave her a sidelong glance. “I read a lot of fantasy. Also, I’m your girlfriend’s best friend. Or whatever you guys are to each other. That means I’m in it. No way I’m sitting on the sidelines now.”

Rio leaned her head against Agatha’s shoulder, and Agatha wrapped an arm around her waist. She didn’t speak right away. The weight of responsibility was pressing hard against her ribs, but there was something stabilizing about the way Alice met her gaze—steady, unwavering.

“Right now,” Agatha said carefully, “we’re just keeping watch. Strengthening wards. Making sure Rio has what she needs to stay safe and grounded. But if it escalates—”

“We’ll handle it,” Alice finished.

Agatha gave her a nod of quiet approval. “Yes.”

Another moment of silence, warm this time. And then Alice, ever the breaker of tension, arched her brows and asked with mock seriousness, “So I’m betting that when you guys first kissed, flowers just exploded out of Rio?”

Agatha nodded, amused.

“Was that a magical reaction or are you two just that gay?”

Rio groaned and covered her face with her hands. Agatha let out an honest laugh.

“Little bit of both,” she said, smirking. “But mostly her.”

~*~

The afternoon sun filtered lazily through the kitchen windows, catching the brown strands in Rio’s hair as she leaned against the counter. Agatha watched her from across the room, where she was finishing the last of the ward adjustments along the back door.

“I don’t need a bodyguard, you know,” Rio said lightly, one brow raised.

Agatha didn’t smile. “That’s not what this is.”

Rio tilted her head. “Then what is it?”

Agatha crossed the kitchen slowly, wiping her hands on the dish towel and letting herself study her—calm, curious, stubborn. “You’re powerful, Rio. And you’re growing stronger by the day. We’ve seen it. So have others.”

Rio’s smile faded a little.

Agatha stepped in front of her and reached out, brushing a bit of flour from her sleeve—leftover from Alice’s enthusiastic pancake experiment. “Which means it’s time we start focusing on more than just blooming flowers and pretty transformations. You need to know how to protect yourself.”

Rio frowned. “You think something’s coming?”

“I think,” Agatha said carefully, “that something always is. Especially when you carry a Thread’s magic. Especially when you don’t know your full strength yet.”

Rio took a breath, a little shaky. “Okay. So… what does that mean? Like, magical kung-fu training?”

Agatha gave a small huff of laughter. “More like reflex work, shielding spells, energy redirection. Defense doesn’t necessarily mean aggression. It just means preparation.”

Rio leaned back a little, gaze skimming the floor. “I’ve never even been in a fight. Unless you count that time in high school where I spilled hot coffee on someone’s foot and they threw a muffin at me.”

“I don’t.” Agatha’s smile was brief. “Which is why we’ll start with the basics. And I’ll ask Wanda to join us. She’s excellent with defensive magic.”

Rio blinked. “Wanda?”

“She’s already volunteered, actually,” Agatha said with a shrug, grabbing her mug. “She says your wild thread power is super exciting and she’s dying to see how it reacts under stress.”

Rio groaned. “That sounds deeply ominous.”

“That’s because it is.”

When Rio glanced up at her with wide eyes, Agatha gave her a sly, teasing grin. “Kidding. Mostly.”

Rio exhaled slowly, chewing her bottom lip. “Okay. Yeah. I guess if I’m going to be a magic person now, I should know how to not accidentally blow myself up.”

Agatha stepped closer again, her voice softer now. “It’s not just about you. It’s about the people you love. And what you’d do to keep them safe.”

Something shifted in Rio’s expression then—less fear, more focus. Her eyes flicked toward the stairs, where Alice had disappeared earlier to journal or nap or both. Then back to Agatha.

“Alright,” she said quietly. “Let’s train.”

Agatha nodded, feeling something sharp and proud settle beneath her ribs. “Good.”

 

~*~

 

The clearing behind Wanda’s house was protected on all sides by a dense barrier of pines and enchanted bramble, quiet enough that even the wind respected its boundaries. It was one of the few places Agatha felt they could truly open up—no tourists, no nosy neighbors, and with all the wards in place, no chance of being spied on. 

Rio stood in the grass, brow furrowed in concentration as she tried for the third time to create a steady shield with her magic. Her palms were outstretched, fingers shaking slightly from effort, and the glowing shimmer of power that had flickered into existence around her arms was already starting to pulse like a heartbeat.

“She’s overextending,” Wanda murmured from beside Agatha. “Not grounding enough.”

Agatha nodded. “She’s trying to brute-force it.”

“I can hear both of you,” Rio called without looking back, the frustration clear in her voice.

“Yes, darling, that’s the point,” Agatha replied, smiling softly. “Now relax. You’re not trying to hold up a wall—you’re asking the magic to protect you. Let it respond to your intent.”

“Like it’s listening?” Rio asked, glancing over her shoulder.

Wanda hummed. “Magic is listening. That’s half the point.”

From the sidelines, Alice was sipping a thermos of tea, sitting cross-legged on a picnic blanket that Wanda had charmed to stay warm. She was absolutely enthralled.

“God, this is like Practical Magic meets X-Men,” Alice muttered. “Is this your danger room, or…?”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “Only if you count poison ivy and judgment as training hazards.”

Alice grinned and gave her a little salute with the thermos.

Agatha stepped forward. “All right. Let’s try a defensive exercise. Freeze time again.”

Rio blinked. “You mean… on purpose?”

“You did it once on instinct. But instinct isn’t the same as control. And if you want to really protect yourself, Rio, we need to train both.”

Rio swallowed, then nodded. “Okay. How do I start?”

“Wanda and I will throw spells,” Agatha said calmly. “Nothing harmful, just fast. Your goal is to feel them coming and freeze them the moment before they hit.”

Alice sat up straighter, eyes wide. “Wait. You’re actually attacking her?”

“Light spells,” Wanda said mildly. “Barely a sting. Think of it like magical dodgeball.”

“Magical traumaball,” Alice muttered.

Agatha took position across from Rio, watching her closely. “Close your eyes. Breathe. Don’t chase the power. Call it to you. Let it wrap around you like mist.”

Rio did as instructed. Her breathing slowed. The air around her seemed to thrum—alive, alert.

Agatha and Wanda exchanged a look. Wanda raised a hand first, murmuring a spell under her breath. A flicker of violet light pulsed toward Rio, and just as it neared her—

Everything stopped.

The sound of wind froze. The crackle of magic midair halted, suspended like glitter in honey. Agatha stood with her arm still lifted, but the world around her shimmered in pale gold.

Rio opened her eyes slowly in the middle of that stillness, face lit with something close to awe.

“Oh,” she whispered. “I did it.”

The moment cracked open like glass as time surged forward again. Wanda’s spell fizzled harmlessly into the grass. Alice gasped. Agatha grinned.

“You’re incredible,” she said, stepping forward. “You didn’t just react—you commanded it.”

Rio’s shoulders dropped with a mix of pride and relief. “It felt easier. Not easy, but… like it knew what I needed.”

Wanda gave a pleased nod. “That’s the Thread in you. She’s waking up fast.”

Alice clapped enthusiastically from the blanket. “Okay, but can we acknowledge that my best friend just Matrix’d magic? I mean, if she learns to freeze time and do a backflip, I’m gonna combust.”

Agatha laughed despite herself. “One step at a time.”

She caught Rio’s gaze then—soft, shining, full of surprise and wonder and maybe something deeper that Agatha didn’t dare name just yet. Not today.

But she felt it. And that was enough.

“Again?” Rio asked, already bracing.

“Again,” Agatha said, pride swelling in her chest. “Let’s push it further.”

~*~

 

The next exercise was meant to be simple.

A conjured obstacle, a push of defensive magic, a focused burst of Rio’s will—just enough to challenge her, not to harm. But power was a wild thing in someone so new to it, and Rio, stubborn and eager as ever, didn’t know how to slow down when she got excited.

Agatha saw it in the flick of Rio’s fingers, in the way her brow creased, in the sudden gust of energy that rippled outward far too fast.

“Wait—” she started.

Too late.

The spell backfired in a bright, crackling burst—like a whip of light snapping back on Rio’s arm. She stumbled with a sharp cry and dropped to her knees in the grass, clutching her shoulder. Wanda was already moving, but Agatha was faster.

“Rio,” she breathed, kneeling beside her. “Let me see.”

“I’m fine,” Rio gritted, even as her fingers trembled.

Alice was halfway to them already, horror all over her face. “What the hell just happened?! She got zapped by her own power? What was that?”

Agatha didn’t answer. She gently took Rio’s arm, rolling back the sleeve of her flannel to reveal the skin beneath—angry, red, already beginning to welt from magical blowback.

Too much power, not enough control.

Rio hissed through her teeth. “Okay. Maybe not fine.”

Agatha exhaled slowly, centering herself. “You’re alright. I’ve got you.”

She curled her hand around Rio’s forearm, her fingers firm but careful. The world narrowed—sound quieting, light dimming, until all that remained was the thrum of power under her skin, ancient and instinctual.

Agatha called it forward not with flash, but with certainty. The light that spread from her palm wasn’t bright or dramatic—it was soft. Steady. 

Rio’s breath hitched, then steadied.

The welt faded slowly, color leeching away like watercolor washed clean. The pain went with it. The heat in the wound disappeared under Agatha’s touch, and the skin knitted back into smoothness as if it had never been hurt at all.

Alice stared. “Holy shit. That’s… that’s not like Rio’s power.”

Agatha allowed herself a breath, her voice even. “No. It’s not.”

Wanda stood nearby, watching the whole thing with a calm that spoke more of trust than surprise.

Alice knelt down beside them, wide-eyed and utterly sincere. “So, like… how powerful are you?”

Agatha didn’t answer. She just brushed a strand of hair from Rio’s face and murmured, “Better?”

Rio nodded slowly, voice quiet. “Yeah. Thank you.”

“You scared me,” Agatha said, barely a whisper.

Rio smiled faintly. “I’m sorry. Guess I got carried away.”

Alice let out a half-laugh, half-sigh and fell backward into the grass. “Okay. Okay. My best friend is a time-stopping nature witch, and her girlfriend is a literal magical doctor with the vibe of a sexy war general. This is fine. Everything is so normal.”

Wanda snorted.

Agatha helped Rio to her feet, steadying her even though she didn’t need to. “That’s enough for today.”

“But—”

“No,” she said more firmly, and Rio didn’t argue. “Resting is also part of learning.”

Rio looked over at Alice, who gave her a huge, lopsided grin and a thumbs up. “Best birthday weekend ever.”

“Also most dangerous,” Wanda added dryly. “And it’s only Sunday.”

Agatha looked at her, a flicker of something fond and fierce blooming low in her chest. “I’m going to make some tea. You’re going to sit and breathe. Deal?”

Rio smiled, just shy. “Yes, ma’am.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and turned toward the house. “And Alice? You’re helping. Might as well learn how to brew something more useful than black coffee.”

Alice jumped up, clearly delighted. “Wait. Magical tea? Is this like, calming? Protective? Makes-you-float kind of tea?”

“No,” Wanda muttered. “It’s chamomile, Alice.”

Alice shook her head. “You people really need a better marketing team.”

~*~

Agatha moved easily around the kitchen, her touch practiced but a little slower than usual, her mind still half on the training session and the flare of fear she’d felt when Rio had gone down. Alice stood by the counter, sleeves pushed up, sorting through the mismatched jars of dried herbs Rio kept in her cupboard like half-forgotten secrets.

“She’s going to be okay,” Alice said after a moment, watching Agatha work. “Isn’t she?”

Agatha glanced at her, then gave a small nod. “She will be. She’s tougher than she looks.” A pause, then: “Though I’d like her to stop getting thrown around by spells during training. That would be nice. But I guess she’s still learning.”

Alice snorted, but her eyes were thoughtful. “I guess I didn’t expect magic to be so… intense.”

“It’s not always like that,” Agatha murmured. “But when it is, it doesn’t care if you’re ready.”

She turned to pour the hot water into the teapot and set it between them on the counter. Alice watched her for a beat longer, lips pressing together before she finally said, “Can I ask you something kind of weird?”

Agatha’s mouth quirked slightly. “Considering the last twenty-four hours, I think you get a pass.”

Alice leaned against the counter. “You said Eliza never mentioned Rio before. Never said she had a granddaughter. But… don’t you think that’s kind of strange?”

That made Agatha go still.

“I mean, Eliza was clearly important to the town. And if Rio’s her granddaughter, you’d think people would know, right? Or at least remember her?”

Agatha turned, brows knitting. “I never heard Eliza talk about a grandchild. But now that you mentioned it… yeah, it is kind of strange.” Her eyes narrowed slightly.

Alice nodded slowly.

“There were rumors back then,” Agatha continued, her voice dropping. “Nothing concrete, just whispers. That Daisy had too much power, that she was unstable. Some said she overdosed, others said she was consumed by magic—burned out from the inside. No one really knew. No one really asked.”

Alice frowned. “And when did that happen?”

Agatha’s gaze drifted toward the window. “I was about twenty-one. My mother disappeared that same winter.”

Alice blinked. “Seriously?”

Agatha gave a slow nod. “She went out one night to do some of her rituals in the woods. She never came back.”

Silence settled for a moment, heavy but not oppressive.

“So Eliza lost her daughter,” Alice said softly, “and you lost your mom. At the same time.”

Agatha exhaled. “I never connected the two before. But it’s hard not to now.”

Before either of them could speak again, the back door creaked and the sound of voices filtered in—Rio’s low murmur, Wanda’s sharper laugh. Alice looked toward the door, then back at Agatha.

“If Daisy really was Rio’s mom,” she said quietly, “then Rio’s been in this longer than she knows.”

Agatha’s eyes lingered on the teapot as if seeing something far beyond it. “Maybe even longer than we know.”

The back door swung open with a gentle creak, and the chill of the late afternoon breeze slipped in before Rio and Wanda did.

“Smells like something’s brewing,” Wanda called lightly, brushing her windblown curls out of her face as she stepped inside.

Rio followed, her cheeks pink from the cold and something else—lingering adrenaline, maybe, or the afterglow of being healed. Her eyes darted between the two women at the kitchen counter. “Hey. What did we miss?”

Alice straightened, eyes flicking briefly to Agatha before she said carefully, “I was just asking Agatha about your grandmother. Eliza.”

Rio blinked. “Eliza?”

Agatha gave a slow nod, moving toward the teapot and pouring herself a cup. “Alice asked if we knew Eliza had a granddaughter.”

Rio’s brow furrowed. “Oh. Did you? I mean, I never knew about her, but now I figure she probably knew something about me if she left me the cottage, right?”

Agatha stepped closer, her voice low but even. “She never mentioned you, Rio. Not to me, or Wanda. No one in the town ever said Eliza had a granddaughter. But now we’re wondering if it’s because something—or someone—made us all forget.”

Rio’s eyes darkened. “Like a spell?”

Agatha nodded. “A strong one. One that affects memory and perception. It’s possible she didn’t just keep you hidden from the world. She might’ve erased your existence from it. At least from everyone’s memory here.”

Rio sat down slowly at the table, her hands curling around a mug of tea she hadn’t even realized she’d picked up. “But why? Why would she do that?”

Wanda leaned against the counter, crossing her arms. “Back then, there were rumors about Daisy—your mother. That she’d vanished under mysterious circumstances. Some said it was magic. Others said it was addiction. But nothing was ever confirmed. I was away at college then, so I don’t really remember.”

“And apparently it happened around the same time Agatha’s mom disappeared too,” Alice added quietly.

Rio’s gaze snapped to Agatha.

Agatha gave a slow nod. “I never connected the two events before. I was twenty one and I wasn’t here. I was in New York at college. My mother went for a walk and never came back. People looked for her for days, but nothing was ever found. It was like she just vanished. But if Eliza lost Daisy then, too… maybe something happened then. Something big enough to make her believe you wouldn’t be safe in Thistle Grove anymore.”

Rio’s throat worked as she tried to swallow the sudden tightness rising there. “So she sent me away? Changed my memories? Everyone else’s, too? That’s insane.”

“She might’ve thought it was the only way to protect you,” Wanda said gently. “Whatever happened to Daisy… maybe Eliza feared the same fate for you.”

Rio let out a shaky breath, her fingers tightening around her mug. “Look, I don’t… I don’t know about any of that. As far as I’ve always known, I was in the system since I was a baby. That’s the story. That’s what’s real to me.”

“Rio,” Agatha said gently, “we’re not trying to take that away from you.”

“I know,” she said quickly, too quickly. “It’s just… even with all this magic stuff being true, and if something did happen back then—something with Daisy—I don’t remember it. Not one second of it. So if Eliza sent me away, if she erased me from this whole town… then she made that choice without me. She made it permanent. She took away the chance I had to grow up with an actual family.”

Her voice cracked, but she swallowed the sound. Her expression held steady, locked tight behind a mask of wry detachment.

“I’m not ready to start rewriting my entire life because of some cooked up theories, I’m sorry.”

Agatha nodded slowly, not pressing. “That’s okay, sweetheart. We’re just… connecting dots. That’s all.”

Rio gave a small nod, but she didn’t look at anyone as she stood and carried her untouched mug to the sink.

Alice watched her carefully, still too new to this world to know what to say. Wanda didn’t speak either.

Rio leaned against the counter, arms folded. Outside, the wind picked up. “Whatever happened to Daisy or your mom or anyone else… it’s not like we have answers anyway. Just questions. And a whole lot of magic we barely understand.”

“Then maybe that’s where we start,” Wanda said, her voice calm but grounded. “Not with the past. With what’s in front of us now.”

That, at least, felt solid enough to stand on. Rio nodded again, slower this time. “Yeah. Okay.”

Agatha caught her gaze and offered the smallest smile. “We go at your pace.”

And for now, that was enough.

~*~

They left Wanda’s house just after dusk, when the air had turned cool and a soft wind carried the scent of pine and smoke through the town. Wanda had offered them another round of tea or even dinner, but the suggestion to head over to the Silver Mare had won out quickly—mostly because Vision had just arrived and declared he definitely needed a drink after the day he’d had.

Now, the five of them made their way down the old cobblestone path toward the only bar in Thistle Grove, boots tapping a soft rhythm. Vision and Wanda walked ahead, chatting easily, while Alice walked with them, asking a string of questions about protective enchantments and illusion spells with the wide-eyed curiosity of someone who’d stepped into a fantasy novel and hadn’t quite come to terms with the fact it was real.

Agatha stayed beside Rio.

At first, Rio hadn’t said much. She nodded occasionally at something Alice said and even cracked a smile at one of Vision’s dry jokes, but Agatha saw the telltale signs—the way Rio’s fingers tugged at the edge of her sleeve, the faint crease between her brows, the way her eyes flicked up toward the darkening sky more than once.

And Agatha felt it too. The shift.

A low, rolling tension curled above them like smoke. The sky had taken on a bruised hue, with clouds thickening faster than the wind could scatter them. A storm was building.

Agatha slowed her pace just a little until they fell behind the others. “You’re being awfully quiet.”

Rio gave her a sidelong glance. “Just tired.”

Agatha raised a brow. “Tired’s not a feeling that brews thunderstorms overhead.”

Rio didn’t laugh. Her gaze flicked upward again, lips pressing together in a line.

“I’m not… upset,” she said eventually. “I just—”

“Feel like everything you thought you knew about your past might be unraveling?” Agatha offered, gently.

Rio let out a slow breath. “Yeah. That.”

They walked in silence for another few steps before Agatha reached for her hand and laced their fingers together. “You don’t have to figure it all out tonight, you know.”

“I know.” But her voice was tight. “It’s just… I always thought I’d been in the system since I was a baby. That I’d never had a family. That I’d been abandoned. But now there’s this idea that maybe I did, and maybe they sent me away. On purpose.”

“We don’t know that,” Agatha said softly. “But knowing Eliza, if she really did do that, then it was definitely out of love, Rio. To protect you.”

Rio looked at her, and for a moment Agatha thought she might argue—but she didn’t. Instead, she squeezed Agatha’s hand and looked ahead again.

The Silver Mare came into view, tucked between two old stone buildings and glowing warmly from the inside out. Music drifted through the cracked front windows—bluesy and slow—and laughter echoed faintly behind the walls.

Agatha let herself smile. “Come on, birthday girl. Let’s drink something ridiculously strong and forget about memory spells and lost mothers for just a little while.”

Rio finally cracked a smile. “As long as there’s no enchanted liquor involved.”

“No promises.”

 

Chapter 17: Seventeen

Chapter Notes

So sorry for the long wait. Had an emergency with my dog and my focus has been pretty much all on her since then.

But I hope you guys enjoy this one.

The Silver Mare looked exactly like what a bar in a town like Thistle Grove should look like—low wooden beams, mismatched stools, a jukebox in the corner playing something old and twangy, and fairy lights strung over the bar that probably stayed up year-round. There was a dartboard with at least four holes in the wall around it, and the faint scent of fried food and pine cleaner lingered in the air.

It was homey. Comforting. Normal.

And Rio needed normal. She needed to not think about foggy memories and missing mothers and the idea that maybe, just maybe, everything she thought she knew about her life was a carefully constructed lie.

“Birthday girl gets the honor of choosing the first round,” Wanda announced, patting Rio on the back before heading straight to the bar with Vision trailing behind her like a shadow. “And I’m making it strong so pick your poison.”

“I trust your judgement, almighty teacher,” Rio replied with a laugh.

Agatha leaned close to Rio’s ear. “One drink, then I’m taking you to the pool table and absolutely kicking your ass. It’s the least I can do.”

Rio laughed despite herself, grateful for the way Agatha’s voice always managed to cut through the fog in her brain. “Bold of you to assume I don’t have secret skills.”

“Oh no, I assume you do. I just assume mine are better.”

Rio grinned and followed Agatha over, sinking into the seat beside her while Wanda returned with a tray full of tequila shots.

“To Rio,” Wanda declared, raising her glass. “For being brave, for turning thirty-five, and for not letting either of those things get in the way of having fun tonight.”

They all raised their shots. Rio hesitated for half a second, then clinked hers against Agatha’s and downed it.

The burn felt good. Like waking up.

One shot turned into two, and soon enough, Agatha was dragging her over to the pool table with a devilish smirk. “You’re not getting out of this,” she said, handing Rio a cue stick. “Birthday or not.”

“You’re enjoying this way too much.”

“Of course I am. I’ve had a long week. Teaching you a lesson in physics and geometry disguised as pool will be the highlight of my evening.”

Rio narrowed her eyes but couldn’t stop the smile tugging at her lips. “Fine. But if I win, you owe me a back massage.”

“If I win, I’ll give you two and more.”

They played three rounds. Rio won one, barely. Agatha won the other two with the kind of smug elegance that made Rio want to both kiss her and smack her in equal measure. By the time they returned to the table, laughing and flushed, Alice was halfway through a sweet cider and Wanda was lining up another shot for Vision, who looked deeply unamused by the sugary cherry garnish on the rim.

Rio flopped into the booth beside Agatha again, catching her breath. “You’re ridiculous.”

“I’m fantastic.”

“That too.”

And just like that, things felt light again.

The clouds hadn’t fully cleared from the sky outside—Rio could still feel the weight of them, heavy and waiting—but inside this little bar, with Agatha’s thigh pressed against hers and the warm buzz of alcohol in her system, it didn’t matter. Not for now.

She didn’t have all the answers, but she had people. She had moments like this. Laughter. Warmth. The comfort of being seen.

~*~

The bar had filled out by the time Rio finished her fifth game of pool — now undefeated, despite Agatha’s increasingly shameless tactics to distract her. There was music playing on the jukebox, something with a heavy beat and a chorus made for shouting, and the birthday girl had earned herself another round of drinks courtesy of Alice and a pair of charming older ladies at the next table over who’d declared her “too pretty not to be dangerous.”

She was flushed and giddy by the time she slid back into her seat beside Agatha, her hand landing instinctively on the older woman’s thigh beneath the table. Agatha didn’t even flinch—she leaned into it, casual and warm and entirely hers.

Vision sat across from them, impeccably dressed in some dark blazer that looked way too sophisticated for a dive bar, even a cozy one like the Silver Mare. He had his hands wrapped around a pint glass, listening to Wanda chat with the bartender about rare meads and mushroom tinctures. But when Rio returned, his attention drifted politely back to her.

“So, Rio,” he said, tone light and inquisitive. “What does it feel like?”

Rio blinked. “What does what feel like?”

“To be a Thread,” he said, tilting his head slightly. “You’re the third, aren’t you?”

She nodded slowly. “Apparently. Still figuring out what that even means, to be honest.”

Agatha chuckled softly beside her. “It means she’s stubborn and reckless and powerful as hell,” she said, brushing a strand of hair from Rio’s cheek. “But also… yeah. It’s a lot.”

Vision smiled. “I’ve read about the Threads. Most of the old texts refer to them like legends—archetypes, not real people. Three witches bound by blood and purpose, representing something older than modern covens ever tried to define.”

“Sounds dramatic,” Rio said, raising an eyebrow.

“Oh, it is,” Wanda said as she rejoined them, sliding another drink in Agatha’s direction. “The kind of thing we used to whisper about at Full Moon ceremonies when we were little girls. ‘What if the three Threads reunite in our lifetime?’ No one ever thought they actually would.”

“And yet, here we are,” Vision said, eyes on Rio now. “All three of you in Thistle Grove. The magic must feel… different. Stronger.”

“It does,” Agatha admitted, taking a sip of her drink. “There’s something stirring. And with Rio here with so much untapped power, it’s like something has turned its head toward us again.”

Rio exhaled slowly. “I don’t even know how to describe it,” she said, resting her elbow on the table. “Half the time it feels like my blood is singing. The other half, I’m just trying not to accidentally summon a rainstorm if I stub my toe.”

Vision leaned forward, thoughtful. “You must be experiencing a sort of magical recalibration. Your presence changes the weave. Brings ancient enchantments back into motion. The land remembers, doesn’t it?”

That made something in Rio still. The land remembers . She’d felt that more than once—walking through the woods, stepping into the garden behind the cottage, her dreams that felt like memories. The land did remember her. Even if she didn’t remember it.

Agatha’s hand found hers under the table again, grounding her.

“You’re handling it beautifully,” she said quietly. “No one expects you to have all the answers yet.”

Rio gave her a small smile. “Yeah, well. I’ve got questions I don’t even know how to ask. Let alone answers.”

Vision studied her a moment longer, then offered a gracious smile. “Sometimes the questions matter more than the answers.”

Here, there was only Agatha.

And that was more than enough.

~*~

They didn’t hear the footsteps at first.

Someone had been there.

And they hadn’t been drunk. Or clumsy.

They’d been watching.

And somewhere, just out of sight, a figure crouched behind the trees. Cloaked in old magic and quiet power, they watched as the two women returned to the warm light of the bar, laughter swallowing them up again.

But the figure didn’t laugh. They just tilted their head.

Three Threads. Together again.

It was only a matter of time now.

~*~

When Rio and Agatha stepped back into the Silver Mare, they were met with a blast of laughter, music, and the clink of glasses. The bar was still lively, though the crowd had thinned a bit, giving everything a looser, more languid energy.

Vision, still seated with a tumbler of something dark, offered a mild smile. “Just fascinated by the convergence we’re witnessing. It’s rare. Historic, even.”

They stayed like that for a while longer, trading stories, laughing louder as the alcohol loosened everyone’s edges. Rio felt warm and buzzy and, despite everything looming beyond the walls of the bar, good. She caught Agatha watching her once or twice—open, amused, hungry.

By the time they decided to call it a night, the moon was high and the wind had picked up again, brushing across her skin like a whisper.

As they stepped outside, Rio glanced up at the clouds shifting over Thistle Grove.

The night air was crisp and smelled faintly of salt and pine. The last burst of laughter echoed behind them as the door swung shut. The buzz from drinks and good company lingered like a glow under their skin.

Rio tugged her coat tighter around her and leaned briefly into Agatha’s side, her cheek brushing the edge of her shoulder. Agatha didn’t even hesitate before curling an arm around her waist, drawing her in close.

Wanda stretched her arms over her head with a groan. “That was fun,” she said, her voice warm with liquor and a little sentimentality. “You two can definitely party.”

“That was your idea, darling,” Wanda said, poking him in the ribs.

“I regret nothing,” Vision replied dryly. He turned to Agatha and Rio, his gaze flickering thoughtfully between them. “Thank you for letting me tag along. It was enlightening.”

Agatha raised a brow at the phrasing, but she was too mellow from whiskey and Rio’s proximity to question it. “We’ll do it again sometime.”

And as they walked down the sleepy street together, something about it felt—if only for a little while—like home.

~*~

When they made it to Agatha’s place, Mr. Scratchy was waiting for them by the door, like a parent ready to scold their teenagers for being out too late.

 “Alice, meet Mr. Scratchy,” Agatha said, guiding Alice into the living room where a sleek, white rabbit with twitching ears hopped back to the couch with a huff. Mr. Scratchy looked at Alice with large, inquisitive eyes before hopping over to her, nudging her leg.

Alice giggled, crouching down to pet him. “He’s adorable! He seems so calm,” Alice said, her voice full of affection as she stroked the rabbit’s soft fur.

“He’s a bit of a character,” Agatha replied with a grin, though there was a fondness in her voice. “He’s my familiar. Comes with the territory.”

Alice gave her a quick wave and entered the room, closing the door behind her.

Rio’s exhaustion, however, had already caught up with her. She wasn’t sure if it was the combination of the long day or the alcohol, but as soon as she laid down on the soft bed in her own room, her body relaxed, and the weight of everything seemed to melt away. Then, a voice—a soft, familiar voice, though not one she had ever heard before. “I love you so much, my little witch,” it whispered, the words sweet and full of love. “I’m so proud to be your mama, baby girl.”

The voice didn’t belong to anyone she knew, but the warmth of it settled over her like a blanket, and she felt a sense of peace that she couldn’t explain. It was comforting, though, as if the universe itself had wrapped her in its arms. The voice spoke again, but it was distant, as if fading away: “I love you.”

She shook her head, trying to clear the remnants of the dream. It had to have been the alcohol. She hadn’t even realized how much she had drunk the night before. Definitely just the alcohol, Rio told herself, pushing the strange, comforting sensation away as best as she could.

But for some reason, that voice, that love, lingered in the back of her mind.

Agatha.

~*~

Not performative, not charming for charm’s sake. Just warm. Honest. Quietly hers.

God, it wasn’t fair how easily Agatha could do that to her.

Agatha held her gaze a second longer, her smile lingering before she turned back to her customer and wrapped up the sale with a few soft-spoken words and a flourish of her hand.

Alice leaned in with a whisper that wasn’t nearly quiet enough. “She smiles like that at you and you’re still trying to say you’re not in love?”

Rio stared at her, deadpan. “Do you want to be hexed?”

Alice grinned, smug as ever, and nudged her forward just as Agatha stepped out from behind the counter.

“Morning,” Agatha said, eyes never leaving Rio. “You found your way back.”

Rio nodded, her voice caught somewhere in her throat. “Yeah. Had to pick up my car. I have to go feed Salem.”

Agatha’s lips twitched into something a little sly. “I’m sure Salem’s been rehearsing his curses all morning.”

Alice gave a theatrical bow. “We’ll have to walk in prepared for battle.”

But Rio couldn’t quite bring herself to look away from Agatha—not with the way she stood there, sunlight dancing through her dark hair, smelling like herbs and honey and safety. Not with the way her smile hadn’t faded, not even a little.

Not with the way Rio could already feel herself falling, just a little further.

Rio had barely managed to string together a coherent thought when Agatha’s gaze flicked down—just briefly—and her smile curved into something sharper, softer, all at once. Her eyes lingered on the open edge of Rio’s coat, where the dark navy collar of her borrowed shirt peeked out unmistakably.

“You’re wearing my shirt,” Agatha said, low and amused, like it was a secret just between them.

Rio opened her mouth to deny it—on reflex, maybe, or because her heart was already hammering too loudly—but she didn’t get the chance.

Agatha stepped closer with the kind of quiet confidence that always made Rio forget how to breathe. She crossed the space between them, then slipped an arm around Rio’s waist and tugged her close.

Rio felt her breath catch—right there in her throat—because Agatha didn’t just hug her. No, she anchored her. One hand on her hip, the other ghosting along her back, holding her like she’d been waiting all morning for the chance.

The shop disappeared a little around them. The jars and herbs and customers and curious best friends all faded into something blurry, something soft. The scent of Agatha’s perfume—lavender, citrus, something sweet and hard to place—settled around Rio like a spell.

Agatha’s voice dipped, just for her. “You look better in it than I do.”

Rio swallowed, her arms instinctively finding their way around Agatha’s waist. “That’s not true.”

“Mm,” Agatha murmured, brushing her thumb along the curve of Rio’s hip through the fabric. “It is.”

Rio felt herself flush, felt the butterflies turn into something molten and warm, fluttering low in her belly. She wanted to stay there forever. Just like that.

But she cleared her throat instead and tried for levity, because that’s what she always did when things felt too real. “I was just borrowing it. Emergency shirt situation.”

Agatha leaned in, voice a little huskier now. “You can borrow anything you want, darling. Though I’m not sure I’ll want to wash it once it smells like you.”

Rio nearly combusted on the spot.

Alice, somewhere in the background, made a dramatic gagging noise that Rio pointedly ignored.

Agatha chuckled softly and pressed a kiss to her cheek—nothing grand, nothing showy. Just soft. Intimate. The kind of kiss that said I see you, I want you.

Rio didn’t let go. Not for a long moment.

She didn’t want to.

 

Chapter 18: Eighteen

Chapter Notes

Thank you so much for your lovely comments!

Agatha watched Rio and Alice walk out the door, the soft chime of the bell the only sound she allowed herself to focus on for a moment. Rio glanced back once—just a quick look, shy and warm beneath the brim of her beanie—and Agatha felt her heart pull in that familiar, ridiculous way.

“Text me when you get a break,” Rio had said over her shoulder at the door, brushing their fingers together for the briefest second. “We’ll come back later if you’re free.”

Agatha had nodded, not trusting herself to say much with Alice standing so smugly at Rio’s side. “Be careful. The roads are slick.”

Rio smiled—soft, like it was just for her. “I always am.”

And then they were gone, their boots crunching into fresh snow as they headed toward the car parked at the end of the path.

Agatha stood still for half a beat, eyes lingering on the spot where Rio had been, before she exhaled through her nose and turned back toward the shop. She tucked a loose strand of hair behind her ear and squared her shoulders.

No time to dwell.

The apothecary had already started to buzz again.

By midmorning, the shop was full—locals popping in for restocks, tourists still lingering in town after the festival over the weekend. The snow had only added to the charm of Thistle Grove, blanketing the town in postcard-worthy quiet, but it also meant chapped lips, seasonal allergies, and an uptick in hot tonic orders.

She didn’t mind. Not today.

Agatha moved through the space like a current—graceful, deliberate, practiced. She mixed teas, measured tinctures, offered advice and subtle charm in equal measure. She knew how to work a room, even one filled with aching joints and wide-eyed city girls asking if the “energy-cleansing salt” was edible.

The bell above the door rang over and over again, and Agatha didn’t stop moving.

She liked this—being busy. It kept her hands occupied and her mind focused. It gave her no space for soft distractions like Rio’s voice in her ear or the warmth of her body under the covers or the way she looked this morning in her shirt, standing in the middle of Agatha’s shop like she belonged there.

But even as she tried to keep her head down, even as she blended and bottled and swept herbs into little waxed paper pouches, the image lingered:

Rio in her shirt.

Rio in her bed.

Rio, sleepy and warm, whispering that she could have all the minutes she wanted.

And gods help her—Agatha wasn’t sure what scared her more: how fast this thing was unfolding, or how badly she already wanted more.

~*~

By the time Agatha made it through the last layer of wards and stepped into the clearing behind Wanda’s house, the nearly winter air nipped at her cheeks and her boots crunched softly over the snow-dusted ground. The protective enchantments shimmered faintly in the air behind her—sigils etched into the bark of the trees, glowing just enough to let her know she was exactly where she was meant to be.

It had been a couple of days. She’d seen glimpses of Rio here and there—quick texts, a few lingering voice messages that played too softly for anyone else to hear—but work had swallowed them both whole. Monday and Tuesday had vanished in a blur of potions and appointments and Rio’s deadlines.

So this—this quiet, secret space in the woods, carved out by Wanda and cloaked in powerful magic—felt like breathing again.

Her eyes found Rio instantly.

She stood near the fire Wanda had conjured, bundled up in a thick sweater, dark curls tucked into a hat that didn’t quite hide the concentration on her face. Her brow was furrowed as Wanda paced in front of her, gesturing toward the open air and tracing glowing defensive runes with a flick of her fingers.

Agatha smiled before she even realized it was happening.

She didn’t call out, didn’t interrupt. She just watched for a second, her chest pulling tight with something too complicated for a name.

Rio was listening—so intently, so open to this strange new world she’d stumbled into. She looked steady. Strong. And something about it made Agatha’s pulse slow in the best way.

Alice sat nearby in a makeshift chair of thickly padded cushions and wool blankets, wrapped up like a human burrito. She gave Agatha a silent wave and pantomimed shivering dramatically as Agatha stepped closer to the fire.

Wanda, of course, didn’t miss a beat.

“You’re late,” she said without looking up, though her lips twitched faintly. “As usual.”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “Some of us have to keep capitalism from collapsing.”

Wanda snorted and gestured toward Rio. “And some of us are trying to make sure your girlfriend doesn’t accidentally explode herself next time she draws the wrong sigil.”

“She’s not my—” Agatha began, then immediately gave up when both Wanda and Alice raised eyebrows in unison. “Fine. Continue.”

Wanda winked and turned back to Rio, whose cheeks were already flushed from the cold—or maybe from Agatha’s arrival. Her eyes flicked toward Agatha just once, a glimmer of something warm and steady passing between them.

Agatha stepped closer, her coat catching firelight as she joined the circle. “Hope I didn’t miss the part where we fight demons.”

Rio smiled, the kind that made Agatha want to pull her in by the collar and kiss her breathless.

“No demons yet,” she said, voice soft but sure. “Just some very judgmental runes.”

Agatha chuckled and folded her arms, settling in beside her. “You’ll charm them eventually. You’ve got that look.”

“What look?”

Agatha didn’t answer—just reached out and brushed a curl from Rio’s cheek, letting her hand linger a second longer than necessary.

That look, she thought, and smiled to herself as Wanda began the next part of the lesson.

Wanda waved her fingers, and the glowing runes she’d been sketching in the air drifted down into the snow like embers. “Alright,” she said briskly, “we’ve covered basic wards, circle casting, and minor hex deflection. Time for something fun.”

Rio’s eyes widened just slightly. “Fun usually means dangerous when you say it.”

“Correct,” Wanda said, far too cheerfully. “But it’s also the quickest way to learn. Now”—she clapped her gloved hands together—“I want you to form a shield. Visualize it like a dome over your body. Hold the image, feel the shape of it in your chest, then pull it into your hands. Got it?”

Rio nodded slowly, brow furrowing again, and raised her hands. The magic was still new, still raw—but it didn’t rebel against her anymore. It met her like something curious, something willing to listen. Pale golden light shimmered at her fingertips as she began to draw the shape Wanda had described.

Agatha, silent at her side, watched with a kind of reverence she usually reserved for rare ingredients and ancient spells. Rio’s lips were slightly parted, her breath puffing in the cold as she concentrated, and her magic responded with a flickering pulse that wrapped around her like heat rising from the fire.

“Good,” Wanda said, nodding. “Now hold it.”

And then she threw a ball of energy at her.

It was small, controlled, nothing dangerous—but Agatha still twitched, even though she knew Wanda wouldn’t actually hurt her. The spell slammed into the shield with a sharp crackle and fizzled out in a burst of sparks.

Rio flinched but didn’t drop the shield.

Wanda grinned. “Not bad.”

Rio looked down at her hands, almost disbelieving. “I did it?”

“You did,” Agatha said, voice warm with pride. “Held it like a pro.”

Rio turned to her, glowing just a little brighter than the runes in the snow, and Agatha couldn’t help herself—she reached out and tucked a loose strand of hair back under Rio’s hat. Her fingers lingered near her cheek, and for a heartbeat, the entire clearing seemed to still around them.

“You’re getting good at this,” Agatha said softly.

Rio ducked her head, but the smile stayed. “I had a good teacher.”

Wanda groaned. “Oh for the love of the goddess, if you two start making out next to my fire I will douse you both with freezing rain.”

Alice snorted from her blanket pile. “Please do. It’s getting saccharine in here.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but didn’t step away, not just yet. She didn’t care if Wanda teased or Alice gagged—she hadn’t seen Rio in days and this moment, this warmth, was hers to savor.

Eventually, Wanda relented with a wave of her hand. “Alright, let’s break for food before I teach her how to hex a man from thirty yards.”

“I already know how to do that,” Rio said dryly.

Agatha grinned, eyes gleaming. “That’s my girl.”

As soon as Wanda dramatically spun on her heel and marched off toward the house, Alice trailing after her with a theatrical sigh and an exaggerated shiver, Rio’s hand shot out and caught Agatha’s wrist.

Agatha turned, one brow arched, amused and already halfway into some flirtatious remark—

But Rio didn’t let her speak.
