She tugged her in close, right up against her, snow crunching under their boots as their bodies aligned. And then she kissed her—really kissed her—deep and slow, like the buildup of a spell finally loosed into the world.

Agatha stilled for only half a breath, and then her arms came around Rio’s waist, pulling her closer. The fire crackled behind them, casting warm flickers across their skin, but it had nothing on the heat curling between them now.

When Rio finally pulled back, her breath visible in the cold, her eyes were darker and full of something steady.

“I missed you,” she said, voice low and a little hoarse. “And I really didn’t want to wait until later to do that.”

Agatha just looked at her for a moment, lips parted, hair tousled, cheeks pink from more than the chill. Then, with a slow smile and a voice like velvet, she murmured, “Do it again.”

And this time, they both leaned in at once.

The second kiss was deeper, slower, like a thread winding tighter between them—until a sharp voice cut through the air like a gust of cold wind:

“Oh my goddess, get your asses inside before I set the ward on fire!”

Rio jerked back with a startled laugh, forehead falling against Agatha’s shoulder as Agatha sighed dramatically.

“Do you ever let people have a moment?” Agatha called toward the house.

“No!” Wanda’s voice floated back from the kitchen door. “Moments are for people who aren’t freezing their asses off while soup gets cold!”

Rio grinned against Agatha’s coat, her breath warming the wool, before finally stepping back. Agatha didn’t let go completely though—she kept one arm slung casually around Rio’s waist as they walked together toward the house, boots crunching through packed snow.

Inside, the kitchen smelled like rosemary and garlic and something rich bubbling on the stove. Wanda had thrown together a hearty stew, and the fire in the hearth made everything feel impossibly cozy. Alice was already curled up at the table with a steaming mug in both hands, looking like a cat who’d claimed a particularly warm sunspot.

“I hate that I’m leaving Sunday,” she moaned. “You’re all just getting to the good part, and I’m going to be stuck on a plane with crying babies and no magic.”

“We’ll save you some cursed herbs as a souvenir,” Wanda deadpanned, setting bowls on the table.

Once everyone had settled in with food and wine, the conversation turned to catch-up. Agatha leaned her elbow on the table, eyes flicking to Rio as she spoke.

“Shop’s been slammed since the weekend,” she said, swirling her wine. “The festival brought in more tourists than I’ve seen since before the pandemic. People suddenly care a lot about winter skin salves.”

Rio smiled around her spoon. “I’ve been wrangling deadlines and trying not to throw my laptop out the window. And Salem has entered his ‘dramatic teenager’ phase. He refuses to eat unless I personally hand-feed him shredded turkey.”

Alice snorted. “You’re raising a prince.”

Agatha, meanwhile, tilted her head. “Anything… strange happen?”

Rio paused. “Besides my cat staging a hunger strike?”

“No, I mean…” Agatha hesitated, searching her words. “I don’t know. The last couple of nights—I’ve had these dreams. Not bad, just… loud. Like the veil between this world and the next has been fluttering.”

Rio blinked. “Actually… I had a weird dream, too. I think I was a kid in it and there was a woman’s voice. I couldn’t see her, but she said she loved me. That she was proud of me.”

Wanda, from across the kitchen, looked up sharply. “That doesn’t sound like just a dream.”

Agatha’s gaze narrowed. “You think—?”

Wanda nodded slowly. “Your powers are increasing fast, Rio. Magic like that doesn’t stay quiet. You might be hearing echoes. Ancestors. Guides. Especially if it was a woman.”

Rio’s throat went a little tight, spoon forgotten in her bowl. “She called me her little witch.”

Alice reached over and touched her hand, her face softening. “You okay?”

Rio swallowed and nodded. “Yeah. It just… felt real. You know?”

Agatha leaned over, bumping her shoulder gently. “You should always write these down. Dreams like that? They’re never just dreams.”

Rio smiled at her, eyes a little glassy, but steady. “I did. The grimoire… it just kind of popped up out of thin air.”

Wanda’s brows arched. “Now that’s interesting.”

Agatha’s brow furrowed slightly, something curious sparking behind her eyes. “Wait, when did this dream happen?”

Rio set her spoon down, the faintest hint of pink blooming in her cheeks. “Monday morning. At your place.”

Agatha blinked. “At my place? And you’re just telling me now?”

Rio gave a helpless shrug, lips tugging into a sheepish half-smile. “You were hungover and grumpy, remember?”

Agatha snorted, leaning back in her chair. “Alright, fair.”

“And then I fell asleep again,” Rio added. “Didn’t even remember the dream until after you’d already left. I was just lying there, thinking about how I wished I had the grimoire so I could write it down, and bam —it dropped onto the bed next to me.”

Alice choked on her stew. “Like… just appeared?”

Rio nodded. “Yeah. One second it wasn’t there, and then it was.”

Agatha’s eyes sharpened, a slow, thoughtful kind of alertness washing over her. “That’s advanced magic. Responsive magic. Your grimoire’s already bonded to you more deeply than we thought.”

Wanda, now lurking in the corner with her own bowl in hand, gave a low whistle. “That book is old, Rio. It doesn’t respond like that unless it truly recognizes you as its owner.”

Rio looked down at her hands, suddenly aware of the quiet humming beneath her skin. “It just felt… normal. Like it was supposed to be there.”

Agatha reached for her under the table, fingers curling around Rio’s without needing to ask. “It was supposed to be there,” she said softly. “And so were you.”

Rio glanced up at her, heart tripping a little.

But Agatha just kept tracing slow, lazy patterns over Rio’s skin with her thumb, quiet and steady. Like she was grounding her. Or maybe anchoring herself.

Rio could feel that same warmth she’d been carrying since Monday morning—the kind that had nothing to do with the fireplace or the wine or the hot stew in her stomach.

It was her.

“So,” Agatha murmured at last, voice pitched just low enough to be just between them, “next time you wake up from a prophetic dream in my bed, maybe tell me about it before three days have passed?”

Rio gave her a look, trying to fight her smile. “I said you were hungover.”

“I’m always hungover on Mondays.”

“That sounds like a you problem.”

That made her give Rio a playful kick under the table, and she leaned in, resting her temple briefly against Agatha’s shoulder, letting herself breathe in the scent of her again.

Agatha tilted her head to rest there a moment too, and they sat like that until Wanda clapped her hands together, loud and commanding.

“Alright, lovebirds. Enough brooding and pining and magical sexual tension. Finish your dinner and let’s get back to work.”

Alice groaned dramatically. “She’s like McGonagall with less chill and more wine.”

“Less talking, more fire rune practice,” Wanda said, already moving toward the back door. “Let’s see if your aim’s gotten any better, Vidal.”

Rio stood, rolling her eyes, but she was smiling, a little warmth tucked beneath her ribs like a secret. She felt Agatha’s hand brush lightly over her lower back as she passed.

“Try not to set yourself on fire,” Agatha murmured, lips close enough to graze her ear.

Rio smirked.

~*~

Agatha watched Rio walk ahead with Wanda and Alice, her coat flaring slightly with each step, the hem brushing the tops of her boots—and her sweater still visible under the lapels. That alone sent a jolt of something electric through Agatha’s chest, like ownership and affection and danger all wrapped in one.

She lingered a beat, pretending to adjust something on the table, but really just needing the moment to catch her breath. Because gods, that girl had no idea what she did to her.

When she finally followed them out into the snow-slicked yard behind Wanda’s house, the wards shimmered faintly overhead like they were aware of her magic, too. She felt them buzz softly at the edges of her senses—alive, alert, protective.

Wanda was already lecturing, using a stick to draw a series of defensive runes in the snow. Rio knelt nearby, brow furrowed in concentration, mirroring the lines with her finger, careful and deliberate. And Agatha… she just watched.

Watched the way Rio chewed on her lower lip when she was focused. The way the runes responded to her touch—glimmering faintly like fireflies caught beneath the surface of the snow. The way she kept glancing back at Agatha when she thought no one was looking.

It hit her then, quiet and sharp.

She was in trouble.

Not because she didn’t trust Rio, or because this was happening too fast—but because for the first time in a very, very long while, Agatha Harkness was starting to believe in things she’d carefully tucked away for decades.

In warmth.

In magic.

In the kind of connection that didn’t burn you up—but lit you up from the inside.

“You’re staring,” Wanda muttered beside her, arms crossed over her chest. “And it’s disgustingly sweet.”

Agatha didn’t even bother to deny it. “She’s good,” she murmured. “Really good.”

“She’s herself,” Wanda said. “That’s what’s making the magic strong. Not training. Not bloodline. It’s her being seen. And letting herself be seen.”

Agatha’s breath caught in her throat. Gods, yes. That was exactly it.

She’d never met anyone who looked at her the way Rio did. Not with awe. Not with fear. But with recognition.

Like she knew her already.

Like she wasn’t afraid of the dark edges.

A gust of wind swirled snow across the clearing, and Agatha tugged her coat tighter, stuffing her hands into her pockets.

She wasn’t ready to say it out loud yet—not even to herself. But if the feeling in her chest was any indication, if the way Rio’s laughter caught on the wind made something inside her ache—

Well.

She was probably going to say it soon.

And for once, that didn’t scare her at all.

 

~*~

Agatha stayed toward the edges of the clearing, leaning against one of the thick pines Wanda had woven a ward into ages ago. It hummed faintly with old magic—hers, Wanda’s, Eliza’s. The tree had seen so many winters and secrets and long-forgotten spells, but tonight it stood witness to something else entirely.

New magic.

Across the clearing, Rio was glowing. Not literally—though Agatha wouldn’t have been surprised if she did—but in that unmistakable way someone looked when they were finally stepping into themselves. Wanda tossed out a lazy little spark of pressure and Rio caught it, eyes narrowing, fingers dancing into the defensive rune she’d just practiced.

The energy bounced off her sigil, cracking harmlessly against a tree trunk behind her. Rio blinked at her own success.

Agatha couldn’t help the grin that tugged at her mouth. “That’s my girl,” she murmured before she could even think better of it.

Alice, wrapped in what looked like three different scarves and a very aggressive sweater, looked up from her spot near the fire and smirked. “Your girl, huh?”

Agatha didn’t answer—just raised one brow in a way that made Alice cackle and clap her gloved hands together.

Wanda was clearly trying not to smile as she addressed Rio again. “Alright, try holding it longer this time. And don’t tense up. Magic wants your intention, not your muscle.”

Rio nodded, adjusting her stance. She looked so serious, so ready, and Agatha felt her heart twist in the way it only did when something truly, unexpectedly good entered her life and she had no idea what to do with it.

Ten minutes later, Wanda gave a sharp nod. “That’s enough for tonight. Go warm up before one of you loses a finger.”

Alice immediately bolted toward the house. “Yes, please. I love magic but not enough to freeze to death for it.”

Wanda’s voice was still ringing across the clearing, sharp and exasperated—“Get your asses inside already!”—but Agatha didn’t move. Not yet.

She reached out, catching Rio gently by the sleeve before she could follow after Alice. The night air was biting, and her gloves were stuffed in her pocket, but she didn’t care. She needed this moment.

Rio turned toward her, expectant, the firelight flickering across her cheeks, her breath visible between them in little silver clouds.

Agatha didn’t say anything at first. She just reached for her—one hand at Rio’s waist, the other brushing her hair back, then cradling her cheek. Her thumb lingered just below her jaw.

And then she leaned in and kissed her.

It wasn’t rushed—it was claiming. Not in a possessive way, but in that quiet, resolute way Agatha had always done everything that mattered: with intention. With truth. With feeling she didn’t bother hiding anymore.

When she finally pulled back, her voice was low, velvet-wrapped and certain. “You’re mine tonight.”

Rio blinked, startled just a second before that slow, crooked smile curved her lips. “Is that so?”

Agatha’s smile matched it. “Mmhm.” She leaned in again, brushing her nose lightly against Rio’s, her voice soft against her skin. “I’ve missed you.”

Before Rio could say anything back, Wanda shouted again, “I swear to the Goddess, I’m putting a freezing hex on both of you—”

Agatha laughed, finally releasing her hold, but not before stealing one last kiss. Quick. Warm. Absolutely hers.

They headed for the house together, and Agatha didn’t let go of her hand once.

~*~

The moment they stepped into the cottage, Agatha made a quiet excuse to freshen up—though really, she just needed a second to breathe. She hadn’t realized how tightly her heart had been wound since that kiss in the snow. How much she’d needed to hold Rio like that again. It was ridiculous, really, the way one woman could upend her entire center of gravity in just a week.

She left Rio and Alice talking in the front room and ducked into the hallway. But just as she reached the bathroom, she caught her own name spoken in Rio’s soft voice and… paused.

It wasn’t polite to eavesdrop.

It also wasn’t like she had much self-control when it came to Rio Vidal.

So she stood quietly, listening through the crack of the door.

“I was thinking of going back to Agatha’s,” Rio said, her voice quieter than usual, almost shy.

Agatha smiled, pressing her lips together.

Alice’s voice was immediate and smug. “Oh?”

“Not for that,” Rio replied, and Agatha could almost hear the blush in her voice. “Just… to be with her.”

A slow, warm ache settled in Agatha’s chest. She closed her eyes.

Then Alice said, “You deserve this. And I’m really, really happy to see you like this. You’re—” A pause. “You’re glowing, Rio.”

And just like that, Agatha forgot how to breathe.

She leaned lightly against the doorframe, barely making a sound. Something inside her softened—no, melted. She was used to being admired, even desired, but this was different. This wasn’t glamour or seduction or charm. This was someone seeing her and choosing her. This was Rio choosing her.

Even when she wasn’t in the room.

She stayed quiet until the conversation shifted, and then moved back into the hall with careful, unhurried steps. Rio turned at her approach, her expression bright and open in that way that always made Agatha want to grab her face and kiss her senseless.

Instead, Agatha offered her arm with a casual sort of elegance and said, “Ready?”

Rio nodded, saying a soft goodbye to Alice. Agatha didn’t say anything, but she gave Alice a brief smile, one that said thank you in a way she’d never be able to say out loud.

Back in the car, the silence was companionable. The roads were mostly clear, snow pushed to the sides like forgotten lace, and the stars above were sharp and bright through the windshield.

Agatha drove with one hand, the other restless with memory—the curve of Rio’s waist, the warmth of her laughter, the way she’d looked in Agatha’s clothes like they’d always belonged to her.

At the red light, the urge rose like a tide she didn’t even try to resist.

She reached over and took Rio’s hand.

No performance, no seduction—just connection. A tether.

Rio looked over, surprised at first, but then she smiled, soft and a little sleepy. That kind of smile that cracked something open inside Agatha’s chest.

She brought Rio’s hand to her lips and pressed a kiss to her knuckles—slow, reverent.

And right then, right between them, something shimmered in the dim interior of the car.

A soft blue light, like moonlight caught in petals.

Agatha glanced down.

A single blue dandelion had bloomed from the cup holder—fresh and impossible. The petals wide and glowing faintly, the stem curled delicately as if it had been waiting all this time to appear.

She blinked. Felt Rio still beside her, breath catching.

Neither of them said a word.

But between the warmth of their hands and the quiet miracle between them, something unspoken had already taken root.

And it was only just beginning to bloom.

~*~

They stepped into the warmth of Agatha’s home, brushing snow from their coats and shaking the cold from their bones. Agatha’s wards hummed softly in greeting, sensing something different in the air—something alive and golden.

She turned to Rio with a soft, expectant smile. “Tea? Or maybe a glass of that wine Wanda left behind. We can unwind a little…”

But Rio’s gaze was already on her—intense and aching in its focus.

“I just want you,” she said, quiet and clear.

It hit Agatha like a spell. Not lust—though that simmered under the surface—but something heavier, sweeter. A truth she wasn’t sure she could name.

Her breath caught, and she took a step forward, cupping Rio’s face in both hands. Her fingers brushed along the strong lines of her jaw, the soft flush in her cheeks. She kissed her—slowly, reverently—as if the universe might fold in on itself if she didn’t do it exactly right.

Rio’s hands found her hips, pulling her close, and they moved together like gravity had never applied to anyone else.

Agatha didn’t bother leading her to the bedroom. She simply walked them backward until the couch caught behind Rio’s knees and guided her down, sinking with her, surrounding her, holding her. They undressed each other with gentle urgency—no frantic pulling, no reckless need. Just patience. Just hunger drawn out into something holy.

Agatha kissed her everywhere—temple, neck, breast, stomach—everyplace Rio had ever carried tension, doubt, pain. She kissed it all away. Her hands moved like she was learning a hymn, a prayer carved into skin and sighs.

“Tell me if it’s too much,” she whispered, resting her forehead against Rio’s.

“It’s not enough,” Rio breathed, voice cracking around the edges. “Don’t stop.”

So she didn’t.

They moved together slowly, achingly, like a dance too old for music. Their breaths synced, soft moans spilling into the silence. The couch creaked under them, the fire flickered low, and the whole world narrowed to skin and touch and breath and this .

This unfathomable connection between them.

The moment they reached their peak—when Agatha felt Rio fall apart beneath her, and she followed not a breath later—a thunderclap cracked above them, loud and sudden, making the walls tremble. Light exploded around them, pouring from their joined hands, their mouths, their hearts. Every inch of their bodies glowed—brilliant white-gold, then blue, then violet like the wildflowers that bloomed when they touched.

The room was alight with it. Pure, radiant magic, rushing from the space between their bodies as if the universe had been waiting for them to mean it.

And this time, they did.

It wasn’t just sex—not like the times before, not even close. Those times had been desperate, beautiful, charged. But this—this was something else entirely. They were making love. Neither of them dared say the words yet, but their bodies knew. Their magic knew.

And maybe… maybe that was enough. For now.

When the light finally softened, fading into a candlelit hush, Agatha collapsed gently onto Rio’s chest. Her heart was thudding, her skin damp, her limbs trembling in that pleasant, aching way that only came with being undone by someone you’d tried so hard not to fall for.

Rio’s fingers threaded through her hair, and Agatha pressed a kiss to her collarbone, eyes fluttering closed.

For a long while, they just breathed.

And in the quiet, with the storm still rolling softly overhead, Agatha let herself imagine what it might be like to keep choosing this. To wake up beside Rio every morning, to fall asleep knowing she was loved even when the words hadn’t yet been spoken aloud.

Maybe one day.

For now, this was everything.

~*~

They stayed tangled on the couch, wrapped in the softest silence, limbs loosely intertwined and skin still humming from the aftershocks of what they’d just shared. The room smelled like sex and cedarwood, like firelight and lavender and something new—something unnamed but thick in the air between them.

Agatha ran her fingers lazily along the slope of Rio’s bare shoulder, watching the way the other woman’s chest rose and fell in slow, contented breaths. She didn’t want to move. Didn’t want to shift even an inch away from this moment.

But then Rio stirred, just slightly, and murmured, “So… that was new.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh against her skin. “The thunder? Or the fact that we nearly lit my entire living room on fire?”

Rio tilted her head just enough to meet her eyes, a crooked smile forming. “Both.”

Agatha smiled back and pressed a gentle kiss to her shoulder. “I’ve never had magic react like that before. Not like that.”

“It felt like…” Rio hesitated, searching for words. “Like the magic knew exactly what was happening. Like it was responding to… us.”

Agatha nodded slowly. “It was. It is.” Her voice dipped into something quieter, more honest. “We’re connected. We always have been. But this—tonight—I think it was the first time we let it happen without holding anything back.”

Rio exhaled, eyes softening. “It didn’t feel scary this time. Just… right.”

“And powerful,” Agatha added, nudging her playfully with her nose. “Very, very powerful.”

“I think we triggered a minor weather event.”

“I know we did.”

They both laughed then—light and unguarded—and it felt like the perfect release. The magic might’ve cracked like thunder, but here, in the aftermath, everything was soft.

“I will say,” Rio murmured, “your training is seriously helping. Wanda’s too. I feel a lot more in control now.”

Agatha raised a brow, clearly impressed. “No accidental flower storms this week?”

“None,” Rio said proudly. “Unless you count the one I caused in your damn cup holder when you held my hand.”

“Oh, that one was sweet,” Agatha teased. “Blue dandelions. You’re such a romantic, Vidal.”

Rio grinned and brushed a lock of hair from Agatha’s cheek. “Couldn’t help it. You were glowing.”

Agatha leaned in and kissed her again—quick and soft and utterly irresistible.

Eventually, she groaned dramatically. “Okay. As much as I’d love to stay here and risk fusing to this couch forever, we should probably move to an actual bed. You know, the thing with pillows and blankets and fewer risks of lower back pain.”

“Ugh. But I like your couch,” Rio teased.

Agatha sat up slowly, grabbing the throw blanket to wrap around her as she stood, and reached out a hand. “Come on. I’ll even let you steal my side of the bed.”

Rio took her hand and let herself be pulled up, stumbling slightly as they laughed their way through discarded clothing and into the hallway.

“You say that like there’s a designated side already,” Rio teased.

“There wasn’t,” Agatha said over her shoulder, “until I started imagining you in it.”

Rio paused just long enough in the doorway to blink at her—and Agatha caught the flicker of something in her eyes. Surprise, affection, and a little bit of that wonder she never tried too hard to hide.

Then they crossed into the bedroom together, bare feet on soft rugs, and the rest of the world melted away again. They didn’t rush. Didn’t need to. They just slipped beneath the covers, laughing as Agatha fought with the too-fluffy duvet and Rio shivered against the cold sheets before snuggling close.

Agatha pulled her in, arms tight around her waist, nose buried in her hair.

It was quiet.

Safe.

Sweet.

And as the moonlight spilled silver across the room, she whispered against Rio’s temple, “You’re not just magic, you know. You’re mine.”

Rio sighed sleepily, a smile in her voice. “Good.”

Then they drifted off, skin warm against skin, heartbeat against heartbeat—no spells, no sparks, no thunderstorms this time. Just peace.

~*~

The dream unfolded gently at first.

Agatha was a child again, no older than eight or nine, her small fingers stained with crushed herbs and moss. Her mother’s voice guided her through the steps of a spell, slow and melodic, like a lullaby. They were in the woods, sunlight dappling through the canopy above, the scent of damp earth and honeysuckle sweet on the breeze. The lake nearby rippled quietly, reflecting the sky in shards of mirrored light.

Evanora stood tall and radiant, her long dark hair braided with bits of lavender and ivy. Her hands moved with practiced ease, lighting the air with tiny sparks as she showed Agatha how to draw energy from the soil beneath their feet. “It’s not about forcing it,” she said softly. “It’s about listening. The earth will always speak to you, if you let it.”

Young Agatha had nodded with rapt attention, mimicking the motion of her mother’s hands, feeling the gentle pulse of something ancient and kind under her skin.

For a moment, everything was perfect.

And then, something shifted.

The warmth drained from the light. The air thickened with silence. The child’s body was no longer her own. Agatha blinked, and when she looked down, she saw her adult hands trembling faintly.

Her mother was still there, but she was older now. Haggard. Her dress torn and damp with mud, strands of gray stark against her dark hair. Her eyes, once so calm and kind, were wild now, sharp with warning. Her hands trembled as she reached for Agatha’s face.

“Nezzera,” Evanora whispered, like it was both a prayer and a curse. “It’s coming.”

Agatha frowned. “What are you talking about?”

“We thought it was bound. We thought it was locked away.” Her voice broke, her breath ragged. “But it’s waking. The balance is shifting. You have to be ready, Agatha.”

“Ready for what?”

Evanora cupped her face with both hands, pulling her close, eyes wide and filled with something that looked like fear. “You need to align. With the others. With her.” Her gaze flicked behind Agatha for a split second—toward the lake, or something beyond it. “You need control. You need each other.”

Agatha’s heartbeat echoed in her ears.

“Who is Nezzera?”

Her mother didn’t answer. She just pressed their foreheads together and whispered, “It’s coming. It’s coming. It’s coming.”

A flash of cold wind surged through the trees. The lake darkened like spilled ink. The sound of something enormous shifting beneath the surface shattered the silence.

And Agatha woke with a gasp, her hand clutching the sheets, the echo of her mother’s voice still ringing in her ears.

It’s coming.

 

Chapter 19: Nineteen

The soft rustle of sheets and the quiet scratch of a pen pulled Rio from sleep.

She blinked against the dim light, disoriented for a breath or two before her eyes found Agatha—sitting upright in bed, back tense, her breath quick like she’d been running. Her hair was a wild halo around her shoulders, and in her lap was a leather-bound notebook. 

Agatha was writing furiously, hand moving like she was racing against time.

Rio’s brow furrowed. She pushed up on one elbow, her voice still rough from sleep. “Hey… what’s going on?”

Agatha didn’t look at her, just raised one hand in a quiet plea. “Just—just a second,” she murmured. “I have to get this down before it slips.”

Rio nodded sleepily, concern creeping beneath the haze of drowsiness. She shifted closer, pressing a kiss to Agatha’s bare shoulder. Her skin was warm but taut, like a storm had just passed through her. Rio’s fingers moved slowly, gently, tracing circles against her back.

She waited.

The only sound in the room was the quick scratching of pen to paper and Agatha’s still-uneven breaths.

After a few minutes, Agatha finally lowered the pen and let out a long, trembling exhale. She stared at the page like it had answers she wasn’t ready for. Rio reached up, brushing a lock of hair behind Agatha’s ear.

“Are you okay?” she asked softly, her voice low in the stillness between them.

Agatha’s eyes flicked to hers, and for the briefest second, Rio saw it—something like fear. Or awe. Maybe both.

Agatha stared at the grimoire on her lap like it might disappear if she blinked. Her hand was still curled around the pen, knuckles pale, but she’d stopped writing. Her chest rose and fell in shallow breaths as she tried to anchor herself back in the waking world.

Rio watched her closely, concern sharpening the sleep from her eyes. “Agatha?” she murmured again, sitting up fully now, hand resting warm and steady against the curve of Agatha’s back. “What happened?”

Agatha didn’t answer right away. Her gaze stayed locked on the page, as if the dream were still lingering there, echoing through the ink.

Then, quietly—almost like it hurt to say—she spoke. “That was the first time I’ve dreamed of her in nearly twenty years.”

Rio’s heart twisted. “Your mother?”

Agatha nodded, and the smallest tremor passed through her. “Not a memory. Not some half-dream where she’s just a shadow. This was her. I could smell the lake. I could feel the wind in the trees. She looked… like she did when I was younger. Before she disappeared.”

Rio shifted closer, brushing her thumb along the base of Agatha’s spine in slow, grounding circles. “What did she say?”

Agatha drew a shaky breath. “She was teaching me magic. We were in the woods, standing near the water, and everything felt… safe. Peaceful. Like when I was a child and she’d sneak me out before dawn to collect dew for potions. I didn’t want to wake up.”

Her voice broke on that last word, raw and honest.

Rio leaned in, pressing her forehead gently against Agatha’s temple, whispering, “I’m here.”

Agatha closed her eyes. “But then she changed. Got older—worn. She looked like she’d lived through something terrible. Her hands were shaking when she took my face in them.” She paused, swallowing. “She warned me. Said something was coming. She called it Nezzera. She said we needed to be ready. That we had to align. That we needed control.”

Rio’s brow furrowed, the word foreign and heavy with meaning. “Have you ever heard of that before?”

“No.” Agatha let out a humorless breath. “And that terrifies me.”

Rio gently took the pen from her hand and set it on the nightstand with the notebook, then opened her arms and tugged her down into the blankets. “C’mere. You don’t have to sit up alone with this.”

Agatha hesitated for just a second, then let herself be pulled into Rio’s warmth. Her limbs were stiff, her breath still uneven, but Rio tucked her close, wrapping her up as if she could shield her from the dream entirely.

They lay there in silence for a moment, Rio’s fingers stroking slowly through her hair.

“You’re safe,” Rio murmured into the crown of her head. “Whatever it is, we’ll figure it out. Together.”

Agatha let out a breath, one that sounded more like surrender than fear, and shifted closer, burying her face in Rio’s shoulder.

“I’ve spent most of my life trying to forget her,” she whispered. “Trying not to need her.”

“I know,” Rio said gently, brushing her lips over Agatha’s forehead. “But maybe now… maybe it’s time to remember. On your terms.”

Silence again. Then Agatha exhaled, long and quiet, finally starting to melt into the curve of Rio’s body.

“Let’s just stay like this,” Rio said, kissing her again. “You can tell me everything when you’re ready. But right now, just be here. With me.”

And slowly, breath by breath, Agatha let herself be held—past and future suspended for just a little while longer.

~*~

Rio stayed still, one arm curled around Agatha’s waist, the other folded under her head as she stared into the quiet dark of the bedroom. She felt the shift when Agatha’s breathing finally slowed, when the tension that had clung to her like a second skin since waking began to melt away. The steady rise and fall of her chest, the subtle weight of her body relaxing into Rio’s — it was the only sign she needed to know she was asleep again.

Rio let out a long breath of her own, soft enough not to disturb her. Her forehead rested lightly against Agatha’s shoulder as her mind whirred restlessly, loud in the stillness.

Nezzera.

The word rang in her head like a bell tolling in the distance, a name with no shape but too much weight. She had no idea what it meant, but the way Agatha had clung to it — the way she’d shaken — made Rio’s stomach twist. Agatha, who always seemed so perfectly in control, who could summon calm with the arch of an eyebrow, had looked almost frightened when she spoke of it.

And that scared Rio more than anything.

What if it was connected to that creepy folklorist who had shown up last week, all smiles and strange questions, poking around town under the guise of research? What if it had to do with the shift in her own magic — her powers that were now awake and electric under her skin, humming louder with each passing day?

She was getting more used to the sensation, sure, but most of the time it still felt like walking around with a lit match pressed to her palm. Something always on the verge of flaring too bright, too fast. Even now, lying still, she could feel the soft buzz beneath her ribs. Not painful, just… restless. Like something waiting to be used.

She looked down at Agatha — beautiful, brilliant, powerful Agatha — and gently brushed a curl away from her cheek. She didn’t want to wake her, not after the night she’d had. But god, she wished she had answers. Or a way to fix it. Or even just a name to go with the fear sitting in her chest.

They needed to figure out what the hell Nezzera was. Before it found them first.

Thunder cracked low and distant, a slow roll that rattled the windows like a warning. Rio flinched. She hadn’t even realized she was holding her breath until the wind picked up outside, battering the house in sudden bursts like something was clawing at the eaves. Her stomach dropped.

Not again.

It had taken her a minute to recognize it—this creeping sensation like the world was responding to her mood. But now that she knew, it was hard to ignore. She was spiraling, full-on panicking in the quiet dark of Agatha’s room, and the damn weather had the nerve to echo it back at her.

“Great,” she muttered, pressing the heels of her palms to her eyes. “Perfect. I’m basically a human barometer with anxiety issues.”

The wind howled again.

She gritted her teeth and shifted a bit in bed, grounding herself with a long, slow breath. Then another. She counted them like Wanda had taught her—inhale for four, hold for four, exhale for six. Over and over. She focused on the way the sheets felt under her fingertips, the sound of Agatha’s steady breathing beside her, the warmth still lingering on the pillow.

Eventually, her heart stopped trying to leap out of her chest. The wind outside began to calm. The thunder faded into silence.

Okay. Okay, better.

She didn’t even remember drifting off again. One moment she was watching the curtains settle, the next she was blinking blearily into sunlight streaming through the windows.

Agatha was gone.

Rio sat up slowly, rubbing the sleep from her eyes. The bed was still warm beside her, but empty. For a second, she panicked again, but then—there. The smell of coffee drifting in through the open door. The gentle clink of ceramic and glass. Agatha was downstairs.

Relief spread through her like honey.

She stretched, legs tangling in the covers, then padded to the wardrobe to grab whatever was closest. Her fingers found a flowy robe in a rich, floral purple that was unmistakably Agatha’s. Rio wrapped it around herself like armor.

She made her way downstairs on quiet feet, the wood cool under her toes. The soft sounds from the kitchen grew louder—something sizzling faintly, the kettle clicking off, Agatha humming low and sweet under her breath.

And just like that, the storm inside her eased for real.

The kitchen was warm with morning light, soft golden rays slanting through the windows and catching on the copper pans that hung above the stove. Rio stopped in the doorway, barefoot and tangled in Agatha’s robe, her breath catching the second her eyes landed on the woman standing by the counter.

Agatha was murmuring quietly to Mr. Scratchy as she fed him, her voice soft, affectionate in a way she rarely used with people. Her hair was still a little tousled from sleep, curling slightly at the ends, and she wore an oversized cream sweater that slipped off one shoulder as she leaned down to scratch behind the rabbit’s ear. The gentle smile on her face was the kind Rio had only seen a handful of times—unguarded, private, real.

And it hit her like a freight train.

This woman. This gorgeous, impossible, powerful woman—she was hers. Not in the possessive way, not in the way you stake a claim, but in the way two people choose each other. The way the world cracks open and makes room for something too big, too bright to be ignored.

Agatha Harkness was hers, and Rio was so stupidly, helplessly, hopelessly in love with her she could barely tell up from down anymore.

The rush of feeling was so sudden, so overwhelming that she staggered back half a step, clutching at her chest like she could physically hold the emotion in.

It was too much.

Too much.

And then, with a soft whoosh, half a dozen azaleas bloomed in her hands.

Blush pink, delicate and sweet, the petals opened like tiny hearts unfurling, catching the sunlight in their folds.

Rio blinked down at them, stunned.

Agatha turned at the soft gasp, eyebrows lifting slightly when she saw her.

“Well,” she said, amused, walking over slowly. “Looks like someone’s powers are feeling a little sentimental this morning.”

Rio just stared at her, flowers trembling in her palms, her heart aching with how much she loved her.

“Yeah,” she whispered. “Something like that.”

Rio took a breath—slow, deep, shaky. Her fingers curled around the stems of the azaleas, still impossibly fresh, their petals trembling with the last shiver of magic. It was almost laughable, how hard her heart was pounding, how breathless she felt over a moment that had no warning, no build-up. Just her body betraying what her heart had been screaming for days.

She crossed the kitchen in a few quiet steps, holding the small bouquet out between them like an offering.

“My lady,” she said, aiming for playful, but her voice was too soft, too full.

Agatha’s expression shifted, her eyes going soft in that way that always made Rio feel like the only person in the world. She reached out and took the flowers with careful fingers, lifting them to her face to breathe them in. “Well, aren’t you a romantic,” she murmured, lips twitching. “Flowers before breakfast?”

Rio gave her a half-smile, brushing her knuckles gently down Agatha’s bare arm. “Just what happens when I think too hard about you feeding your rabbit in the morning light. Apparently I’m not emotionally stable enough for that level of domestic bliss.”

Agatha laughed under her breath, quiet and warm, before her eyes searched Rio’s face again—really searched it. “Hey,” she said softly, “how are you doing?”

Rio blinked. “Me?”

“You had a front row seat to my midnight breakdown,” Agatha said, wry but tender. “I figured I should return the favor.”

Rio hesitated, then let her hands find Agatha’s waist, drawing her in just a little closer. “I was more worried about you. After that dream, after what your mom said…”

Agatha’s smile dimmed slightly, but only for a breath. “I’m okay,” she said. “Still rattled. But having you there… it helped. A lot.”

She reached up, cradled Rio’s cheek with one hand, the other still holding the flowers.

Then, just like that, she kissed her—slow and deep, a morning kiss that felt like everything. Like gratitude, like grounding, like I see you and I want you here. Her hand slid around the back of Rio’s neck, holding her close as if she couldn’t quite stand the distance of even an inch between them.

When they parted, their foreheads rested together, breath mingling.

“Good morning,” Agatha whispered.

Rio smiled, finally settling into her skin. “Yeah,” she breathed. “It really is.”

Agatha pulled back just enough to grab a pan off the stove, flipping something that sizzled pleasantly—eggs, maybe, or the start of an omelet. “Okay, so I’m thinking breakfast sandwiches,” she said over her shoulder. “I’ve got fresh sourdough, eggs, a little leftover kale, and I can melt that nice sharp cheddar I know you like—”

She moved like a storm in a teacup, precise but kinetic, her robe swishing at her ankles and hair loosely pinned at the back of her head. Mr. Scratchy sat at her feet, now thoroughly fed and watching her with a kind of rabbit reverence.

“And I’ll need to open the shop by ten. I promised Mrs. Halberg I’d restock her tinctures, and the Pendle twins are picking up that custom salve for their grandmother. Oh, and I’m almost out of valerian root, which means I’ll have to go up to Portland next week unless the supplier magically decides to restock earlier, which he never does. So that’s going to be a day trip, maybe two—”

Rio leaned against the counter, just watching her, the corner of her mouth twitching.

“—and we really need to talk to Wanda about the dream. About Nezzera, whatever the hell that is. I was thinking maybe tonight we could have dinner and start figuring it out? I mean, not like it’s going to be an easy Google search, and I don’t even know where to begin, but—”

Agatha turned to grab plates and Rio moved in. With a soft, purposeful tug, she wrapped both arms around Agatha’s waist, stopping her mid-sentence. Agatha blinked, startled by the contact and the sudden stillness.

Rio leaned in and pressed a gentle kiss to her lips, slow and grounding.

“Breathe,” she murmured against her mouth.

Agatha’s hands stilled on the edge of the counter. Her body relaxed by degrees, tension leaking from her like steam. She let her forehead fall against Rio’s, her eyes slipping shut with a breath that came easier this time.

“You’re right,” she said, voice quieter now. “I just… I don’t like not knowing. It makes my skin itch.”

Rio smiled softly, fingers tracing soothing circles at the small of her back. “We’ll figure it out. One thing at a time. And if we’re having those breakfast sandwiches, I call dibs on the crispy edge of the cheddar.”

That earned a breathy laugh, warm and real. “Deal,” Agatha said, and for the first time that morning, she sounded like she believed it too.

~*~

 

Rio kept her fingers laced with Agatha’s all the way from the house to the apothecary, and it was impossible not to feel the quiet pride swelling in her chest. She didn’t want to let go of her hand. Not just because of how warm and familiar it felt, but because it was important. Holding Agatha’s hand like this, in public, in broad daylight—it mattered. Even if it was just a sleepy Monday morning in a town that still smelled like firewood and pine needles. 

It mattered.

But she felt the shift almost immediately.

A few people glanced their way longer than they should’ve. A man walking his dog frowned in that subtle, tight-lipped way that didn’t scream disapproval, but didn’t bother to hide it either. Two older women paused their conversation outside the bakery as they passed, their words trailing off mid-sentence. Rio caught the glance, then the quick whisper.

It wasn’t new. It wasn’t shocking. She’d grown up with this, bristled against it, learned how to steel herself against it. But something about feeling it here—in Thistle Grove, where she’d started to feel safe—hit different. It scratched under her skin.

Agatha clearly noticed. Her thumb rubbed over the back of Rio’s hand gently, her own voice low and calm. “Ignore them,” she said without missing a step. “It’s just the usual handful of crusty homophobes. They’ve always been here. They’ll always be here. Don’t let them in.”

Rio nodded, but her eyes flicked around again. It wasn’t just the glances. There was something else. Something colder, like a shadow trailing just out of sight.

She couldn’t name it, but it stuck in her chest like a thorn.

When they reached the apothecary, Agatha pulled her into a quick kiss at the door, her hand warm at Rio’s jaw. “I’ll see you later, okay?”

Rio nodded again, but she lingered, eyes flicking around the cobbled street one more time. “Yeah,” she said. “Later.”

She kissed her again, softer this time, then let go.

Once Agatha disappeared behind the green-and-gold door of the shop, Rio pulled out her phone and sent a quick text to Alice.

Rio

meet me at the hollow? need coffee and your face. 

She pocketed her phone and started walking, her boots crunching against the frosty path, the weight of the strange feeling still pressing at the base of her spine like the whisper of a storm just over the hill.

~*~

 

Alice stepped into The Hollow like she owned the place, brushing snowflakes off her coat as she scanned the tables. Rio caught her eye from the back corner and gave a small wave, already nursing her second coffee of the morning. No sign of Lilia—just the teenage girl who sometimes helped out behind the counter, earbuds in and barely sparing Rio a glance when she’d handed over the mug earlier.

Alice made her way over with that familiar bounce in her step, dropping into the seat across from her with a little grin that said I know exactly what I’m walking into.

“So,” she began, dragging the word out as she leaned her elbows on the table. “How was your night with the enchantress?”

Rio groaned. “God, don’t call her that.”

Alice just raised her brows and tilted her head, waiting.

Rio tried to keep the smirk off her face but failed miserably. “It was good.”

“Mmhmm. Good, she says.” Alice leaned in. “You’re glowing, you know. It’s annoying.”

Rio laughed under her breath, cheeks burning. She wrapped her hands tighter around the warm mug, staring at the swirl of cream still settling at the top. For a second, she thought about changing the subject—about keeping this thing just for herself a little while longer. But then the words pushed up through her throat before she could stop them.

“I love her, Al.”

It came out quiet, but steady. A truth she hadn’t meant to voice out loud, but now that it was hanging there between them, she couldn’t pretend it wasn’t real. Her heart thudded hard in her chest. She lifted her eyes slowly to meet Alice’s across the table.

Alice blinked. “Oh.”

Rio gave a shaky smile. “Yeah.”

“Wow,” Alice said, voice softer now. “You okay?”

Rio let out a long breath. “I think so? I don’t know. It hit me this morning like a train. I was watching her feed Mr. Scratchy and I just—” she shook her head, overwhelmed at the memory, “—it felt like my chest couldn’t hold it anymore.”

Alice’s expression softened, all playfulness gone. “And what are you gonna do with all that love, huh?”

Rio huffed a laugh, blinking back the ridiculous sting in her eyes. “I have no idea.”

But deep down, she thought maybe she did.

Rio’s eyes prickled a little, the kind of sting that always came with being seen—really seen—by someone who knew her to the core.

Alice squeezed her hand again, thumb brushing gently over her knuckles. “For what it’s worth, I’m really happy for you, Rio.”

Rio blinked, looked at her best friend, and tried not to crumble into emotional goo on the spot.

Alice went on, softer now. “I mean it. I’ve seen you go through a lot of crap. And after stupid Carol—God, don’t get me started—”

Rio let out a snort despite herself. “Yeah, I still don’t know what I was thinking.”

“You weren’t,” Alice said dryly. “You were in love with the idea of her. Not the actual self-centered trainwreck.”

“Harsh,” Rio said, even as a smile tugged at her lips. “But fair.”

“But this,” Alice continued, leaning forward again, eyes lit with something more earnest now, “this is different. I knew the second I met Agatha—even if it was just over FaceTime, and she looked like she wanted to hex me for interrupting your night—that this wasn’t just a fling. She looked at you like you were the whole damn moon.”

Rio’s breath caught.

“And you?” Alice added, “You looked back like you finally remembered what it felt like to be wanted. Not used. Not tolerated. Wanted.”

Rio had to look away for a second, swallowing around the lump in her throat. “She makes me feel like… like there’s more of me than I ever thought there was.”

Alice smiled so softly it made something ache in Rio’s chest.

“Then hold on to that,” she said. “Because that ? That’s real.”

Rio wiped quickly at her eyes, laughing under her breath as she sniffled. “God, I’m pathetic.”

Alice handed her a napkin with a gentle smirk. “You’re not pathetic. You’re in love. It’s disgusting. I’m thrilled.”

That pulled another watery laugh out of her, and she leaned back in her seat, crumpling the napkin in her hand. The Hollow buzzed softly around them, the clinking of mugs and low conversation filling in the quiet spaces. It was cozy, safe—but Rio still glanced around before she spoke again, her voice softer now.

“I’ve gotten used to having you here,” she said, eyes dropping to her half-empty coffee mug. “I don’t want you to go.”

Alice tilted her head with a little smile. “I’m not gone yet.”

“I know,” Rio said, then hesitated. Her fingers tightened slightly around the mug. “There’s something else.”

Alice’s eyebrows lifted a little, but she stayed quiet, giving her the space to keep going.

Rio lowered her voice even more, eyes flicking around the room just to be sure no one was close enough to really hear. “Agatha had a dream last night. About her mom. It was… intense.”

Alice leaned in. “What kind of dream?”

“She said she hadn’t dreamed of her in like over twenty years. But last night, her mom was there. Said something was coming. Something called Nezzera.” The name alone sent a strange tingle down her spine.

Alice frowned, sitting back slightly. “That sounds… made up and ominous.”

Rio nodded. “That’s the vibe. And the way it shook Agatha—I’ve never seen her like that. She’s always so composed. But after the dream? She looked terrified.”

“And you don’t know what it is? This Nezzera thing?”

“No idea,” Rio whispered, then added, “I shouldn’t even be talking about this out in the open. I just… needed to tell someone.”

Alice’s eyes softened. “You can always tell me. You know that.”

Rio gave her a grateful look, reaching for her hand again across the table. “I know.”

And for a moment, in the quiet safety of her best friend’s presence, the weight in her chest didn’t feel quite so heavy.

~*~

The sun had barely dipped below the horizon when they gathered once again behind Wanda’s house, the clearing bathed in the silvery glow of a near-full moon. A ring of protective wards shimmered faintly at the edges of the woods, pulsing softly like a heartbeat. Snow had begun to fall again, light and slow, dusting the trees and turning the ground into a quiet canvas of white.

Rio tugged her coat tighter as she stepped into the clearing. Alice was already curled up near the firepit, swaddled in scarves and sipping from a thermos. Agatha stood a few paces away, looking beautifully unreadable, her arms crossed and her gaze sharp as it flicked between Rio and Wanda.

It was Wanda who broke the silence.

“Gloves off, Vidal,” she called, already walking toward the center of the clearing with her staff in hand. “We’re not playing around anymore.”

Rio blinked, caught a little off guard. “Wow, okay. Intense tonight, huh?”

Agatha stepped beside her, tone dry. “She’s been like this all day?”

Rio’s stomach dropped. “You told her about the dream?”

Agatha nodded once. “Had to.”

Wanda didn’t even try to sugarcoat it. “A premonition from Evanora isn’t something we take lightly. If she’s warning us about something called Nezzera, and she appeared in your dream like that… well, that’s the universe telling us to get our asses moving.”

“So…” Rio started slowly, eyeing Wanda’s stance. “What does that mean for me?”

“It means,” Wanda said, already rolling up her sleeves, “you’re not just learning how to defend anymore. You’re learning how to strike. If something’s coming, we’re not going to just wait around and hope it goes away. You need to be ready.”

“She’s right,” Agatha added quietly, her voice lower now, just for Rio. “You’ve come so far already. But I don’t think this is going to stop unless we push forward.”

Rio looked at them both—Wanda, crackling with unrelenting fire, and Agatha, steady and grounding beside her. Her heart was still fluttering from what she and Agatha had shared the night before, but this was different. Bigger. Scarier.

Still, she pulled off her gloves, letting the magic at her fingertips meet the cold air like a slow-burning ember.

“Alright,” she said, jaw set. “Let’s see what I’ve got.”

And just like that, the training began—with more intensity than ever before.

~*~

Wanda started with sharp, focused drills—projectile deflection, burst shields, reflex enchantments. She didn’t pull her punches, sending actual kinetic pulses at Rio, who fumbled the first two but managed to throw up a barrier just in time to absorb the third. It crackled gold and green around her, flickering at the edges like it wasn’t sure what shape it wanted to take.

“That’s better,” Wanda said with a grudging nod. “Again.”

They ran the sequence three more times. Rio’s form improved with each attempt, her footing more grounded, her reactions quicker. But she was breathing hard by the end, magic buzzing wild in her bloodstream.

Agatha had been quiet, watching from the edges, but now she stepped forward.

“That’s enough for a moment,” she told Wanda, who didn’t argue but arched a brow like she’d be counting the seconds. Agatha turned to Rio. “You’re burning too hot. You need to learn how to pull it back in before it explodes on its own.”

Rio nodded, still catching her breath. “I know. It feels like it’s just—always there. Right under the surface.”

“I know the feeling,” Agatha murmured. She stepped closer, held out her hands. “Can I?”

Rio nodded and placed her hands in Agatha’s. A warm current immediately passed between them, steadier than before. Agatha’s eyes fluttered shut as she took a breath, centering them both.

“Your magic’s like a storm,” she said softly. “But storms don’t have to destroy. They can shift the air, bring rain to starving roots, wash away the rot.”

“Poetic,” Wanda muttered in the background.

Agatha ignored her. “Try this,” she continued, eyes opening and locking with Rio’s. “Focus on my voice. Let the magic settle behind your ribs—not in your hands, not in your throat. Here.” She guided Rio’s hands to rest over her sternum.

Rio did as she said, closing her eyes, focusing on the thrum of power pulsing in her chest. She imagined it coiling, tightening, pulling back like a tide instead of crashing like a wave.

“Good,” Agatha whispered, her fingers brushing over Rio’s wrists. “Now, when you exhale, let it go—but only a thread. Just a flicker.”

Rio exhaled slowly, and a faint gold glow shimmered between her palms—a soft, gentle pulse instead of the uncontrolled sparks from before.

Agatha smiled, pride blooming across her face. “There. That’s it.”

“Damn,” Rio whispered. “I actually… did that?”

“You did,” Agatha said, squeezing her hands. “And you’re only getting stronger.”

Wanda clapped once, teasing, but firm. “Alright, golden girls. Back to business.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but stepped aside, giving Rio one last smile. “I’m not going anywhere.”

And just like that, they picked up again—this time, with Rio a little steadier on her feet, her power a little more her own.

Wanda threw them into partnered combat drills next—nothing too serious, just a few structured sequences meant to train Rio’s reaction time and instinctual casting. And because Agatha was the best partner to push her without breaking her, Wanda handed Rio off with a wink and a “Have fun, kids,” before retreating to the other side of the garden with a glass of something suspiciously red.

Agatha arched a brow as she faced Rio, drawing two short wooden staffs from the stack by the wall. “I know you’re a soft-hearted plant witch, but tonight you’re going to try and knock me on my ass.”

Rio smirked, taking the staff. “You say that like I haven’t wanted to do that since the day we met.”

Agatha laughed, genuinely and without walls, and Rio felt the sound run through her like sunlight. “Then show me what you’ve got, Vidal.”

They began to spar—not with full force, but enough that it took effort, concentration. Agatha moved like a dancer, precise and sharp, and Rio did her best to match her, fueled more by instinct than training. But something had shifted. She wasn’t just reacting anymore—she was reading Agatha. Her movements, her energy. She could feel the tension in the air a second before a strike, sense the hum of magic as it shifted through her opponent’s limbs.

They danced in a slow, charged circle, magic sparking faintly around their hands.

“Focus,” Agatha murmured, her voice low. “Not just on me—on you. Don’t forget who you are.”

Rio narrowed her eyes, swept low, and caught Agatha off guard with a burst of vines that sprung up from the grass and tangled around her ankles. Agatha stumbled, and Rio grinned in victory for all of two seconds—until Agatha snapped her fingers and the vines withered into ash, and she spun Rio off balance with a flick of her wrist.

They both went down—Agatha landing atop her with a grunt and a laugh, their breaths mingling in the quiet that followed.

“Well,” Agatha said, a little breathless. “That was mildly humiliating.”

Rio laughed, heart pounding from more than just exertion. “You let me win.”

“I let you almost win.”

They stayed like that for a moment, the sound of the night all around them—crickets, the soft rustling of leaves, the distant hoot of an owl. Then Agatha shifted just slightly, brushing Rio’s hair from her forehead.

“You’re getting good,” she said, serious now.

“I have good teachers,” Rio replied, smiling.

Wanda’s voice cut through the moment like a knife. “Alright, break it up, lovebirds! Save it for after you figure out how to dodge without falling all over each other!”

Agatha groaned and rolled off her, offering a hand to pull her up. “She’s insufferable when she’s right.”

Rio took her hand, still smiling. “Guess we’ll just have to show her what we’re made of.”

They got back up, dusted themselves off, and fell into position again—tired, sweaty, a little bruised, but both of them smiling in that quiet, powerful way that said we’re not done yet.

They ramped things up as the moon climbed higher. Wanda had insisted it was time to push Rio past her comfort zone, and Agatha—though clearly reluctant—agreed with a clipped nod.

“You said you wanted to be ready,” Wanda said, stretching her arms and cracking her neck. “Now you’re going to learn what it feels like to be outnumbered. We’ll take it easy on you.” Her grin was all teeth. “At first.”

Rio swallowed, adjusting her stance. “Define easy.”

“Still breathing,” Agatha quipped, but her tone was dry, careful. She glanced at Wanda, then back at Rio. “We’ll go slow, darling. Just remember to ground yourself. You’re stronger than you know.”

The air crackled between them as both witches circled her. Wanda struck first, a wave of red magic like a whip that Rio barely dodged. Agatha followed immediately with a flick of her fingers that sent a shock of air toward her chest. Rio instinctively summoned a wall of vines, shielding herself, but they evaporated under Wanda’s next burst.

It became a dance, one Rio was just barely keeping up with. She could feel her power rising in her chest like a tide, fast and furious, and every block, every counterstrike made it surge higher.

“Breathe!” Agatha called, voice sharper now. “You’re pushing too hard—”

But Rio couldn’t slow it down. Her vision blurred, her heart thudded in her ears, and when Wanda sent a stronger bolt of magic her way, Rio didn’t even think. She threw both hands forward, screaming inside with the force of it, and a pulse of magic erupted from her like a wave.

It wasn’t just wind. It wasn’t just light.

It was raw power.

Both Agatha and Wanda were thrown back—Agatha managing to shield herself mid-air, but Wanda hit the ground hard and rolled to a stop, groaning.

“Wanda!” Agatha cried, already on her knees beside her best friend, magic glowing golden and immediate as she pressed her hands gently over Wanda’s shoulder.

Rio’s heart plummeted. “Oh my God. I—I didn’t mean to—” She sprinted over, falling to her knees across from Agatha. “I didn’t know it would hit that hard. Is she—?”

“I’m fine,” Wanda said, breathless but smirking through a wince. “Just a little crispy around the edges. Someone’s been eating her magical Wheaties.”

But the joke didn’t land for Rio. Her hands were shaking. She stared at the small burn on Wanda’s shoulder, at the way Agatha’s magic stitched it back together with soft light.

“I’m so sorry,” she whispered. “I didn’t—”

“You did,” Agatha said, her voice gentle but steady. “And that’s good.”

Rio blinked, stunned.

“You’re not going to learn how to control it by being afraid of it,” Agatha said, her fingers never faltering as she worked. “You reacted to danger. You protected yourself. It wasn’t perfect—but it was powerful. And next time, it’ll be better.”

Wanda gave her a crooked grin. “Besides, if I had a nickel for every time I’ve been knocked on my ass by a young witch coming into her own, I’d have a whole damn coin purse.”

Rio huffed a laugh, still shaken. “You should’ve warned me.”

“We did,” Agatha and Wanda said in unison, then exchanged a look and rolled their eyes.

Rio sat back on her heels, exhaling slowly. She could still feel the power in her fingertips, buzzing like electricity under her skin. But now it came with something else too—a flicker of confidence. Of control.

Agatha touched her hand, just briefly, grounding her. “We’ll figure it out together. Okay?”

Rio nodded, finally letting herself believe it. “Okay.”

Wanda flexed her newly-healed shoulder, rotating it with an audible pop. “Well,” she said, dragging herself to her feet with a grunt, “that was bracing.”

Rio stared at her, wide-eyed. “You want to keep going?”

Wanda flashed her a wicked grin. “Damn right I do.”

“Wanda,” Agatha chided softly, though there was no real heat behind it. She helped Rio stand, brushing dirt from her arm with gentle fingers. “Maybe we should give her a minute—”

“Nope.” Wanda cracked her knuckles and rolled her neck, already back in stance. “She’s fine. Look at her—she’s buzzing like a live wire. The best way to learn is to do. And she needs to know she can land a hit without falling apart about it.”

Rio blinked at her. “You literally just got blown off your feet.”

“Which means,” Wanda said with an exaggerated shrug, “I better learn how to dodge faster.”

Agatha glanced at Rio, brow lifted in silent question.

Rio let out a long breath, fingers twitching as magic stirred inside her again. “Alright. Let’s go again.”

Wanda grinned. “Now that’s the spirit.”

~*~

Wanda lit the last of the candles on the kitchen table with a snap of her fingers, their golden glow flickering across the mismatched plates and bowls of charcuterie she’d thrown together—fig jam, rosemary crackers, slices of smoked gouda and Manchego, a pile of prosciutto, and olives glistening in oil and herbs. The wine was already flowing.

Agatha sat cross-legged at one end of the table, her elbow resting on the wood, fingers curled around a glass of red. Her eyes were distant, a crease between her brows as she swirled the wine but didn’t drink it. Rio sat beside her, still quietly buzzing from the training, her knees bruised and her power faintly pulsing under her skin like a restless tide. Wanda, across from them, looked the most relaxed of the three—even with a faint scuff mark on her shoulder.

“So,” Wanda said after a long sip of her wine, “Nezzera.”

The word settled over the table like a shadow.

Agatha finally took a sip, then nodded. “That’s what she said. My mother. In my dream. It didn’t feel like a memory—it felt like a warning.”

“And you’ve never heard that word before?” Wanda asked.

“Never.” Agatha’s voice was low, almost hesitant. “I checked every single magic book I own. Every single page of my Grimoire. Nothing.”

Rio leaned forward, her voice soft. “Could it be older than what’s recorded? Something suppressed, or forgotten on purpose?”

Wanda’s eyes narrowed slightly in thought. “Wouldn’t be the first time. The Watchers have a habit of sweeping the dangerous stuff under the rug, especially if it didn’t suit their tidy narratives.”

Agatha’s lips pressed into a tight line. “My mother told me we needed to align. That we needed control. That it’s coming.”

“That’s more than a warning,” Wanda said. “That’s a countdown.”

Rio reached for a slice of bread, mostly to have something to do with her hands. “So how do we figure out what it is before it shows up at our doorstep?”

Agatha looked at Wanda, then back at Rio. “We dig. We start with the Archives, and the personal grimoires of the Threads. We should talk to Lilia about access to the magic Archives. If this thing has a history, we’ll find it. And if not…”

“We start writing our own,” Wanda said.

Agatha nodded slowly. “Exactly.”

Rio raised her glass, her hand steady despite everything swirling inside her. “To digging up ghosts.”

Wanda smirked and clinked her glass against Rio’s. “To blowing them up if we have to.”

Agatha’s glass met theirs last, her smile soft, touched with something fierce. “To not facing any of it alone.”

They drank to that—quietly, reverently. The warmth of wine filled Rio’s chest, but it was the shared glances, the strength of the moment, that truly grounded her. She looked between the two witches across the table and felt a quiet sense of awe. These weren’t just powerful women. They were hers. Her people now. Her strange, terrifying, brilliant family.

Chapter 20: Twenty

Agatha walked between Rio and Alice as they made their way up the small stairs of the sagging porch of the cottage, the old wood creaking under their weight. The moon was high, casting everything in a pale glow that softened edges and made the world feel suspended in something dreamlike. Rio’s hand brushed against hers now and then, a gentle touch that grounded her, made her remember that not everything had to feel like a warning.

Alice let out a stretch and a yawn so exaggerated it had to be performative. “As much as I’d love to continue our magical group therapy, I’ve got a thing tonight.”

Agatha arched a brow. “A thing?”

“A date,” Alice said with a grin. “Well. Potential date.”

Rio turned to her, skeptical. “With who? The only people under fifty and older than 25 in this town are us and that goth barista who clearly hates everyone.”

Alice laughed and fished her phone out of her jacket. “Matched with her when I got to town. She just texted to meet up at the Silver Mare.”

She turned the phone toward them, and Agatha squinted at the screen. A striking Black woman with a shaved head smiled out at them, all confidence and charm. She wore a sleek leather jacket, tattoos inked delicately along her collarbone, and held a glass of whiskey with an effortless kind of cool. Underneath her picture: Dr. Jennifer Kale.

Rio’s jaw dropped. “No way. That’s Salem’s vet!”

Agatha couldn’t help the smirk that curled her lips. “Jennifer Kale. She’s brilliant. And intense.”

Alice pocketed her phone with a shrug. “She’s hot, smart, has opinions, and she asked me out. I’d be stupid not to go.”

Agatha chuckled. “Well, if you disappear into the woods never to be heard from again, we’ll know who to question.”

“I’ll send my location,” Alice said, already halfway down the walk. “Don’t wait up!”

They watched her go, the air falling into a soft hush around them. Agatha could still feel Rio’s hand in hers, warm and steady.

By the time they reached the cottage, the moon was high and the sky scattered with stars, the air smelling like pine and woodsmoke. Agatha unlocked the door and pushed it open, the familiar creak of old hinges welcoming them home.

Rio slipped past her with slow, dragging steps, shoulders a little hunched, eyes rimmed with exhaustion. Salem darted in behind them, letting out a chirp of greeting before disappearing into the living room.

Agatha turned to speak, but Rio beat her to it with a sleepy murmur.

“Babe… I know we talked about tea and cozying up, but I think I’m gonna have to take a raincheck. I’m so wiped, I don’t even know what dimension I’m in anymore.”

Agatha’s expression softened. “Of course, darling. Go to bed. I’ll be right behind you.”

Rio offered a grateful little smile and kissed Agatha’s cheek, already shrugging out of her hoodie as she made her way toward the stairs.

Agatha watched her go—her usually vibrant energy dulled to embers—and felt a tug in her chest. She was proud of how far Rio had come, how fiercely she threw herself into her training, but she couldn’t help the faint undercurrent of worry that pulsed beneath it.

She moved through the motions of locking up the house, feeding Salem, extinguishing the candles with a flick of her fingers. Then she followed Rio upstairs.

By the time she reached the bedroom, Rio was already under the covers, curled up on her side. One arm flung across the pillow, hair a dark tumble around her face. She was already half-asleep, blinking slowly as Agatha slid into bed behind her.

Agatha pressed a kiss to the back of her shoulder, then draped an arm over her waist.

“Goodnight, my darling,” she whispered, even though she wasn’t sure Rio could hear it.

The only response was a sleepy little sigh and the relaxing of muscle against her body.

Agatha closed her eyes and let herself fall into the quiet.

~*~

Sunlight filtered through the gauzy curtains, painting soft gold across the white sheets. Agatha stirred slowly, blinking herself awake to the sound of birdsong and the gentle shifting of the woman beside her.

Rio had turned onto her back in her sleep, the duvet pulled down around her waist, her tank top slightly askew.

It was then that Agatha saw it—faint shadows of bruises blooming along Rio’s ribs and the edge of her shoulder, half-hidden by the cotton fabric.

Her heart caught.

Carefully, so as not to wake her, she sat up and gently brushed the strap of Rio’s tank top aside. The marks were clearly from the night before—likely when Wanda had pushed her to her limits, and Agatha had been too caught up in the moment to notice how much Rio had taken on.

She reached out and traced the edge of a bruise with trembling fingers, the glow of healing magic already flickering to life in her palm. Rio stirred under the touch.

“Hmm?”

“You’re hurt,” Agatha said softly, brows drawn.

Rio blinked at her, eyes still bleary. “What?”

Agatha shifted so she was leaning over her properly now, letting her hand hover over one bruise. “You didn’t feel this last night?”

Rio looked down and winced, reaching to touch her own side. “Oh. Damn . I didn’t even realize. I was running on so much adrenaline, I guess I didn’t notice.”

Agatha sighed, pressing her palm gently to Rio’s skin. “You don’t always have to be the strongest one in the room, you know.”

Rio gave a sheepish smile, leaning into the warmth. “I kinda do when I’m being double teamed by two witches who’ve been practicing magic since they were in diapers.”

That made Agatha chuckle in spite of herself. 

“I don’t regret it,” Rio said softly. “I need to be ready. Whatever this Nezzera thing is—we can’t afford to be sloppy.”

Agatha sobered again, the healing magic flowing quietly beneath her skin. “No. We can’t.”

She bent down and kissed the center of a fading bruise.

“But I still need you in one piece, love.”

Rio closed her eyes. “I’m not going anywhere.”

Agatha’s magic flowed steady and golden through her fingertips, gentle as it sunk into Rio’s bruises. She watched them fade, the dark patches softening into nothingness, skin healing beneath her touch. But even after the last one disappeared, she didn’t pull her hand away. Her fingers lingered, warm and light along Rio’s ribs.

“You didn’t even say anything,” Agatha murmured. “You let me walk around all night like I hadn’t noticed you were hurting.”

Rio let out a low breath, eyes still half-lidded against the morning light. “Didn’t feel it at the time. Adrenaline, maybe. Power. I don’t know. I just wanted to be good enough.”

Agatha’s throat tightened. “You are.”

Rio looked at her then, really looked, and something in her expression softened. Agatha felt it like a wave, the tenderness, the unspoken things hanging in the space between them. It made her want to kiss her and hold her and never let her go.

So she did. She leaned in and kissed Rio—slow and full of meaning, the kind of kiss that spoke all the things they hadn’t said aloud. Rio responded with a sigh against her mouth, fingers slipping up into Agatha’s hair.

The kiss deepened with quiet urgency, their bodies moving closer like they couldn’t help it. Clothes were pushed away in lazy motions, not rushed but inevitable, and soon they were skin to skin beneath the covers, all warm lines and breathless touches.

Agatha moved over her with reverence, like Rio was something rare and holy. Every kiss, every slow roll of her hips, was a vow she couldn’t quite name yet.

Rio gasped, pulling her closer. “Don’t stop,” she whispered, and Agatha never would—not for her.

They moved together with an aching sweetness, like it wasn’t just want anymore, but something deeper, fuller. Something they hadn’t dared name but could feel in every brush of fingers, every shared breath, every trembling moment where the world narrowed to just this.

When they reached that peak together, Agatha cried out into the curve of Rio’s neck, her magic sparking out in light. She felt Rio do the same, a bright, blinding moment of connection. A crack of thunder echoed distantly overhead—just one. As if the world itself had acknowledged what had happened between them.

Not just sex. Not even just magic.

Something more.

Afterward, Agatha lay tangled against her, heart still racing, fingers tracing idle patterns across Rio’s stomach. Rio’s hand was in her hair again, slow and soothing, and they didn’t speak for a long time.

It was Rio who broke the silence first, her voice low and a little hoarse. “I don’t know what we’re doing,” she said. “But I know I don’t want it to stop.”

Agatha lifted her head just enough to look at her. “Me neither.”

She leaned in, kissed the corner of Rio’s mouth, and let herself linger there.

Neither of them said the words.

But the air was thick with them.

~*~

By the time Agatha emerged from the shower, dressed in one of Rio’s soft vintage tees knotted at the waist and a pair of borrowed jeans that fit almost indecently well, the smell of vanilla and cinnamon had filled the entire cottage.

The scent hit her like a spell the moment she stepped into the kitchen.

Rio was at the stove, flipping golden pancakes like it was second nature, hair still damp and curling around her ears, wearing nothing but boyshorts and a robe that barely stayed closed. She turned and gave Agatha a wicked little grin over her shoulder.

“Hope you’re hungry,” Rio said. “I’ve earned the right to gloat a little.”

Agatha leaned against the doorframe, arms crossed, a fond smile playing on her lips. “Oh, you absolutely have. That was… incredible.”

Rio’s eyes twinkled as she slid a pancake onto the growing stack. “Well. I aim to please.”

Salem wove between Agatha’s ankles with a delicate mewl, tail flicking. She reached down and scratched him behind the ears, earning a pleased purr.

The moment was quiet and full of ease, and Agatha felt it settle into her bones. She hadn’t known how badly she’d needed this—domesticity, intimacy, warmth. She hadn’t dared imagine it could be this easy with someone.

Then the front door creaked open, and Alice breezed in wearing the same clothes from the night before, hair a bit mussed, and lipstick a little smudged. She looked far too smug for someone who clearly hadn’t slept.

“Good morning, sapphics!” she announced, flopping into a chair like she owned the place.

Rio laughed. “Alice. Subtle.”

Agatha stole a kiss from Rio as she passed her, just a soft press of lips that made Rio’s ears flush red and her knees go a little weak. Then she sat down beside Alice, snatching a piece of sliced banana from the counter.

Alice waggled her brows at her. “You look suspiciously glowy, Agatha.”

Agatha raised a brow, but her smirk betrayed her. “So do you.”

Alice gave an exaggerated shrug. “Listen, I don’t want to brag but Salem’s local vet? Knows her way around more than just animals.”

Rio choked on a laugh, tossing a dishtowel in her best friend’s direction. “Gross.”

Agatha just grinned into her coffee mug. “I like her.”

Alice beamed. “She likes you too. Though I warned her about the two of you being absolutely insufferable when you’re in the same room.”

Rio finally brought over a plate stacked with pancakes, set it in front of Agatha with a dramatic flourish, and gave her a look that was somewhere between adoring and exasperated. “You’re lucky you’re hot.”

Agatha leaned in and murmured, “You keep making me pancakes, I’ll let you call me lucky forever.”

Rio blushed again, and Alice made a gagging noise. Salem, unfazed, hopped up onto the windowsill to bathe in the morning sun.

It was cozy and ridiculous and so stupidly perfect that for a moment, Agatha forgot the looming shadow of that dream, forgot the word Nezzera, forgot the weight that came with being a Thread.

Right now, there were pancakes, coffee, and the woman that made her world spin completely out of control with how much she loved her.

She’d take the peace where she could.

~*~

Agatha lingered longer than she should at the breakfast table, caught between the warmth of the food, the laughter, and the way Rio’s eyes crinkled when she smiled. But the clock ticked ever onward, and the apothecary wasn’t going to open itself.

“I really do have to go,” she murmured, even as her body made no move to leave. Salem pawed lazily at the hem of her shirt like even he disapproved.

Rio walked her to the door, her hand brushing lightly against the small of her back, and Agatha leaned into the touch instinctively. They paused on the threshold—just a few steps from the front porch, with sunlight cutting soft golden lines between the trees.

Agatha turned to face her, already tilting in for a kiss, and when Rio met her lips it was slow and aching and far too short. She felt it all the way down to her toes, like the warmth of a spell casting itself inside her ribcage.

When they pulled apart, Rio looked dazed in the prettiest way, her lips parted like she still had something left to say.

And then, she said it.

“I love you.”

It was so soft, Agatha almost missed it. But it landed like thunder.
