Rio blinked, visibly startled that the words had actually left her mouth, like some part of her brain hadn’t caught up with her heart. She opened her mouth again, as if to take it back or soften it, but Agatha didn’t let her.

Instead, she kissed her.

Really kissed her—deep and searching, her hands in Rio’s curls, her whole body pressing close like maybe if they stayed like this, time would stop spinning so damn fast.

When they finally broke apart, Agatha stayed close, forehead pressed to Rio’s.

“I love you too,” she breathed, barely above a whisper. “So much I don’t even know what to do with myself anymore.”

They stood there like that, wrapped in silence and each other, until the air shimmered.

It wasn’t just the air, though.

They didn’t notice it at first—not until Rio gasped and pulled back slightly, eyes wide as she glanced over Agatha’s shoulder.

Agatha turned.

The porch—Rio’s poor, sagging, weather-beaten porch—was no longer sagging. No longer cracked and leaning. The wood looked freshly sanded and stained, the railings smooth and polished, each slat perfectly placed.

And then the flowers.

Azaleas. Clematis. Wisteria. Blooms of every shade curled over the posts and beams like they had grown there for decades, full and vibrant, humming with unseen magic.

“Oh my god,” Rio whispered, her fingers curled lightly around Agatha’s wrist.

Agatha didn’t say anything at first. Her throat felt thick. Her heart thundered.

The magic wasn’t just responding to Rio’s power—it was responding to them. To their love. Their truth.

“Well,” Agatha finally said, her voice quiet and thick with emotion, “that’s new.”

Rio let out a breathless laugh, both of them still in awe.

Agatha reached down and linked their fingers, grounding herself in the touch. She didn’t care that she was late anymore. She’d never felt more present than she did in this moment.

Magic was real. Love was real. And she wasn’t afraid anymore.

They lingered on the porch, reluctant to pull away. The winter morning was crisp, breath visible in soft clouds between kisses. The air held that clean, cold scent that always followed an overnight frost, and yet everything around them—especially the porch now blooming with enchanted life—felt impossibly warm.

“I really have to go,” Agatha said, voice low, her gloved hand still wrapped in Rio’s.

“You do,” Rio whispered, though neither of them moved.

Agatha gave her one last, lingering kiss, slow and warm against the chill, then finally forced herself to step back. As she walked down the steps, she felt the faint crunch of frost-softened boards beneath her boots—new wood, still faintly warm from magic. A ribbon of white ivy curled around the railing as if it had always been there.

She looked back one last time—Rio standing there in a hoodie and flannel pants, hair messy, eyes soft—and then she got in her car and headed into town.

The drive was slow. A light dusting of snow still clung to the edges of the road, and the trees were bare and skeletal, reaching long fingers across the sky. The holiday lights strung up along Main Street flickered to life even though it was barely mid-morning—silver stars and warm golden orbs wrapped around lamp posts like a greeting.

Agatha parked just outside the flower shop—she had promised Lilia she’d pick up some dried winter roses—and pulled her coat tighter around herself as she stepped out. The cold bit at her cheeks, but she barely noticed. She still felt warm, her chest full of something heavy and bright and terrifyingly lovely.

She was halfway across the sidewalk when—

“Well, well,” came the unmistakable voice of Sharon Davis, her breath fogging slightly as she approached in a long charcoal coat and red scarf. “If it isn’t Agatha Harkness, glowing like she’s walked straight out of a Christmas card.”

Agatha blinked, momentarily caught off-guard. “Mayor Davis. Morning.”

“Mmhmm,” Sharon said, hands tucked neatly in her coat pockets as she took in Agatha’s flushed cheeks and almost dreamy expression. “You’ve got that look. You know the one. Like someone just gave you exactly what you didn’t know you needed.”

Agatha tried to school her face into something neutral, but it was impossible. Her lips curled in that stupid, genuine smile that kept happening lately. “It’s been… a good morning.”

“I’ll bet it has,” Sharon said knowingly. “Didn’t think I’d see the day, but… I’ve got to say, it suits you. Happy looks good on you.”

Agatha looked down briefly, adjusting her scarf like it might hide the feeling brimming in her chest.

“Thank you,” she said, quieter than she meant to.

“Don’t thank me,” Sharon replied, already moving toward the town hall. “Just hold onto it.”

Agatha stood for a moment as the cold nipped at her cheeks, her breath curling in the air. Snow started to fall again—light flurries that dusted the street like powdered sugar.

She reached into her coat pocket, pulled out her phone, and texted Rio:

Agatha

you’re trouble. magical, wonderful trouble.

also, i miss you already.

Then she shoved her hands back into her pockets and walked toward her shop, heart beating so loud it drowned out the bells jingling overhead.

~*~

Agatha had barely turned the sign to OPEN and started sorting out the stock behind the counter when the bell above the door rang.

She didn’t glance up at first—customer traffic this time of year usually meant holiday colds and last-minute herbal remedies—but something about the silence that followed made her pause.

No idle chatter. No curious footsteps. Just stillness.

And then a voice: calm, crisp, familiar.

“Hello again, Ms. Harkness.”

Her breath caught.

She looked up slowly—and there she was. Mara Greaves. Standing just inside the doorway like she belonged there, dressed in that sleek black coat and burgundy gloves, speckled with melted snow. Her silver-blonde braid was tucked neatly over one shoulder, and her expression held the same too-knowing calm it had during their last encounter.

Here. In her shop. Again.

Agatha offered a practiced, polite smile. “Dr. Greaves. Back so soon?”

Mara tilted her head slightly. “I never did finish browsing. And this time of year? Well… there’s always something to find in an old place like this.”

Agatha didn’t move from behind the counter, though she felt every hair on the back of her neck prickle. “Looking for anything in particular? Oils? Tinctures?”

“Insight,” Mara said simply, stepping farther into the shop and brushing her fingertips across a hanging bundle of dried thyme. “This town is layered, you know. History isn’t just in books—it’s in walls. In blood.”

Agatha’s smile didn’t waver. “Sounds like something a folklorist would say.”

Mara’s eyes glittered with amusement. “That’s what I am.”

“Right,” Agatha murmured. “A folklorist.”

There was a beat of silence. Then:

“She’s learning quickly,” Mara said, voice softer now. “The girl. Rio.”

Agatha didn’t blink. “She’s none of your business.”

“I’m simply observing,” Mara replied, her gaze drifting to the dusty shelf of protective stones. “But you’re guiding her. Preparing her. That’s always been your role, hasn’t it?”

Agatha’s smile thinned. “You must have me confused with someone else.”

“No,” Mara said, voice almost gentle. “I don’t.”

That did it. Agatha stepped out from behind the counter, her posture casual, but her energy humming just beneath the surface.

“You said you were here to research stories,” she said. “Buy some herbs. Drink some tea. I suggest you stick to that.”

Mara gave a faint, almost approving smile. “You’re good at this. The pretending.”

Agatha’s jaw clenched. “This conversation is over.”

“I’m sure you believe that,” Mara said, turning slowly toward the door. “But you know what’s coming. You felt it the moment the name was spoken.”

Agatha didn’t answer.

Mara glanced back once, her eyes sharp. “Not everything buried stays asleep.”

Then she walked out, the bell over the door jingling like nothing had happened.

Agatha stood there for a moment, the silence stretching long and heavy around her.

And then she reached for her phone and texted Wanda first.

Agatha

she was here again. she brought up rio. she knows something. maybe more than she’s letting on.

Then another message to Rio, right after:

Agatha

hey, love. everything okay? let me know when you’re free.

Because whatever this was? It wasn’t over.

Not even close.
